Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
10 min
When Is Compensation Due in Conditional Divorce?
Series of rulings on khula' with specified monetary compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between phrasings that make compensation obligatory in khul' and those that do not, and apply the Hanafi rule on option conditions.

Core Idea
In Hanafi khul', payment is due only when the compensation is made a condition of the divorce, not when it is a separate statement.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents several scenarios of conditional divorce with monetary compensation. Understanding the precise wording is critical: whether the husband says 'for a thousand' (making it a condition) or 'and upon you a thousand' (separate debt) determines if she must pay. Moreover, the validity of an option condition depends on who holds it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is khul' – a divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation. The ruling is that the divorce is valid (sahih) if accepted; the payment may or may not be due.
Khul' in Hanafi fiqh is a ba'in (irrevocable) divorce.
2
Distinguish the two key phrasings
Pay attention to the Arabic prepositions: 'على' (for/upon) indicates the compensation is a condition of the divorce; 'و' (and) separates the compensation from the divorce. 'You are divorced for a thousand' makes the payment a condition; 'You are divorced and upon you a thousand' makes it a separate debt.
The Hanafi school treats these as legally distinct.
3
Apply the rule to partial fulfillment
If the wife demands three divorces for a thousand and the husband gives one, she owes one-third of the thousand – the compensation is proportional to the divorce granted.
Each divorce is valued equally.
4
Analyze the option condition
If the husband adds an option for himself (e.g., 'I have an option of three days'), the condition is invalid – the divorce is final. If the option is for the wife, it is valid; she may reject within the period.
The husband cannot reserve a right to cancel a divorce he has pronounced.
5
Note the ikhtilaf with Shafi'i
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that even with 'and upon you', the payment is due because the condition is part of the contract. The Hanafi response is that the wording shows a separate debt, not a condition for divorce.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf (mukhtalaf fih).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سپر د کرنا لازم ہے اور بحر متحقق ہونے کی صورت میں قیمت لازم ہے عورت نے کہا طلقنی ثلاثہ بالف شوہر نے ایک طلاق دیدی عورت پر ثلث الف لازم ہے عورت نے کہا طلقنی علی الف شوہر نے ایک طلاق دیدی عورت پر کچھ لازم ہوگا یا نہیں اور شوہر کو رجوع کا حق ہوگا یا نہیں ، اقوال فقہاء شوہر نے کہا طلقی نفسک ثلاثا بالف یا علی الف عورت نے اپنے آپ کو ایک طلاق دی کوئی بھی طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی شوہر نے کہا انت طالق علی الف عورت نے قبول کر لیا عورت مطلقہ ہو جائے گی اور عورت پر ہزار لازم ہوں گے شوہر نے اپنی بیوی کو کہا انت طالق و علیک الف عورت نے قبول کر لیا یا آقا نے غلام کو کہا انت حر و علیک الف غلام نے قبول کر لیا غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا اور عورت مطلقہ ہوگی اور دونوں پر کچھ لازم نہیں ہوگا، اقوال فقہاء شوہر نے کہا انت طالق علی الف اس شرط پر کہ مجھے خیار ہے یا مجھے تین دن کا خیار ہوگا عورت نے قبول کر لیا اگر خیار شوہر کیلئے ہے تو باطل ہے اور اگر عورت کیلئے ہے تو جائز ہے اور اگر عورت نے تین دن میں رد کر دیا تو خیار باطل ہے
It is necessary to deliver, and in the case of the sea being verified, the price is necessary. A woman said: 'Divorce me three times for a thousand.' The husband gave one divorce. One-third of a thousand is necessary upon the woman. A woman said: 'Divorce me for a thousand.' The husband gave one divorce. Will anything be necessary upon the woman or not, and will the husband have the right of return or not? Statements of the jurists. The husband said: 'Divorce yourself three times for a thousand or for a thousand.' The woman gave herself one divorce. No divorce occurs at all. The husband said: 'You are divorced for a thousand.' The woman accepted. The woman becomes divorced, and a thousand is necessary upon the woman. The husband said to his wife: 'You are divorced and upon you is a thousand.' She accepted. Or the master said to the slave: 'You are free and upon you is a thousand.' The slave accepted. The slave becomes free, and the woman becomes divorced, and nothing is necessary upon either. Statements of the jurists. The husband said: 'You are divorced for a thousand on the condition that I have the option, or I will have an option of three days.' The woman accepted. If the option is for the husband, it is invalid. If it is for the woman, it is valid. If the woman rejected within three days, the option is invalid.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage presents a series of rulings on conditional divorce with monetary compensation (khula' with a specified amount). It opens with the ruling that if a woman demands a threefold divorce for a sum (e.g., one thousand) and the husband issues only one divorce, she owes one-third of the sum (since each divorce is valued separately). The second scenario considers a demand for a single divorce for a thousand, raising the question of whether she owes anything and whether the husband can take her back (رجوع). The answer is implied in later rulings: if the husband says 'You are divorced for a thousand' and she accepts, she is divorced and owes a thousand; but if the wording is 'You are divorced and upon you is a thousand,' she is divorced but owes nothing because the obligation is not part of the divorce contract—it is a gift or debt. Similarly, with a slave, 'You are free and upon you is a thousand' results in freedom without payment. The passage then addresses a conditional option: if the husband says 'You are divorced for a thousand on condition that I have the option,' the condition is invalid because the divorce is final; if the option is for the wife, it is valid, and if she rejects within three days, the option lapses.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation.
ثلث الف (thulth al-alf): One-third of one thousand (dirhams).
علی الف (ala al-alf): For a thousand – making the compensation a condition of the divorce.
و علیک الف (wa alayka alf): And upon you is a thousand – separates the compensation as a debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a woman says 'Divorce me three times for a thousand' and the husband gives only one divorce, how much does she owe in Hanafi fiqh?
A) One thousand dirhams.
B) Nothing, because the condition was not fulfilled.
C) One-third of a thousand dirhams.
D) The matter is left to the husband's discretion.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi khul', the obligation to pay compensation depends entirely on the wording: 'for a thousand' makes it a condition, whereas 'and upon you a thousand' makes it a separate debt with no payment required.

Khula' with a Minor Wife and Father as Guarantor
Rulings on khula' of a minor wife with father's guarantee.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which a khula' with a minor wife is valid in Hanafi fiqh and identify who bears the financial obligation.

Core Idea
A minor's khula' is valid if she accepts or if her father guarantees the payment.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya deals with a particular case of khula' (divorce by redemption) involving a minor wife. The key issue is whether such a divorce can be effective given the minor's lack of legal capacity. The text outlines three scenarios, showing how the father's guarantee or the minor's acceptance can make the khula' valid. Understanding these rulings is essential for correctly applying the law of khula' to cases involving minors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
Read the passage and list the three distinct cases of khula' with a minor wife presented.
The scenarios vary based on who guarantees the payment and whether the minor accepts.
2
Determine validity for each scenario
For each scenario, decide whether the khula' is valid immediately or contingent on a condition.
Contingent means the khula' is suspended until the condition is fulfilled.
3
Identify the condition that makes it effective
In each case, pinpoint the exact condition that renders the khula' valid (father's guarantee or minor's acceptance).
The condition varies: in one scenario it's the father's guarantee; in another it's the minor's acceptance.
4
Determine financial liability
Identify who is obligated to pay the consideration (khula' money) in each valid scenario.
The minor is never liable; the father is liable when he guarantees, otherwise no payment is due.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شوہر نے ہزار پر خلع کیا اس شرط پر کہ لڑکی کا باپ ضامن ہو گا ضلع ہو جائے گا اور ہزار باپ پر لازم ہوگا شوہر نے ایک ہزار کو صغیرہ پر شرط کیا تو ضلع عورت کے قبول کرنے پر موقوف ہوگا اگر عورت اہل قبول میں سے ہے عورت نے قبول کر لیا طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی شرط کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے اور مال واجب نہیں ہوگا شوہر نے صغیرہ سے اس کے مہر پر ضلع کیا اور باپ مہر کا ضامن نہیں تو صغیرہ کے قبول کرنے پر موقوف ہوگا اگر باپ مہر کا ضامن ہو گیا عورت مطلقہ ہو جائے گی
The husband made khula' for a thousand on the condition that the girl's father be the guarantor. The khula' is valid, and the thousand is obligatory upon the father. The husband stipulated one thousand upon the minor, so the khula' is contingent upon the woman's acceptance. If the woman is capable of acceptance and she accepts, the divorce occurs due to the condition being fulfilled, but the wealth is not obligatory. The husband made khula' with the minor for her mahr, and the father is not the guarantor of the mahr, so it is contingent upon the minor's acceptance. If the father becomes the guarantor of the mahr, the woman becomes divorced.
Source pages p. 7

Commentary
This passage deals with khula' (divorce by redemption) involving a minor wife (صغیرہ). The first scenario: the husband makes khula' for one thousand on condition that the minor's father is the guarantor. The khula' is valid, and the father must pay the thousand, not the minor. Second scenario: the husband stipulates the payment on the minor herself; then the khula' is contingent upon her acceptance. If she is capable of acceptance (i.e., she is discerning, usually above the age of discretion), and she accepts, the divorce takes effect, but she does not owe the money because a minor cannot be obligated in such contracts. Third scenario: the husband makes khula' in exchange for her mahr, and the father does not guarantee the mahr; the khula' is contingent on her acceptance. If the father guarantees the mahr, the minor becomes divorced (since the guarantee transfers the obligation to the father). The key principle is that a minor's khula' is not valid unless she accepts if she is capable, and the guarantee of a guardian can transfer the monetary obligation.

Key Terms
ضلع (khul'): Another term for khula' (divorce by redemption).
صغیرہ (saghirah): A minor female who has not reached puberty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, if a husband makes khula' with his minor wife for one thousand and the father guarantees the payment, who owes the thousand?
A) The minor wife.
B) The father.
C) The husband.
D) No one; the khula' is invalid.

Key Takeaway
A minor's khula' is valid if she accepts (if capable) or if her father guarantees the payment, and she is never financially liable.

Rulings on Impotent Husband and Majbub
Ruling procedure for male impotence and mutilation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi procedure for an impotent husband and apply the distinction between 'unnin and majbub.

Core Idea
Impotent husband gets one year; majbub is separated immediately.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on marital separation due to male impotence or mutilation. The passage distinguishes between the impotent man ('unnin) and the man whose penis is cut off (majbub), and outlines the procedure for the judge, including inspection and oaths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the types of male defects discussed
Note that the passage covers two distinct cases: 'unnin (impotent) and majbub (penis cut). Understand that these are treated differently.
'Unnin requires a one-year respite; majbub leads to immediate separation.
2
Understand the procedure for impotence
The judge gives one year; if the husband becomes capable, no separation; otherwise separation as talaq bain. The wife must demand it.
The separation is irrevocable divorce (talaq bain).
3
Handle disputes about intercourse
If the husband claims intercourse but the wife denies, and she is thayyib (non-virgin), the husband's word with oath is accepted. If the wife is still a virgin, inspection is done.
If inspection shows virgin, wife gets option; if non-virgin, husband's oath stands.
4
Apply the rule for majbub
For a majbub husband, there is no respite. The judge separates immediately upon the wife's demand.
Immediate separation because there is no hope of cure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب العنين وغيره
جب زوج عنین ہو حاکم اسے ایک سال مہلت دے اگر قادر علی الجماع ہو گیا فیھا ورنہ دونوں میں تفریق کر دے
یہی حکم عورت کے مطالبہ کا ہے
یہ فرقت طلاق بائنہ ہے
میاں بیوی کا جماع ہونے نہ ہونے میں اختلاف ہو گیا اگر عورت ثیبہ ہے تو مرد کا قول قسم کے ساتھ معتبر ہے اگر شوہر مجبوب الذکر ہے تو قاضی فورا تفریق کر دے اگر عورت مطالبہ کرے
جب عنین کو ایک سال کی مہلت دی اور اس نے کہا میں نے جماع کیا عورت انکار کرتی ہے قاضی عورتوں سے معائنہ کروائے اگر وہ باکرہ کہ دیں تو اسے اختیار دے دیا جائے اگر وہ شیبہ کہہ دیں زوج مقسم اٹھائے
اگر عورت پہلے سے شیبہ ہے مرد کا قول قسم کے ساتھ معتبر ہوگا
اگر زوجہ میں کوئی عیب ہو عورت کیلئے خیار نہیں ہے، امام شافعی کا نقطہ نظر
شوہر مجنون یا برص یا جذام کا مرض ہو عورت کیلئے خیر نہیں ، امام محمد کا مذہب
Chapter on the Impotent and Others. When the husband is impotent, the judge gives him a one-year respite; if he becomes capable of intercourse within it, [fine]; otherwise, the judge separates them. This ruling applies upon the wife's demand. This separation is an irrevocable divorce (talaq bain). If a dispute arises between husband and wife whether intercourse occurred, and the wife is a non-virgin (thayyib), the husband's word with oath is accepted. If the husband is one whose penis is cut off (majbub al-dhakar), the judge immediately separates them if the wife demands. When the impotent man is given a one-year respite and he says 'I had intercourse,' but the wife denies, the judge has women inspect [her]. If they say she is a virgin, she is given the option; if they say she is a non-virgin, the husband takes an oath. If the wife was previously a non-virgin, the husband's word with oath is accepted. If the wife has a defect, she has no option (khiyar) – according to Imam Shafi'i's view. If the husband has insanity, vitiligo, or leprosy, the wife has no option – according to Imam Muhammad's school.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on impotence and defects presents the Hanafi rulings on marital separation due to inability to consummate. The opening rule: an impotent husband is given one year to prove his ability; if he fails, the judge annuls the marriage as a talaq bain. This is upon the wife's demand. The passage then addresses disputes: if the husband claims intercourse but the wife denies, and she is thayyib (not a virgin), the husband's oath is accepted. If the husband is majbub (his penis cut), separation is immediate. For the impotent man, if he claims intercourse after the year, the court inspects the wife; if she is still virgin, she has the option; otherwise, the husband's oath stands. A key Hanafi position: defects in the wife do not give her a right to annul the marriage – this is contrasted with Imam Shafi'i who allows such option. Similarly, for defects in the husband like insanity or leprosy, Imam Muhammad says no option for the wife, implying the school's position (though Abu Hanifa's view may differ). The passage includes intra-Hanafi (Imam Muhammad) and inter-madhhab (Shafi'i) disputes.

Key Terms
عنین ('unnin): An impotent man unable to achieve erection.
مجبوب الذکر (majbub al-dhakar): A man whose penis has been cut off.
ثیبہ (thayyib): A non-virgin woman (previously married or widowed).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if the husband is majbub al-dhakar?
A) He is given a one-year respite.
B) The judge immediately separates them if the wife demands.
C) The marriage becomes fasid.
D) The wife must wait five years.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between impotence (one-year respite) and complete incapacity (immediate separation), with evidentiary rules for disputes.

The Wife's Right to Annul Marriage Due to Defects (Khiyar al-Ayb)
Madhhab dispute on khiyar al-ayb in marriage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that a wife has no khiyar (option) to annul the marriage due to defects in herself or her husband, and contrast it with the Shafi'i and Imam Muhammad views.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, a wife cannot annul a marriage based on defects in either spouse.

This lesson focuses on the critical ikhtilaf (dispute) regarding khiyar al-ayb in marriage. The Hanafi school holds that neither spouse has the right to annul due to defects, unlike the Shafi'i school which grants the wife an option. The passage also mentions an intra-Hanafi difference attributed to Imam Muhammad concerning defects in the husband.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position on khiyar al-ayb
The text states that if the wife has a defect, she has no option. Similarly, if the husband has defects like insanity or leprosy, she has no option. This is the mufta bihi position.
This is contrary to the Shafi'i school.
2
Note the opposing view of Imam Shafi'i
Imam Shafi'i allows the wife to annul the marriage if the husband has a defect, analogizing to the option of defects in sales.
The passage mentions this as 'Imam Shafi'i's view'.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi opinion of Imam Muhammad
Imam Muhammad explicitly states that the wife has no option even if the husband has insanity, vitiligo, or leprosy. This reinforces the Hanafi stance but may differ from other Hanafi opinions.
Imam Muhammad's view is presented as authoritative in this passage.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In Hanafi, the wife remains bound to the marriage unless she can seek khula' or divorce by other means. In Shafi'i, she can obtain an annulment immediately.
This difference affects the wife's ability to exit the marriage without the husband's consent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب العنين وغيره
جب زوج عنین ہو حاکم اسے ایک سال مہلت دے اگر قادر علی الجماع ہو گیا فیھا ورنہ دونوں میں تفریق کر دے

جب عنین کو ایک سال کی مہلت دی اور اس نے کہا میں نے جماع کیا عورت انکار کرتی ہے قاضی عورتوں سے معائنہ کروائے اگر وہ باکرہ کہ دیں تو اسے اختیار دے دیا جائے اگر وہ شیبہ کہہ دیں زوج مقسم اٹھائے

Chapter on the Impotent and Others. When the husband is impotent, the judge gives him a one-year respite; if he becomes capable of intercourse within it, [fine]; otherwise, the judge separates them. This ruling applies upon the wife's demand. This separation is an irrevocable divorce (talaq bain). If a dispute arises between husband and wife whether intercourse occurred, and the wife is a non-virgin (thayyib), the husband's word with oath is accepted. If the husband is one whose penis is cut off (majbub al-dhakar), the judge immediately separates them if the wife demands. When the impotent man is given a one-year respite and he says 'I had intercourse,' but the wife denies, the judge has women inspect [her]. If they say she is a virgin, she is given the option; if they say she is a non-virgin, the husband takes an oath. If the wife was previously a non-virgin, the husband's word with oath is accepted. If the wife has a defect, she has no option (khiyar) – according to Imam Shafi'i's view. If the husband has insanity, vitiligo, or leprosy, the wife has no option – according to Imam Muhammad's school.

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on impotence and defects presents the Hanafi rulings on marital separation due to inability to consummate. The opening rule: an impotent husband is given one year to prove his ability; if he fails, the judge annuls the marriage as a talaq bain. This is upon the wife's demand. The passage then addresses disputes: if the husband claims intercourse but the wife denies, and she is thayyib (not a virgin), the husband's oath is accepted. If the husband is majbub (his penis cut), separation is immediate. For the impotent man, if he claims intercourse after the year, the court inspects the wife; if she is still virgin, she has the option; otherwise, the husband's oath stands. A key Hanafi position: defects in the wife do not give her a right to annul the marriage – this is contrasted with Imam Shafi'i who allows such option. Similarly, for defects in the husband like insanity or leprosy, Imam Muhammad says no option for the wife, implying the school's position (though Abu Hanifa's view may differ). The passage includes intra-Hanafi (Imam Muhammad) and inter-madhhab (Shafi'i) disputes.

Key Terms
خیار (khiyar): The right to annul a marriage due to a defect.
برص (baras): Vitiligo, a skin condition causing white patches.
جذام (jutham): Leprosy, a chronic infectious disease.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which position does Imam Muhammad hold regarding the wife's option when the husband has leprosy?
A) The wife has the option to annul.
B) The wife has no option.
C) The marriage is automatically annulled.
D) The wife must wait one year.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, marital defects do not grant the wife a right to annul the marriage, contrary to the Shafi'i school.

Establishing Paternity Through Conditional Divorce Declaration
Ruling on paternity when a man says 'if I marry X, she is divorced'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on paternity when a conditional divorce is pronounced before marriage and identify the condition of the six-month minimum pregnancy period.

Core Idea
A child born within six months of marriage is attributed to the father even if a conditional divorce was uttered.

This lesson examines a specific scenario from the chapter on establishing lineage (nasab). A man makes a conditional divorce statement before marriage, then marries the woman. She gives birth within six months. The Hanafi school provides a clear ruling that the child is his and full mahr is due. Understanding this ruling requires grasping the significance of the six-month period, which is the minimum duration of pregnancy in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional statement
Recognize that the man says 'If I marry X, she is divorced.' This is a conditional talaq (talq mu'allaq). Under Hanafi law, if the condition occurs (marriage), the divorce takes effect.
The divorce does not invalidate the marriage retroactively.
2
Determine the timeframe of birth
The text states the child is born within six months from the day of marriage. Six months is the minimum pregnancy period in Hanafi jurisprudence.
If the child is born after six months, paternity is not automatically established.
3
State the ruling on paternity
The child is legally attributed to the man as his son. The conditional divorce does not prevent this attribution.
The ruling assumes consummation of marriage or valid seclusion that allows conception.
4
State the ruling on mahr
The full dower (mahr) is obligatory upon the man. This is because the marriage was consummated (implied by the birth).
Even if divorce took effect, the husband must pay full mahr if consummation occurred.
5
Understand the underlying legal principle
The Hanafi school considers the six-month minimum as a qat'i condition for attributing paternity to the husband. This protects lineage and prevents attribution of children conceived before marriage.
This principle is based on hadith and qiyas on the minimum duration of pregnancy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب ثبوت النسب
مرد نے کہا ان تزوجت فلان بھی طالق پھراس کے ساتھ نکاح کیا پھر اس نے نکاح کے دن سے لے کر چھ ماہ میں بچہ جنابیہ اس کا بیٹا ہے اور مرد پر مہر لازم ہے
Chapter on Establishing Lineage. A man said: 'If I marry so-and-so, she is divorced.' Then he married her, then she gave birth to a child within six months from the day of marriage. That child is his son, and the full dower is obligatory upon the man.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This brief passage from the chapter on establishing paternity (nasab) presents a specific scenario. A man makes a conditional pronouncement: 'If I marry X, she is divorced.' He then goes ahead and marries her, and she gives birth within six months of the marriage date. The ruling states that the child is legally his, and he must pay the full dower (mahr). The six-month period is significant because it is the minimum period of pregnancy according to Hanafi fiqh. Since the child is born within this time from the marriage, it establishes paternity. The conditional divorce does not prevent the child from being attributed to him. The ruling also implies that the condition triggered, so the wife is divorced, but the pregnancy and paternity are established. This is a straightforward ruling without ikhtilaf in the given text.

Key Terms
نسب (nasab): Lineage or paternity, the legal attribution of a child to a father.
مہر (mahr): The dower or bridal gift obligatory upon the husband in marriage.

B) Six months
C) One year
D) Immediately

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a child born within six months of marriage is attributed to the husband even if a conditional divorce was pronounced before marriage, and full mahr is due.

Definition and Conditions of Raj'ah (رجعت)
Defines raj'ah and lists its conditions and proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Shar'i definition of raj'ah, list its five conditions, and identify the proofs from Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma'.

Core Idea
Raj'ah is the husband's right to resume the marriage during 'iddah without a new contract, subject to five conditions.

This passage opens the chapter on raj'ah. Since raj'ah naturally follows divorce, it is placed after the divorce chapter. We will first understand the linguistic and technical meaning of raj'ah, then examine the five conditions that must be met, and finally see the three sources that establish its legitimacy in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
Understand the placement and linguistic meaning
Note why this chapter comes after divorce: raj'ah is temporally and naturally subsequent. The author traces the root r-j-', meaning 'to return', and gives Quranic examples of both intransitive and transitive uses. This linguistic foundation helps grasp the Shar'i concept.
The phrase 'بَابُ الرَّجُعَةِ' means 'Chapter of Raj'ah'.
2
Grasp the Shar'i definition
In Shari'ah, raj'ah is defined as 'maintaining the ownership of marriage as it was' (مِلْك النِّكَاح بِدَسْتُور). That is, the husband retains his marital rights over his wife during her 'iddah after a revocable divorce, without needing a new contract.
This distinguishes raj'ah from a new marriage (nikah).
3
Memorize the five conditions
The passage lists five conditions: (1) the divorce was given with explicit words or certain kinayah words (i.e., it was a revocable talaq), (2) no wealth was exchanged (not khul'), (3) not three divorces, (4) the wife was consummated (madkhul biha), (5) the 'iddah is still ongoing. All five must be present for valid raj'ah.
If any condition is missing (e.g., three talaqs or 'iddah expired), raj'ah is invalid.
4
Recognize the three sources of proof
The legitimacy of raj'ah is proven by: (a) Quran: 'And their husbands have more right to take them back' (2:228), (b) Sunnah: the Prophet told Ibn 'Umar to take back his wife, and the Prophet himself took back Sawdah, (c) Ijma': consensus of the scholars. These make raj'ah an established ruling with no disagreement.
The phrase 'وَأُحُقُ بِرَدِّهِنَّ' is the core textual proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ترجمہ (یہ) باب رجعت کے (حکم کے بیان ) میں ہے
باب طلاق المريض
تشریح چونکہ رجعت طلاق سے طبعا موخر ہے اسلئے وضعا اور ذکر ابھی مؤخر کر دیا گیا تا کہ وضع طبع کے موافق ہو جائے۔ رجعت ، راء کے فتحہ اور کسرہ کے ساتھ ہے۔ مگر فتح کے ساتھ پڑھنا انصح ہے۔ رَجَعَ يَرجِعُ ضرب سے ہے۔ معنی ہیں واپس آنا ، لوٹنا، کہا جاتا ہے الی الله مرجک ۔ رجع لازم اور متعدی دونوں طرح مستعمل ہے۔ پس رجوع مصدر لازم ہے۔ جیسے قعود اور جلوس ۔ لازم کی نظیر باری تعالى كا قول لئن رجعنا الى المدينة (اگر لوٹے ہم شہر کی طرف) فلما رجعوا الى ابيهم (پس جب وہ اپنے باپ کی طرف لوٹے ) و انا الیه راجعون (اور ہم اسی کی طرف لوٹیں گئے ) اور متعدی میں استعمال کی مثال باری تعالیٰ کا قول فان رجعك الله الى طائفة منهم (اگر لوٹا دے تجھ کو اللہ ان میں سے ایک جماعت کی طرف) ثم ارجع البصر (پھر لوٹا تو اپنی نگاہ)۔

(۴) عورت مدخول بہا ہو۔
(۵) عدت موجود ہو۔
رجعت کا ثبوت کتاب اللہ، حدیث اور اجماع نینوں سے ہے۔ اسلئے اسکی مشروعیت میں کسی کا اختلاف نہیں ہے۔ کتاب سے ثبوت کی مثال و بُعولتهنَّ أَحَقُّ بِرَدَهنَ اى برجُعَتهنَّ اور حدیث سے ثبوت کی مثال حضرت عمر سے آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول مر ابنک فليراجعها اور آپ صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حضرت سودہ سے مراجعت فرمائی اور رجعت کی صحت پر اجماع بھی منعقد ہوا ہے۔ (مینی شرح کنز )
Chapter of Raj'ah. Translation: This chapter is about the ruling of raj'ah. Chapter of the Divorce of the Sick Person. Explanation: Since raj'ah is naturally later than divorce, therefore in structure and mention it has been delayed so that the structure matches the nature. Raj'ah, with fatha and kasra on the ra'. However, reading with fatha is more correct. Raj'a yarji'u is from the pattern of dharaba. Meaning: to return. It is said: 'To Allah is your return.' Raj'a is used both as intransitive and transitive. Therefore ruju' is an intransitive infinitive, like qu'ud and julūs. Examples of intransitive: Allah's saying 'If we return to the city', 'When they returned to their father', 'And to Him we return.' Example of transitive: Allah's saying 'If Allah returns you to a group of them', 'Then return your sight.' In Shari'ah terminology, raj'ah means to maintain the ownership of marriage as it was. And for raj'ah there are several conditions, consider them below: 1) Giving divorce with explicit words or some kinayah words mentioned previously, i.e., i'taddi, istaqbali, rahmik, anti wahidah. 2) There is no wealth in exchange for the divorce. 3) He does not effect three divorces. 4) The woman is consummated. 5) The 'iddah is present. The proof of raj'ah is from the Book of Allah, Sunnah, and consensus. Therefore there is no disagreement regarding its legitimacy. From the Book: the example 'And their husbands have more right to take them back.' From the Sunnah: the Prophet's saying to 'Umar: 'Tell your son to take her back.' And the Prophet himself took back Sawdah. Consensus has also been established on the validity of raj'ah. (Mini Sharh Kanz)
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is a definition_ruling that introduces the chapter on raj'ah (returning to the wife after a revocable divorce). The author begins by explaining why this chapter is placed after the chapter on divorce: because raj'ah is temporally and naturally subsequent to divorce. He then gives the linguistic definition of raj'ah from the root r-j-', meaning to return, and provides Quranic examples. In Shari'ah terminology, raj'ah is defined as maintaining the ownership of marriage (milk al-nikah) as it was, i.e., the husband retains his marital rights without a new contract. Five conditions are listed for raj'ah: 1) the divorce must be revocable, given with explicit words or certain kinayah words; 2) no wealth is exchanged for the divorce (i.e., it is not a khul'); 3) the number of divorces does not complete three; 4) the wife must have been consummated (madkhul biha); 5) the 'iddah is still ongoing. The legitimacy of raj'ah is established by three sources: Quran (2:228: 'their husbands have more right to take them back'), Sunnah (the Prophet told Ibn 'Umar to take back his wife, and the Prophet himself took back Sawdah), and ijma' (consensus). The passage emphasizes that there is no disagreement among scholars on the basic permissibility of raj'ah.

Key Terms
رجعت (raj'ah): In Shari'ah terminology, maintaining the ownership of marriage as it was during the 'iddah after a revocable divorce, without a new contract.
مدخول بہا (madkhul biha): A woman with whom the husband has consummated the marriage (i.e., actual intercourse has occurred).
عدت (iddah): The waiting period a woman must observe after divorce or death, during which she cannot remarry.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The divorce must be revocable (not three divorces).
B) The wife must consent to the raj'ah.
C) The wife must be consummated (madkhul biha).
D) The 'iddah must still be ongoing.

Key Takeaway
Raj'ah is the husband's right to resume the marriage during 'iddah after a revocable divorce, subject to five clear conditions, and is proven by Quran, Sunnah, and Ijma'.

Husband's Right to Raj'ah During Iddah
States the ruling that a husband may take back his wife during iddah regardless of her consent

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raj'ah during 'iddah, identify the Quranic proof, and explain why the wife's consent is not required.

Core Idea
The husband can take back his wife during 'iddah without her consent—the Quranic command is absolute.

Raj'ah, or taking back one's wife during the waiting period after a revocable divorce, is a unique right given to the husband. This passage from Al-Hidayah establishes that the husband may exercise this right unilaterally, regardless of the wife's wishes. The key proof is the unqualified Quranic command, and the legal reasoning centers on the nature of raj'ah as a continuation of marriage ownership.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its scope
Identify the act being ruled upon (raj'ah after one or two revocable divorces) and the hukm (permissible/mubah). Note that the wife must have been consummated and the 'iddah must be current.
The ruling applies only to revocable divorces (talaq raj'i), not to irrevocable or triple divorces.
2
Identify the primary proof (dalil)
Locate the Quranic verse cited (Surah At-Talaq 65:2) and note that it is quoted without qualification. The imperative 'amsikuhunna' is a command to hold back, interpreted as permission for raj'ah.
The verse does not condition raj'ah on the wife's consent.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah (legal implication)
Explain how the absolute wording of the verse proves the ruling. The absence of any condition regarding the wife's satisfaction indicates that the husband's right is unilateral.
Hanafi usul: al-amr al-mutlaq yufid al-wujub or al-ibahah; here it indicates permission.
4
Note the condition of 'iddah
The author explains that raj'ah is only possible during the 'iddah because it is a continuation of ownership (istidamah al-milk). After the 'iddah expires, the marriage is dissolved.
The 'iddah is a necessary condition (shart) for the validity of raj'ah.
5
Consider cross-madhhab differences
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees regarding the method: he requires a verbal statement if the husband can speak, whereas the Hanafi school allows action alone. Both agree that consent is not required.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is minimal in most cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا طلق الرجل امرأته تطليقة رجعية او تطليقتين فله ان يراجعها في عدتها رضيت بذلک اولم ترض لقوله تعالى فامسكوهن بمعروف من غير فصل ولابد من قيام العدة لان الرجعة استدامة الملك الاترى انه سمی امساكا و هو الابقاء وانما يتحقق الاستدامة في العدة لانه لا ملک بعد انقضائها

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جب مرد نے اپنی مدخول بہا بیوی کو ایک طلاق رجعی یا دو طلاقیں دے دیں تو مرد کو اختیار ہے کہ وہ اس سے اسکی عدت میں مراجعت کر لے۔ عورت اس پر راضی ہو یا نہ ہو ۔ دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فَإِذَا بَلَغْنَ أَجَلُهُنَّ فَأَمْسِكُوهُنَّ بِمَعْرُوفٍ أَوْ فَارِقُوهُنَّ بِمَعْرُوف یعنی جب عورتوں کی عدت قریب اتم ہو جائے تو تم کو اختیار ہے۔ اگر رجعت کو اختیار کرنا چاہوتو بغیر ضرر پہنچائے ان کو روک لو اور اگر جدا کرنے کا ارادہ ہو تو بغیر ضرر پہنچائے ان کو جدا کر دو ۔ اس آیت میں مطلقا مراجعت کا ذکر ہے۔ عورت کی رضاء یا عدم رضاء کی تفصیل نہیں ہے۔ اس وجہ سے رجعت کا حکم مطلق رکھا گیا۔
دوسری دلیل ابوداؤد کی روایت ہے: عن عمر رضی الله تعالى عنه ان النبى طلق حفصة رضى الله تعالى عنها ثم راجعها اور حدیث ابن عمر میں ہے انه علیه السلام قال له مر ابنك فليراجعها الحديث (متفق عليه ) اور رجعت کیلئے عدت کا موجود ہونا ضروری ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ رجعت نام ہے ملک نکاح کو برقرار رکھنا۔ چنانچہ آپ دیکھئے کہ قرآن پاک میں رجعت کا نام امساک ہے اور امساک کے معنی ہیں باقی رکھنا اور ملک نکاح کو برابر باقی رکھنا عدت میں ہوسکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ عدت گذر جانے کے بعد ملک نکاح ہی نہیں رہتی تو باقی رکھنا کہاں سے ہو گا۔ پس جب عدت پوری ہو گئی تو محل امساک نہیں رہے گا۔
And when a man divorces his wife one revocable divorce or two divorces, he has the right to take her back during her 'iddah, whether she is pleased with that or not, due to the saying of Allah Almighty: 'So hold them back with honor' without any qualification. And the existence of the 'iddah is necessary, because raj'ah is the continuation of ownership. Do you not see that it is called 'imsaak' (holding) and it is preservation. The preservation is only realized in the 'iddah, because there is no ownership after its expiry. Translation: And when a man gives his wife one revocable divorce or two divorces, the man has the option to take her back during the 'iddah, whether the woman is pleased with it or not, due to the saying of Allah 'hold them back with honor' without any detail. And the presence of the 'iddah is necessary because raj'ah means to maintain ownership. Do you not see that it is named 'imsaak' and 'imsaak' is preservation. And the preservation can only be in the 'iddah because after the 'iddah passes, there is no marriage ownership. Explanation: The scenario is that when a man gives his consummated wife one revocable divorce or two divorces, the man has the option to take her back during her 'iddah, whether the woman is pleased with it or not. The proof is the saying of Allah 'When they reach their term, then hold them back with honor or separate from them with honor.' This verse mentions raj'ah in an absolute sense; there is no detail about the woman's consent or lack thereof. Therefore the ruling of raj'ah is made absolute. The second proof is the hadith of Abu Dawud: 'The Prophet divorced Hafsah and then took her back.' And in the hadith of Ibn 'Umar: 'He (peace be upon him) said to him: Tell your son to take her back.' (Agreed upon). And for raj'ah, the existence of the 'iddah is necessary. The proof is that raj'ah means to maintain the ownership of marriage. For you see, the Qur'an calls raj'ah 'imsaak', and 'imsaak' means to preserve. And to preserve the ownership of marriage can only happen in the 'iddah, because after the 'iddah expires, there is no marriage ownership, so where would preservation come from? So when the 'iddah is complete, there is no place for 'imsaak'.
Source pages p. 34

Commentary
This passage is a ruling_with_proof that establishes the husband's unilateral right to raj'ah during the 'iddah. The author begins by stating the ruling: if a man gives one or two revocable divorces, he may take back his wife during her 'iddah, regardless of whether the wife agrees. The proof is the Quranic verse 'hold them back with honor' (65:2), which gives the husband the choice without mentioning the wife's consent. The author then explains that the existence of the 'iddah is essential because raj'ah is the continuation of marital ownership. Since ownership ends when the 'iddah expires, raj'ah is only possible during the 'iddah. The commentary further clarifies the scenario: the wife must be consummated (madkhul biha). Additional proof is provided from the Sunnah: the Prophet took back Hafsah after divorcing her, and he instructed Ibn 'Umar to take back his wife. The passage emphasizes that the absolute wording of the Quran and the actions of the Prophet show that the wife's consent is not required. The legal reasoning (ta'lil) is that raj'ah is called 'imsaak' (holding) in the Quran, and 'imsaak' means preservation; preservation of the marital bond can only occur if the 'iddah is still ongoing.

Key Terms
رجعت (raj'ah): The husband's act of taking back his wife during the 'iddah after a revocable divorce, continuing the marriage without a new contract.
عدت (iddah): The waiting period (three menstrual cycles or three months) that a woman observes after a revocable divorce, during which the husband may take her back.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The hadith of the Prophet taking back Sawdah.
B) The Quranic verse 'hold them back with honor' which is unqualified.
C) The consensus of the companions.
D) The analogy with the initial marriage contract.

Key Takeaway
The husband's right to raj'ah during 'iddah is unilateral; it does not require the wife's consent based on the absolute Quranic command.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Tahlil: Marriage with Condition
Intra-Hanafi dispute on marriage with condition of tahlil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on marriage with the condition of tahlil and explain the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) of each.

Core Idea
A marriage with condition of tahlil is valid but makruh; tahlil is achieved only according to Abu Hanifa, not his two disciples.

This lesson examines the intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether a marriage contracted with an explicit condition of tahlil makes the woman lawful for her first husband after consummation and divorce. The source passage from Hidayah presents three distinct views, each with its own proof and underlying principle. Understanding this dispute clarifies how differing usul principles can lead to different rulings within the same madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What specific legal question is being disputed? The question is: Does a marriage with the condition of tahlil make the woman lawful for the first husband after consummation and divorce?
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his proof
Abu Hanifa says the marriage is valid and tahlil is achieved. His proof: The hadith curses the act but does not invalidate the marriage; a condition does not affect the validity of the contract. Consummation in a valid marriage is sufficient.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
State Abu Yusuf's position and his proof
Abu Yusuf says the marriage is fasid (invalid) because it resembles a temporary marriage (mut'ah), and thus tahlil is not achieved.
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: he differs from Abu Hanifa.
4
State Muhammad's position and his proof
Muhammad says the marriage is valid but tahlil is not achieved. The man hastened what the Law delayed (tahlil should be without pre-condition), so he is punished by preventing the goal—analogous to a murderer being denied inheritance.
Also differs from Abu Hanifa.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and the practical consequence
The relied-upon view is Abu Hanifa's. Practical consequence: the woman becomes lawful for the first husband. According to the other two, she does not, so the first husband cannot remarry her until she marries another man (without condition) and is divorced again.
The marriage itself is makruh in all views.

جیسا کہ اگر کسی شخص نے اپنے مورث کو قتل کر دیا تو وہ شخص میراث سے محروم کیا جائے گا۔ کیونکہ شریعت نے جس چیز کو موخر کیا تھا اس نے اس چیز کو جلد حاصل کرنے کا ارادہ کیا ہے۔ امام ابو حنیفہ سے روضتہ الزند طلاق دی یا قاضی اور حاکم کے حکم سے تو یہ عورت زوج اول کے لئے حلال ہو جائے گی۔ امام ظہیر الدین نے کہا کہ یہ بیان اس کے علاوہ کسی دوسری کتاب میں موجود نہیں۔ لہذا یہ بیان قابل اعتماد نہیں ہے اور نہ اس کے Chapter of the sick man's divorce. The master's intercourse with his slave-girl does not make her lawful, because the goal is the husband's marriage. And if he marries her with the condition of tahlil, the marriage is makruh by his saying, peace be upon him, 'Allah curses the muhallil and the one for whom tahlil is done.' This is its application. If he divorces her after intercourse, she becomes lawful for the first husband due to the occurrence of intercourse in a valid marriage, for a marriage is not invalidated by a condition. From Abu Yusuf: the marriage is invalid because it is in the meaning of a temporary marriage, and it does not make her lawful for the first due to its invalidity. From Muhammad: the marriage is valid as we have explained, but it does not make her lawful for the first because he hastened what the Law delayed, so he is punished by preventing his objective, as in the case of killing the testator. Translation: Qaduri said: The master's intercourse with his slave-girl does not make her lawful, because the goal is the husband's marriage...
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage from Hidayah, commented by Ashraf al-Hidayah, addresses the ruling on tahlil (making a woman lawful for her first husband after a triple divorce). The original Arabic matn states that a master's intercourse with his own slave-girl does not make her lawful for her first husband because the Qur'anic condition is marriage (nikah) to another husband, and a master is not a husband. The commentary explains the scenario: if a man divorces his wife (who is a slave) twice, and after iddah her master has intercourse with her, she does not become lawful for the first husband. A tradition from Uthman, Ali, and Zayd illustrates the disagreement: Uthman and Zayd considered the master as a husband, while Ali rejected this. The main discussion then turns to marriage with an explicit condition of tahlil. The matn rules such a marriage makruh (disliked) based on the hadith cursing the muhallil and muhallal lahu. However, if the second husband consummates and then divorces, she becomes lawful for the first. This is because the marriage is valid despite the condition; a fasid condition does not invalidate a marriage (according to the Hanafi position). All three imams agree that the marriage with condition is valid (though Abu Yusuf rules it fasid in one narration). The disagreement is on whether it makes the woman lawful for the first husband: Abu Hanifa says yes (because valid marriage with consummation), Abu Yusuf says no (because the marriage is fasid), and Muhammad says no (because the man hastened what the Law delayed, so he is punished by preventing the goal, analogous to a murderer being denied inheritance). The commentary also mentions a rare narration from Abu Hanifa in Rawdat al-Zandbisti that the marriage is permissible and the condition is permissible, even that if the second husband does not divorce, the judge can compel him. However, Imam Zahir al-Din says this narration is unreliable and not acted upon.

Key Terms
تحلیل (tahlil): The act of making a woman lawful (halal) for her first husband after a triple divorce, through marriage and consummation with a second husband.
محلل (muhallil): The second husband who marries a woman with the intention of making her lawful for her first husband.
محلل له (muhallal lahu): The first husband for whom the woman is made lawful through tahlil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi) in the passage, what is the ruling on a marriage contracted with the explicit condition of tahlil after consummation and divorce?
A) The marriage is valid and the woman becomes lawful for the first husband.
B) The marriage is invalid (fasid) and she does not become lawful.
C) The marriage is valid but she does not become lawful.
D) The marriage is makruh and invalid.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, a marriage with the condition of tahlil is valid but makruh; the relied-upon position is that it achieves tahlil, though Abu Yusuf and Muhammad disagree.

The Second Husband's Effect on Divorces: Does He Destroy Less Than Three?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on effect of second marriage after less than three divorces

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on whether a second marriage destroys divorces less than three and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between the Shaykhayn and Imam Muhammad.

Core Idea
The second husband destroys all prior divorces, restoring three, according to the Shaykhayn.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a critical point in the law of tahlil: when a woman divorced once or twice remarries, then returns to her first husband, how many divorces does he have left? The answer depends on whether the second husband's marriage 'destroys' the previous count. Within the Hanafi school, there is a well-known disagreement between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on one side and Imam Muhammad on the other. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to reason with proof texts (hadith vs. quranic reference) and to distinguish between legal concepts of prohibition and lawfulness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the legal question
A free woman is divorced once or twice, her iddah expires, she marries another husband, then returns to the first husband. The question: How many divorces does the first husband have left?
The scenario assumes a valid second marriage with consummation.
2
State the position of the Shaykhayn
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the second husband destroys all divorces less than three, so the first husband has three full divorces.
3
State the position of Imam Muhammad
Imam Muhammad holds that the second husband does not destroy less than three; he only destroys the triple divorce. The first husband retains the remaining divorces (e.g., if one was given, he has two left).
4
Analyze the proofs
The Shaykhayn rely on the hadith 'Allah curses the muhallil and the one for whom tahlil is done' – calling the second husband a muhallil (one who establishes lawfulness) implies his marriage wipes out all prior divorce counts. Imam Muhammad relies on the Quranic verse (2:230) which describes the second husband as the 'end of the prohibition' – a termination that only applies after a complete (triple) divorce.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واذا طلق الحرة تطليقة او تطليقتين وانقضت عدتها وتزوجت بزوج أخر ثم عادت الى الزوج الأول عادت بثلث تطليقات ويهدم الزوج الثانى مادون الثلث كما يهدم الثلث وهذا عندابي حنيفة وابي يوسف وقال محمد لا يهدم مادون الثلث لأنه غاية للحرمة بالنص فيكون منهيا ولا انهاء للحرمة قبل الثبوت ولهما قوله عليه السلام لعن الله المحلل والمحلل له سماه محللا وهو المثبت للحل ترجمہ اور جب کسی مرد نے آزاد عورت کو ایک یا دو طلاقیں دیں اور اس کی عدت گزرگئی اور اس عورت نے کسی دوسرے شوہر سے نکاح کر لیا پھر یہ عورت پہلے شوہر کے پاس لوٹ آئی ( تو یہ عورت) تین طلاقوں کے ساتھ لوٹے گی اور زوج ثانی تین سے کم ( طلاقوں کو ) اسی طرح منہدم کر دے گا جس طرح تین کو اور یہ حکم شیخین کے نزدیک ہے اور امام محمد نے فرمایا کہ دوسرا شوہر ) تین سے کم کو منہدم نہیں کرتا ۔ امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ زوج ثانی حرمت کی انتہاء ہے بہ نص قرآنی ۔ پس زوج ثانی حرمت غلیظہ کو ختم کرنے والا ہوا اور حرمت کو ختم کرنا (حرمت غلیظ ) کے ثبوت سے پہلے نہیں ہوسکتا اور شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے زوج ثانی کو حلالہ کرنے والا کہا اور حلالہ کرنے والا وہ ہے جو حلت کو ثابت کر دے۔
And if a free woman is divorced once or twice and her iddah expires, and she marries another husband, then returns to the first husband, she returns with three divorces. The second husband destroys what is less than three just as he destroys three. This is according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: He does not destroy what is less than three, because he is the end of the prohibition by text, so he is a terminator, and the termination of the prohibition cannot occur before its establishment. Their proof is his saying, peace be upon him: 'Allah curses the muhallil and the one for whom tahlil is done.' He called him muhallil, and he is the one who establishes lawfulness. Translation: And when a man divorces a free woman once or twice and her iddah passes, and she marries another husband, then she returns to the first husband, she returns with three divorces. The second husband destroys less than three just as he destroys three. This is the ruling according to the two shaykhs. Muhammad said: The second husband does not destroy less than three. Muhammad's proof: The second husband is the end of the prohibition by the Qur'anic text, so he is the one who terminates the prohibition, and termination cannot occur before the prohibition is established. The proof of the two shaykhs: The Prophet, peace be upon him, called the second husband a muhallil, and the muhallil is the one who establishes lawfulness.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage from Al-Hidayah deals with the effect of a second marriage on the number of divorces a woman has. The scenario: a free woman is divorced once or twice by her first husband. After her iddah, she marries another man (second husband). Then she divorces from the second (or he dies) and returns to the first husband. The question is: how many divorces does the first husband have left? According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Shaykhayn), the second marriage 'destroys' (yahdima) whatever divorces are less than three, meaning that the husband's previous count of one or two is wiped out and he starts with three full divorces. So if she returns, he has the right to three divorces. Imam Muhammad disagrees: the second husband only destroys the triple divorce (i.e., if she was divorced thrice, the second marriage makes her lawful again, but if the first husband divorced her once or twice, the second marriage does not wipe those away; the first husband retains the remaining divorces. His reasoning: the second husband is the 'end of the prohibition' (ghayat li'l-hurma) according to the Qur'anic text 'until she marries another husband' (2:230). That verse applies only when there is a complete prohibition (thubut al-hurma), which only occurs after a triple divorce. Before that (i.e., after one or two divorces), there is no complete prohibition, so the second husband cannot terminate it. The Shaykhayn counter with the hadith cited earlier: the Prophet cursed the muhallil and the one for whom tahlil is done. He called the second husband a muhallil, and the muhallil is the one who establishes lawfulness (yuthbit al-hill). Since the second husband is called muhallil generally, his effect is to make the woman lawful for the first husband, and by entering the marriage, he destroys all previous divorce counts. This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).

Key Terms
يهدم (yahdimu): The second husband's marriage destroys (nullifies) the previous divorce count, so that the first husband regains the right to three divorces.
غاية للحرمة (ghayat li'l-hurma): The second husband is the end (termination) of the prohibition; i.e., his marriage ends the irrevocable prohibition that occurs after three divorces.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if a free woman is divorced twice, then remarries, and returns to her first husband, how many divorces does the first husband have?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) None

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the second husband's marriage destroys all prior divorces, regardless of whether they were one, two, or three, as per the Shaykhayn.

Marriage with Condition of Tahlil: Validity and Effect
Intra-Hanafi dispute on marriage conditioned on tahlil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relied-upon Hanafi position on a marriage conditioned on tahlil and distinguish it from the positions of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.

Core Idea
A marriage conditioned on tahlil is valid, but the condition is void and tahlil is not achieved.

When a marriage is explicitly conditioned on the second husband divorcing the woman so she can return to her first husband, is the marriage valid? Does it achieve tahlil? This lesson explores the intra-Hanafi dispute on this issue, covering the dominant position, the objections of the Sahibayn, and a rare narration from Imam Abu Hanifa. You will learn the reasoning behind each view and the operative ruling for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and the act
Recognize that the condition of tahlil means the second husband agrees to divorce the woman so she becomes halal for her first husband. The act is a marriage contract with this explicit condition.
This is a conditional marriage, not a temporary marriage.
2
State the dominant Hanafi position
The majority of the Hanafi school (the relied-upon view) holds that the marriage is valid (sahih), the condition is void, and the woman is not halal for the first husband.
Marriage is not invalidated by void conditions.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's objection
Imam Abu Yusuf (in one narration) considers the marriage fasid because it resembles a temporary marriage (nikah muwaqqat), which is invalid. The condition makes the marriage time-limited.
This is based on qiyas with mut'ah.
4
Examine Muhammad's nuance
Imam Muhammad holds the marriage valid but the woman not halal. He uses a qiyas: just as a killer is deprived of inheritance for hastening the delay, the condition nullifies the tahlil as a penalty.
The analogy is with inheritance deprivation (Quranic principle).
5
Consider the rare narration and its rejection
A rare narration from Imam Abu Hanifa states both marriage and condition are valid, and the woman becomes halal after divorce. However, Imam Zahir al-Din rejects it as unreliable because it appears in no other book.
Thus, the mufta bihi is the first view.

Chapter of Divorce of the Sick. Ashraf al-Hidayah commentary on Hidayah volume 5: it is found that the condition of tahlil is required. As for whether marriage with a condition of tahlil is valid or not, we say that the marriage is valid because invalid conditions do not make marriage invalid. And from Abu Yusuf there is a narration that marriage with a condition of tahlil is invalid because it is like a temporary marriage. He said, 'I married you until such time,' so it is a temporary marriage, which is invalid. So this marriage is invalid, and such a person is not a muhallil for the first husband because for tahlil a valid marriage is necessary. And from Muhammad there is a narration that marriage with a condition of tahlil is valid because invalid conditions do not nullify marriage, but the woman is not halal for the first husband. The evidence is that the person hastened what the Shari'ah delayed. So his objective was prevented and a penalty was imposed, just as if a person kills his predecessor, he is deprived of inheritance. From Abu Hanifa it is narrated in Rawdat al-Zandabasti that marriage with a condition of tahlil is permissible and the condition is also permissible such that if the second husband does not divorce after consummation, the ruler will force him to divorce. If he divorces of his own accord or by order of the judge, then the woman becomes halal for the first husband. Imam Zahir al-Din said that this statement is not found in any other book, so it is not reliable and a ruling will not be given according to it.
Source pages p. 62

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the validity of a marriage contracted with the condition of tahlil (making a woman halal for her first husband after three divorces). The author first states the relied-upon position: the marriage is valid because a marriage is not invalidated by void conditions. He then narrates from Imam Abu Yusuf that such a marriage is invalid because it resembles a temporary marriage (nikah mut'ah), which is prohibited. This is based on a narration from Abu Yusuf. Next, he mentions a narration from Imam Muhammad that the marriage is valid but the woman does not become halal for the first husband. The reasoning is that the condition explicitly aims to hasten what the Shari'ah has delayed (tahlil only after the second marriage ends naturally), so as a penalty the woman remains prohibited. A qiyas (analogy) is made to a person who kills his predecessor: he is deprived of inheritance because he hastened the delay. Finally, a rare narration attributed to Abu Hanifa is cited stating both marriage and condition are valid, but Imam Zahir al-Din declares it unreliable as it appears in no other book. The operative ruling (mufta bihi) is the first view: the marriage is valid but the condition is void and the woman is not halal.

Key Terms
تحلیل (tahlil): The act of making a woman halal (permissible) for her first husband after three irrevocable divorces, typically through a second marriage.
محلل (muhallil): The second husband who, by marrying and consummating with a thrice-divorced woman, makes her permissible for remarriage to her first husband.
نکاح موقت (nikah muwaqqat): A temporary marriage fixed for a period, which is invalid (fasid) in Hanafi law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi Hanafi position, what is the ruling on a marriage contracted with an explicit condition of tahlil?
A) The marriage is invalid (fasid) because the condition is void.
B) The marriage is valid but the woman does not become halal for her first husband.
C) The marriage is valid and the woman becomes halal after divorce by the second husband.
D) The marriage is valid only if the second husband intends to divorce.

Key Takeaway
Marriage with a condition of tahlil is valid under Hanafi law, but the condition is void and the woman is not made halal for her first husband.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
10 min
Perpetual Ila' and Its Cycles through Remarriage
Rulings on perpetual Ila' cycles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the ruling of perpetual Ila' after four months, state why no further divorce occurs before remarriage, and apply the rule of recurring Ila' upon remarriage up to three divorces.

Core Idea
Perpetual Ila' triggers one ba'in divorce every four months without intercourse, but only after each remarriage.

This lesson explores the scenario of perpetual Ila' (yamīn muṭlaqa). The key principle is that the oath persists indefinitely, but divorce does not recur automatically because after ba'in separation, the wife loses her right to intercourse — hence no oppression. When the husband remarries her, the Ila' resumes, and a new four-month period begins. This cycle can repeat up to three divorces. After three divorces and an intervening marriage (tahlil), the original Ila' no longer applies. Understanding these cycles is essential for correct application of Ila' rulings.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish temporary vs perpetual Ila'
Identify whether the oath is for a fixed four-month period (mu'akkata) or perpetual (mu'abbada). In temporary, the oath lapses after four months. In perpetual, it remains.
The condition for Ila' is an oath of at least four months.
2
Apply the initial four-month rule
After four months without intercourse, one ba'in divorce occurs. The oath remains because no violation (hanth) occurred to remove it.
3
No further divorce before remarriage
After ba'in separation, the wife has no right to intercourse, so the condition of oppression (zulm) is absent. Therefore, no second divorce occurs even if additional four-month periods pass before remarriage.
Some scholars (Faqih Abu Sahl) hold that if four months pass within the 'iddah, a second divorce does occur, but the relied-upon view is no divorce until remarriage.
4
Ila' returns upon remarriage
When the husband remarries his ex-wife after ba'in, the Ila' returns. A new four-month period begins from the date of remarriage. If he does not have intercourse within that period, a second divorce occurs.
If remarriage occurs before 'iddah expires, the new period starts from the divorce, not the remarriage (according to al-'Inayah).
5
Limit to three divorces and effect of tahlil
The cycle can repeat up to three divorces. After three divorces, the wife becomes haram (requires tahlil). After she marries another man and is divorced, if the first husband remarries her, the original perpetual Ila' does not apply — no divorce occurs because the Ila' is restricted to the first marriage.
The oath itself remains; if he has intercourse, he must expiate the oath.

واقع نہ ہوگی۔ کیونکہ یا ایلا صرف پہلی ملک کے ساتھ مقید تھا۔ اسلئے کہ ایلا تعلیق طلاق کے مرتبہ میں ہے اور یہ مسئلہ فرع ہے مختلف فیہ تیجیزی مسئلہ کی جو باب الایمان فی الطلاق میں گزر چکا کہ امام زفر کے نزدیک تعلیق باطل نہیں ہوتی اور ہمارے نزدیک باطل ہو جاتی ہے۔ مبسوط میں بیان کیا ہے کہ جس نے اپنی بیوی سے ایلاء کیا کہ خدا کی قسم تجھ سے دلی نہیں کروں گا پھر اس کو تین طلاقیں منجز دید میں تو ہمارے نزدیک ایلاء باطل ہو گیا اور امام زفر کے نزدیک باطل نہیں ہوا ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ایلا ، طلاق موجل ہے مملو کہ تین طلاقوں پر منعقد ہوگا اور اس عورت پر تین واقع ہو جانے کے بعد کوئی طلاق باقی نہیں رہی لہذا ایلاء بھی باقی نہ رہا۔ اور اسی طرح اگر وہ اس ایلاء سے تین بار بائنہ ہوگئی پھر دوسرے شوہر کے بعد اس سے نکاح کیا تو بھی ہمارے نزدیک ایلاء باطل ہو گیا اور امام زفر کے نزدیک باطل نہیں ہوا البتہ یمین باقی رہے گی۔ کیونکہ یمین مطلق عن الوقت ہے اور ولی یہ کرنے کی وجہ سے حانث ہونا بھی نہیں پایا گیا پھر اگر اس عورت سے اس نے ولی کر لی تو اپنی قسم کا کفارہ ادا کرے کیونکہ اب قسم توڑ نا پایا گیا۔ واللہ اعلم چار مہینے سے کم میں قسم کھانے والا مولی نہیں ہے
It remains because it is absolute and no violation occurred to remove it, but divorce does not recur before remarriage because prevention of right is not found after ba'in separation. If he returns and marries her, the Ila' returns. If he has intercourse, then after four months another divorce occurs because the oath remains due to its absoluteness, and by marriage her right is established so oppression occurs, and the beginning of this Ila' is from the time of marriage. If he marries her a third time, Ila' returns and another divorce occurs after four months if he does not approach her, as we explained. If he marries her after another husband, no divorce occurs by that Ila' because it is restricted to the divorce of this ownership, and it is a branch of the disputed issue of ta'liq, which has passed before. The oath remains due to its absoluteness and absence of violation. If he has intercourse with her, he expiates his oath due to occurrence of violation. Translation: If he had sworn for four months, the oath terminates. Because the oath was temporary for that period, and if he swore perpetually, the oath remains. Because the oath is absolute and violation did not occur so that it would be removed, but before marriage divorce does not occur. Because after ba'in separation, prevention of the right is not found. So if he marries her again after ba'in, Ila' returns. If he performs intercourse in the first instance, then it's fine; otherwise, after four months a second divorce occurs. Because the oath is absolute and remains, and by marriage her right is established, so oppression occurs, and the beginning of this Ila' is considered from the time of remarriage. Then if he marries her a third time, Ila' returns and a third divorce occurs after four months, provided he did not have intercourse within four months, for the reason we stated. Then if he marries her after another husband, no divorce occurs by this Ila' because the Ila' is restricted to the first marriage's divorce, and this is a branch of the disputed issue of ta'liq which passed earlier. The oath still remains due to its absoluteness and absence of violation. Then if he has intercourse with her, he expiates his oath because violation is found. Explanation: When four months pass and the husband does not have intercourse, there are two scenarios. First: he swore not to approach her for four months. Second: he swore never to approach her, e.g., saying 'By Allah I will not approach you ever' or without mentioning 'ever'. In the first scenario, after four months without intercourse, the oath lapses because it was temporary. In the second scenario, after four months without intercourse, one ba'in divorce occurs and the oath remains, because the oath is not restricted to a time, so it is perpetual, and due to absence of intercourse the husband is not violative so the oath is not removed. However, before marriage if another four months pass, according to 'Ammat al-Masha'ikh a second divorce does not occur because after ba'in separation there is no right to intercourse, so the husband is not oppressive and no compensation is required. Faqih Abu Sahl and Sahib al-Muhit hold that if four months pass before expiry of 'iddah, a second divorce occurs, and similarly a third, because Ila' is like a repeated condition for divorce, as if he said 'Whenever four months pass and I do not approach you, you are ba'in talaq.' If he explicitly stated that condition, the ruling would be as we said, so here too. And if after ba'in and expiry of 'iddah the husband remarries her, Ila' returns. If he has intercourse during the Ila' period, the oath is broken and expiation is due; if not, after four months a second divorce occurs. Because the oath, being absolute, remains, and by marriage her right is established, so oppression occurs, so ba'in divorce removes it. The beginning of the second Ila' is from the time of remarriage, but if remarriage occurs before 'iddah expires, the beginning is from the time of divorce, not remarriage (al-'Inayah). Then if he marries her a third time, Ila' returns and a third divorce occurs after four months, provided no intercourse in that period. The proof passed earlier that the oath, being absolute, remains and by marriage her right is established, so oppression occurs. (al-'Inayah) The author says: When three divorces have made her severely prohibited, she marries another husband and had intercourse, then the second husband divorces her and her 'iddah expires, then if the first husband (the one who made Ila') marries her, no divorce occurs by that Ila' because it was restricted to the first marriage. Because Ila' is in the category of ta'liq of divorce, and this is a branch of the disputed issue of ta'liq which passed in Bab al-Iman fi al-Talaq that Imam Zufar holds ta'liq is not invalidated, while we hold it is invalidated. In al-Mabsut it is stated: If a man makes Ila' with his wife saying 'By Allah I will not have intercourse with you', then gives her three divorces immediately, according to us the Ila' becomes invalid, while Imam Zufar holds it does not. Our proof is that Ila' is a deferred divorce which cannot be contracted upon three divorces, and after three have occurred no divorce remains, so Ila' does not remain. Similarly, if she becomes ba'in three times by this Ila', then after another husband he marries her, according to us the Ila' becomes invalid, while Imam Zufar holds it does not. However, the oath remains because it is absolute and no violation is found. Then if he has intercourse with her, he expiates his oath because violation is found. And Allah knows best. A person who swears for less than four months is not a muli.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on perpetual Ila'. The author distinguishes between a temporary oath (mu'akkata) for four months and a perpetual oath (mu'abbada). In the temporary case, the oath expires after four months without intercourse. In the perpetual case, after four months without intercourse one ba'in divorce occurs, and the oath remains. The oath does not cause further divorces before remarriage because after ba'in separation the wife has no right to intercourse, so no oppression. Upon remarriage, the Ila' returns and a second divorce occurs after another four months without intercourse. This can continue up to three divorces. After three divorces and an intervening marriage (tahlil), if the first husband remarries her, the Ila' does not apply because it is restricted to the first marriage. The passage also records an intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam Zufar regarding ta'liq: if the husband gives three divorces explicitly, Imam Zufar holds the Ila' remains, while the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold it becomes invalid because no divorce is left to be deferred. The oath itself remains, but the Ila' ruling is lifted; thus if he has intercourse, he must expiate the oath. The passage concludes by stating that an oath for less than four months does not constitute Ila' at all.

Key Terms
إيلاء (īlā'): A vow by a husband to abstain from sexual intercourse with his wife for four months or more, which can lead to divorce.
يمين مطلقة (yamīn muṭlaqa): An absolute or perpetual oath not restricted to a specific period.
حنث (ḥinth): Violation of the oath (by having intercourse), which triggers expiation.
بينونة (baynūna): Complete separation (ba'in divorce) after which the wife is not permissible without a new marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In perpetual Ila', after four months without intercourse, what happens if the husband does not approach his wife and has already given one ba'in divorce before remarriage?
A) A second divorce occurs immediately.
B) No divorce occurs because there is no right to intercourse after ba'in.
C) The oath expires and no divorce occurs.
D) The husband must expiate the oath.

Key Takeaway
Perpetual Ila' remains effective and causes one ba'in divorce every four months without intercourse, but only after each remarriage; no further divorce occurs before remarriage due to the absence of oppression.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute: Effect of Three Explicit Divorces on Ila'
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ta'liq and Ila'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the majority and Imam Zufar's positions on whether Ila' is invalidated by three explicit divorces, identify the proof for each, and apply the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
Three explicit divorces invalidate Ila' because no divorce remains to be deferred; Imam Zufar holds the Ila' persists.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the effect of ta'liq (suspensive condition) on Ila'. The source passage discusses whether a perpetual Ila' remains valid if the husband, after making Ila', subsequently gives his wife three explicit divorces (talaq munajjaz). The majority of Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold that the Ila' becomes invalid because it is a deferred divorce, and after three divorces no additional divorce can occur. Imam Zufar, however, maintains that the ta'liq (the Ila') is not invalidated; the oath remains as a condition for future divorces upon remarriage. Understanding this dispute clarifies the distinction between the oath itself (yamīn) and the legal mechanism of Ila' as a deferred divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The husband has made perpetual Ila' (e.g., 'By Allah, I will not have intercourse with you'). Then, before the four months expire or after, he explicitly divorces his wife three times (e.g., 'You are divorced, divorced, divorced'). The question: Is the Ila' still valid?
Ila' is a deferred divorce suspended on the expiration of four months without intercourse.
2
State the majority position
Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad hold that the Ila' becomes invalid. Reason: Ila' is a deferred divorce (talaq mawjūl). After three divorces have been given explicitly, no divorce remains to be deferred; therefore, the Ila' is null.
This applies even if the wife becomes ba'in three times by the Ila' itself.
3
State Imam Zufar's position
Imam Zufar holds that the Ila' is not invalidated. He views the Ila' as a suspensive condition (ta'liq) that, once made, remains effective. The subsequent explicit divorces do not cancel the condition; the Ila' will apply upon remarriage.
Imam Zufar's view is a minority position within the Hanafi school.
4
Analyze the proof (dalil) for each
Majority: Ila' cannot be contracted upon three divorces because it is a deferred divorce; after three divorces, no further divorce is possible. Imam Zufar: Ta'liq is not invalidated by subsequent divorce; the oath remains as a condition for future divorces upon remarriage.
The source does not give an explicit rebuttal but notes that the majority view is the relied-upon (mufta bihi).
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
Practical consequence: According to the majority, the husband must renew Ila' after remarriage if he wishes; according to Imam Zufar, the original Ila' applies upon remarriage. The tarjih (preference) is the majority view, as recorded in al-Hidayah.
The oath itself remains; if he has intercourse, he must expiate.
