Khul' with Unspecified Dirhams: Liability for Three
Ruling on khul' with ambiguous 'dirhams'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi linguistic principle that the plural indicates at least three to determine the minimum compensation in a khul' contract when the amount is unspecified from a phrase like 'min darahim'.

Core Idea
When a wife says 'min darahim' in khul', she must pay three dirhams because the plural minimum is three and 'min' is explanatory, not partitive.

In this passage, we encounter a specific case of khul' divorce where the wife offers unspecified 'dirhams' as compensation. The husband agrees, but she has nothing in her hand at that moment. What amount must she pay? The Hanafi ruling relies on a precise linguistic analysis of the Arabic phrase, distinguishing between explanatory and partitive uses of the particle 'min'. This lesson unpacks the linguistic reasoning and its application to determine the obligatory payment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is khul' initiated by the wife with the phrase 'khala'ni 'ala ma fi yadi min darahim'. The husband agrees. She has nothing. The ruling is that she must pay three dirhams.
2
Locate the core linguistic issue
The key is the word 'min' and the plural 'darahim'. Is 'min' partitive (meaning 'some of') or explanatory (connecting the phrase)? Also, what does the plural imply about quantity?
3
Understand the Hanafi linguistic principle
Hanafi linguists hold that the minimum of a plural in Arabic is three (jam' al-qillah). Additionally, 'min' here is used as 'li al-sila' (explanatory) because removing it would make the sentence grammatically incomplete. Thus, it does not indicate a portion.
Compare: 'min al-tab'idiyya' (partitive) would mean 'some of'.
4
Apply the principle to derive the ruling
Since 'min' is explanatory, the plural 'darahim' retains its full meaning: at least three. Therefore, the wife owes three dirhams, even though she had nothing at the time.
The obligation is a debt (dayn) arising from the khul' contract.
5
Note the ikhtilaf (disagreement)
If 'min' were interpreted as partitive, the phrase would mean 'some of the dirhams in my hand', and if she had none, she would owe nothing. The Hanafi position is based on the explanatory 'min' and is the mufta bihi (relied-upon opinion).
This ikhtilaf highlights the importance of linguistic precision in fiqh.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و لوقالت خالعنى على مافى يدى من دراهم او من الدراهم ففعل فلم يكن فى يدهاشيء فعليها ثلثة دراهم لانها سمت الجمع واقله ثلتة وكلمة من ههنا للصلة دون التبعيض لأن الكلام يختل بدونه
And if she says: 'Divorce me for khul' on what is in my hand of dirhams or of the dirhams,' and he does so, and there was nothing in her hand, then she owes three dirhams, because she mentioned the plural and its minimum is three, and the word 'min' here is for conjunction (al-sila) not for partitivity (al-tab'id), because the speech would be incomplete without it.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage states a ruling and its proof. The ruling: if a woman initiates khul' by saying 'khala'ni 'ala ma fi yadi min darahim' (or 'min al-darahim'), and the husband agrees, but she actually has nothing in her hand, she must pay three dirhams. The proof is linguistic: she used the plural form 'darahim,' and the minimum of the plural in Arabic is three. The word 'min' here is not partitive (meaning 'some of') but rather explanatory (li al-sila/bayan), because without it the sentence would be defective. The author explains that wherever the sentence is complete without 'min,' it indicates partitivity; if incomplete, it indicates explanation. Here, deleting 'min' would make the sentence incomplete, so it is explanatory, and the plural retains its full meaning of at least three. Thus, she owes three dirhams.

Key Terms
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation paid to the husband.
من (min): Here, it is used as a conjunctive particle (li al-sila) meaning 'of' in an explanatory sense, not partitive.
جمع (jam'): The plural form; in Arabic, the minimum of the plural (jam' al-qillah) is three.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Two dirhams
C) Three dirhams
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a woman uses the plural 'darahim' with explanatory 'min' in a khul' contract, she owes at least three dirhams even if she has nothing at the time.

Khul' on a Runaway Slave with Immunity Condition
Ruling on khul' for a runaway slave with condition of immunity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on a stipulation of immunity in khul' for a runaway slave and explain why the condition is fasid while the contract remains valid.

Core Idea
Condition of immunity in khul' for a runaway slave is fasid, but the khul' remains valid; wife must deliver slave or its value.

In this passage, al-Marghinani addresses a specific case of khul' where the wife offers an absconding slave as the consideration and stipulates that she is free from liability for delivering him. The ruling clarifies that such a stipulation is not effective; she remains obliged to deliver the slave or pay its value. The reasoning draws on the nature of khul' as a contract of exchange, analogized to sale and marriage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the condition
The act is khul' (divorce initiated by the wife) where the consideration is a runaway slave, and the wife stipulates that she is free from liability for the slave. Identify the ruling: is she free from liability?
The passage says 'she is not free'—the condition is void.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is qiyas: khul' is a contract of exchange (mu'awadah), which inherently requires the countervalue to be safe from loss. The stipulation of immunity contradicts this essential requirement.
The Arabic phrase: 'لانه عقد المعاوضة فيقتضى سلامة العوض'
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Because khul' is like a sale, the consideration must be deliverable. Stipulating immunity from liability negates the obligation to deliver, which is against the nature of the contract. Hence the condition is fasid and void.
The condition is void (yubtil), but the contract is not invalidated.
4
Note the exception: fasid conditions do not void khul'
Although the condition is fasid, khul' itself remains valid. Only the condition is void. This is analogous to marriage where a fasid condition does not invalidate the marriage.
الا ان الخلع لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة
5
Apply the analogy to marriage
The author states that the same ruling applies to marriage: if a woman marries a man with a runaway slave as mahr and stipulates immunity, she still must deliver the slave or its value.
وعلى هذا النكاح

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان اختلعت على عبد لها ابق على انها بريئة من ضمانه لم تبر أو عليها تسليم عينه ان قدرت و تسلیم قیمته ان عجزت لانه عقد المعاوضة فيقتضى سلامة العوض واشتراط البراءة عنه شرط فاسد فيبطل الا ان الخلع لا يبطل بالشروط الفاسدة وعلى هذا النكاح
And if she takes khul' for a slave of hers who is absconding, on the condition that she is free from liability for him, she is not free; she must deliver his physical self if she is able, and deliver his value if she is unable, because it is a contract of exchange (mu'awadah) so it requires safety of the countervalue; stipulating freedom from it is a fasid (invalid) condition, but it is void, and khul' is not invalidated by fasid conditions. And on this is analogized marriage.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage gives a ruling and its proof. The ruling: if a woman takes khul' from her husband in exchange for a runaway slave, and she stipulates that she is not liable for delivering the slave, she is not freed from that liability. She must deliver the slave if she can; if she cannot, she must pay the slave's market value. The proof: khul' is a contract of exchange (mu'awadah), which inherently requires that the countervalue (the slave) be free from defects or loss. By stipulating immunity from liability, she is imposing a condition that contradicts the nature of the contract. Therefore, the condition is fasid (invalid) and is void. However, khul', like marriage, is not invalidated by a fasid condition; only the condition is void, and the contract remains valid. So she owes the slave or its value. The author analogizes this to marriage: if a man marries a woman with a runaway slave as mahr, and stipulates immunity from liability, he is still liable to deliver the slave or its value.

Key Terms
عبد آبق (abd abiq): A slave who has run away from his owner, making delivery uncertain.
شرط فاسد (shart fasid): A condition that contradicts the nature of the contract, rendering it invalid but not nullifying the contract itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a woman takes khul' for a runaway slave with the condition that she is not liable, what must she do?
A) She is free from liability, no payment
B) She must deliver the slave or pay its value
C) The khul' is invalid
D) She must pay only if the slave is found

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a condition of immunity from delivery in khul' is fasid and void, but the khul' itself remains valid, obligating the wife to deliver the consideration or its value.

Khul' with a Minor Wife: Conditions and Mahr Scenarios
Rulings on khul' with a minor wife: condition and mahr scenarios.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on khul' with a minor wife, explain why compensation is not obligatory, and identify the two narrations regarding the father's acceptance.

Core Idea
A minor's khul' is valid for divorce but does not impose financial liability on her.

This passage from the chapter of Khul' addresses the specific situation when a husband makes khul' with his minor wife. The text differentiates between the validity of the divorce and the obligation of compensation, highlighting the minor's lack of capacity to bear financial liability. It also presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the father's acceptance is valid, with two transmitted narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The husband makes khul' with his minor wife by offering a condition (e.g., 1000 dirhams) or using her mahr. The ruling: the divorce (talaq) is valid if the minor accepts.
The minor must have understanding of khul' implications.
2
Determine the financial consequence
Even though the husband stipulated compensation, the minor is not liable to pay because she lacks legal capacity for financial obligations (ahliyyat al-ghurm).
The mal (wealth) is not wajib upon her.
3
Analyze the two narrations on father's acceptance
If the father accepts the khul' on behalf of the minor, there are two narrations: one validates (istihsan), the other invalidates (qiyas on shart yameen).
The first narration considers it pure benefit for the minor.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
The preferred position is the validity of the father's acceptance because it is naqa' mahd (pure benefit).
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
5
Apply to the mahr scenario
If khul' is on the mahr and the father does not guarantee it, the same rules apply: minor's acceptance causes divorce but mahr is not dropped.
The father's acceptance again has two narrations.

Chapter of Khul'. And the wealth is not obligatory because she is not among those liable for compensation. If the father accepts on her behalf, then there are two narrations. Translation: And if the husband made this thousand dirhams conditional upon the minor wife, then the validity of khul' is dependent on her acceptance, provided she is capable of accepting. So if the minor accepts, the divorce occurs because the condition is met, and the wealth is not obligatory because the minor is not capable of compensation. Then if the father accepts the khul' compensation on her behalf, there are two narrations. Explanation... And similarly, if he made khul' with her on her mahr and the father did not guarantee the mahr, it is dependent on her acceptance. So if she accepts, she is divorced and the mahr is not dropped. And if the father accepts on her behalf, then according to two narrations. Translation... Explanation...
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage from the chapter of Khul' discusses the legal rulings when a husband makes khul' with his minor wife (sagheerah) under two scenarios: first, when the husband conditions payment of a specified amount (e.g., 1000 dirhams) on her; second, when the khul' is on her mahr (dower) without the father's guarantee. The core ruling is that the validity of khul' with a minor depends on her own acceptance, provided she has the legal capacity to understand that khul' ends the marriage and entails giving compensation. If she accepts, the divorce takes effect (talaq occurs) because the condition of acceptance is met. However, the compensation (mal) is not obligatory upon her because as a minor she is not legally capable of bearing a financial liability (ghurm). If her father accepts the khul' on her behalf, there is a well-known ikhtilaf (dispute) within the Hanafi school: one narration (riwayah) validates the father's acceptance, likening it to accepting a gift for her benefit (since she gains freedom without paying). The other narration invalidates it, arguing that this acceptance is analogous to a conditional oath (shart yameen), which cannot be delegated to another person. These two narrations are recorded in the sources, and the mufta bihi (operative position) is the first (validity) as it is based on istihsan (juristic preference). In the second scenario (khul' on mahr without father's guarantee), the same rulings apply: the minor's acceptance effectuates divorce but does not nullify her right to the full mahr, because she is not liable for compensation. The father's acceptance again carries the two narrations. This passage illustrates the Hanafi principle that a minor's financial transactions are void (batil), but her personal status actions (like khul') can be valid with guardian consent under certain conditions.

Key Terms
صغیرہ (sagheerah): A minor female who has not attained puberty; legally incapable of binding financial obligations.
روایتان (riwayatan): Two transmitted opinions within the Hanafi school on a specific issue, often from different imams or narrations.
شرط یمین (shart yameen): A conditional oath; here, an analogy that the khul' condition is like an oath which cannot be delegated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The talaq does not occur because the minor cannot give consent.
B) The talaq occurs and the minor must pay 1000 dirhams.
C) The talaq occurs but the minor does not have to pay anything.
D) The talaq occurs and the father must pay the 1000 dirhams.

Key Takeaway
In khul' with a minor wife, the divorce takes effect upon her acceptance, but she is not liable for compensation; the father's acceptance is valid according to the preferred Hanafi view.

Father Guarantees Mahr in Khul' with Minor: Qiyas vs Istihsan
Ruling on father's guarantee with qiyas vs istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafi fiqh applies istihsan over qiyas in the case of a father guaranteeing mahr in khul' with a minor before consummation, and state the resulting ruling.

Core Idea
Istihsan reduces father's liability to half mahr because khul' before consummation only concerns half the mahr.

This passage presents a classic Hanafi demonstration of istihsan overriding qiyas. The scenario involves a father guaranteeing his minor daughter's entire mahr (1000 dirhams) in a khul' divorce before consummation. Strict analogy (qiyas) would hold the father liable for the full amount, but juristic preference (istihsan) reduces it to 500 dirhams, aligning with the underlying purpose of the transaction and customary practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
State the case: father guarantees the mahr of 1000 dirhams in khul' with minor before consummation. The ruling by istihsan is that the father must pay 500 dirhams; by qiyas he would pay 1000.
The text explicitly says 'يلزمه خمس مائة استحسانا' (500 obligatory by istihsan).
2
Understand the strict qiyas argument
Strict analogy: the father guaranteed the full mahr, so he should pay the full amount (1000). This would be the ruling if only qiyas were applied.
Qiyas here is based on the literal guarantee.
3
Trace the istihsan reasoning
Istihsan relies on the effective cause (illa): before consummation, only half the mahr is owed to the wife. Therefore, the actual compensation in khul' is effectively half the mahr. The father's guarantee is interpreted as covering that amount.
The text says: 'لانه يراد به عادة حاصل ما يلزم لها' (the usual purpose is to obtain what is obligatory for her).
4
Compare the adult woman's case (asl)
The case of an adult woman making khul' before consummation on her full mahr (1000) provides the analogy. By qiyas she would pay an extra 500, but by istihsan she pays nothing because the husband's purpose is to drop the entire mahr. This parallels the minor case.
In the adult case, istihsan eliminates the extra payment; in the minor case, it reduces the father's liability to half.
5
Recognize the role of custom and purpose
Istihsan prevails because it aligns with the custom ('urf) and the underlying purpose of khul' - to dissolve the marriage and settle the mahr obligation equitably. Strict qiyas would lead to hardship and contradict common practice.
This demonstrates the Hanafi method of prioritizing istihsan over qiyas when the latter produces harsh results.

Source Text

And if the father guaranteed the mahr, and it is a thousand dirhams, the woman is divorced because his acceptance is found and that is the condition, and 500 dirhams are obligatory upon him by istihsan, and by qiyas the thousand would be obligatory upon him. Its origin is in the case of an adult woman when she made khul' before consummation on a thousand while her mahr is a thousand: by qiyas an extra 500 is upon her, but by istihsan nothing is upon her because the usual purpose is to obtain what is obligatory for her. Commentary
This passage continues the discussion of khul' with a minor wife, now focusing on the scenario where the father guarantees the mahr (dower) amount. The ruling: if the father guarantees the mahr (which is 1000 dirhams in this example), then the divorce occurs because the father's acceptance fulfills the condition. However, the father is only obliged to pay 500 dirhams by istihsan (juristic preference), whereas qiyas (analogy) would require 1000 dirhams. The text explains the reasoning by drawing an analogy (asl) to the case of an adult woman who makes khul' before consummation on an amount equivalent to her mahr (1000 dirhams). In that case, qiyas dictates that she must pay an extra 500 dirhams on top of the mahr she already owes? Actually careful: The asl: adult woman makes khul' before consummation for 1000 while her mahr is 1000. Since she hasn't received the mahr, by talaq before consummation, half the mahr (500) falls due from husband. But she agreed to pay 1000 total? The text says: qiyas would require 500 extra upon her (i.e., she must pay 500 more to make 1000, because 500 is already dropped from husband's liability? Let me parse: The adult woman owes 1000 in khul'; but 500 of that is offset by the half mahr that was due to her. Actually, hanafi ruling: If a woman makes khul' before consummation for the full mahr or more, she must pay the difference between what she agreed and what her husband owes her as half mahr. Here, she agreed to pay 1000; husband owes her 500 as half mahr, so she must pay 500 to the husband. So qiyas: she must pay 500 extra (in addition to the half mahr already dropped). Istihsan: she pays nothing extra because the husband's purpose is to drop the entire mahr, and that purpose is achieved. In the minor case, the father guarantees the mahr (1000). The minor had not received mahr. By qiyas, father would pay 1000 (since he guaranteed the full amount). But istihsan reduces it to 500, because the actual consideration in khul' is half the mahr (since before consummation, half mahr is due). So the father's liability is only half. The text emphasizes that istihsan is based on the usual purpose of such khul' transactions. This illustrates the Hanafi method of preferring istihsan over strict qiyas when the latter leads to hardship or contradicts custom.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides strict qiyas to avoid hardship or to align with custom and underlying purpose.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical deduction; here, strict analogy would require the full amount of the guarantee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When the father guarantees the mahr (1000 dirhams) in khul' with his minor daughter before consummation, how much is he required to pay by istihsan?
A) 1000 dirhams (the full amount).
B) Nothing, because the minor cannot be liable.
C) 500 dirhams (half the mahr).
D) It depends on the daughter's agreement.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, istihsan overrides qiyas in khul' with minor before consummation, reducing the father's guarantee to half the mahr because only that amount is due to the wife.

Introduction to Zihar: Comparison with Khul'
Opening of Bab al-Zihar explaining its relation to the previous chapter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define zihar and khul', explain the difference in their legal effects, and state why the chapter on khul' precedes zihar.

Core Idea
In zihar the marriage remains but intercourse is haram; in khul' the marriage ends.

This lesson opens the chapter on Zihar, a pre-Islamic form of divorce-like prohibition. The author immediately connects it to the previous chapter on Khul' (divorce initiated by the wife) by noting that both arise from nushuz (rebellion). He explains that Khul' is placed first because its legal effect is more severe: Khul' severs the marriage, while Zihar only prohibits intercourse while the marriage continues. Understanding this distinction is essential before diving into the detailed rulings of Zihar.

Guided Path
1
Define Zihar and Khul'
Identify the two legal concepts: Zihar is a husband's statement comparing his wife to a female relative, creating a temporary prohibition; Khul' is a divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation.
Both involve marital discord, but the outcomes differ.
2
Compare the legal effects
Note that in Khul' the marriage is completely severed (tahrim stronger), while in Zihar the marriage remains but intercourse becomes haram until expiation.
This is the key distinction.
3
Understand the order of chapters
Khul' is placed before Zihar because its prohibition is stronger (tahrim aghlaz). The chapter sequence reflects increasing severity.
The author uses this as a teaching tool.
4
Apply the definitions
Practice distinguishing between a Khul' statement and a Zihar statement in simple scenarios.
Focus on the intent and consequence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الظهار ترجمہ (یہ) باب ظہار ) کے احکام کے بیان میں ) ہے۔ تشریح ظہار اور ضلع میں مناسبت یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک نشوز اور سرکشی کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے اور ضلع کو ظہار پر اس لئے ظہار اورضلع ہرایک سےہوتا اور کو پر اس مقدم کیا ہے کہ ضلع میں تحریم زیادہ ہے کیونکہ ضلع کی صورت میں نکاح منقطع ہو کر تحریم ثابت ہوتی ہے اور ظہار میں نکاح باقی رہتے ہوئے حرمت ثابت ہو جاتی ہے۔
Chapter of Zihar. Translation: This is a chapter on the rulings of Zihar. Explanation: The connection between Zihar and Khul' is that each of them occurs due to nushuz (rebellion) and disobedience. And Khul' has been placed before Zihar because in Khul' the prohibition (tahrim) is stronger, as in Khul' the marriage is severed and prohibition is established, whereas in Zihar the marriage remains while prohibition occurs.
Source pages p. 106

Commentary
This short passage opens the chapter on Zihar (ظہار), which is a pre-Islamic form of divorce where a man says to his wife 'You are to me like the back of my mother' (zihar). The author explains why this chapter follows the chapter on Khul': both occur due to nushuz (rebellion or disobedience) of the wife. However, the order places Khul' first because the prohibition (tahrim) resulting from Khul' is stronger: in Khul', the marriage is severed (the marital bond is terminated), while in Zihar, the marriage remains but a prohibition on intercourse is established until expiation. Thus, Khul' involves a more severe legal consequence. This introductory note sets the stage for the detailed rulings of Zihar that follow in the subsequent pages.

Key Terms
ظہار (zihar): A form of divorce-like prohibition where the husband compares his wife to his mother's back, making her temporarily prohibited until expiation.
خلع (khul'): Divorce initiated by the wife in exchange for compensation to the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because Khul' involves a stronger prohibition (tahrim) than Zihar.
C) Because Zihar is more common than Khul'.
D) Because Khul' only applies to minors.

Key Takeaway
Khul' severs the marriage, while zihar only prohibits intercourse; thus khul' is placed first due to its stronger legal effect.

Invalidity of Zihar in a Fuduli Marriage Before Ratification
Explaining the invalidity of zihar in a fuduli marriage before ratification

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why zihar is invalid in a fuduli marriage before ratification and distinguish it from the case of emancipating a bought slave using the concept of rights vs. speech acts.

Core Idea
Zihar requires false speech; if the woman is not a lawful wife at the time, the comparison is truthful and does not constitute zihar.

In this passage from Al-Hidayah, we examine a specific ruling: if a man marries a woman through an unauthorized agent (fuduli) without her permission, then pronounces zihar before she ratifies the marriage, the zihar is invalid even if she later accepts. The key is that zihar is defined by the Quran as 'evil and false speech' (munkaran min al-qawl wa zuran). For it to be false, the woman must be a lawful wife at the time of utterance. Since she was not, the speech was truthful, and zihar does not take effect. The passage also addresses a potential analogy with the emancipation of a slave bought from a usurper, which is suspended on ratification, and explains why the analogy fails.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is zihar (saying 'You are like my mother's back to me') performed in a marriage contracted by a fuduli. The ruling is that the zihar is invalid (batil).
2
Understand the essential element of zihar
Zihar requires false speech comparing a lawful wife to a mahram relative. Without falsity, the essential element (rukn) is absent.
Quran 58:2 describes zihar as 'evil and false speech'.
3
Analyze the proof
At the time of zihar, the woman was not a lawful wife (haram due to lack of permission), so the comparison was truthful. Hence the speech is not 'evil and false' and does not constitute zihar.
4
Address the objection
Why is zihar not suspended like emancipation in the usurper case? Because emancipation is a right of ownership that can be suspended; zihar is a speech act that must be false at the moment.
The qiyas with the usurper's slave fails due to different natures (right vs. speech).
5
Apply the distinction
Learn the rule: the validity of zihar depends on the marital status at the time of utterance, not later ratification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

فان تزوج امرأة بغير امـرهـاثـم ظاهر منها ثم اجازت النكاح فالظهار باطل لانه صادق في التشبيه وقت التصرف فلم يكن منكرا من القول والظهارليس بحق من حقوقه حتى يتوقف بخلاف اعتاق المشترى من الغاصب لانه من حقوق الملك

والظهار ليس بحق سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے سوال یہ ہے کہ ظہار موقوف ہے ملک نکاح پر اور ملک نکاح موقوف ہے عورت کی اجازت پر اس وجہ سے مناسب ہے کہ ظہار عورت کی اجازت پر موقوف ہو پس جب عورت نکاح کی اجازت دید سے تو ظہار صحیح ہو جانا چاہیے جیسے کسی شخص نے غاصب سے غلام خرید کر آزاد کر دیا ہوتو یہ آزاد کرنا اس پر موقوف ہے کہ مغصوب منہ یعنی مالک اس بیچ کی اجازت دئے جو غاصب اور مشتری کے درمیان ہوئی ہے، پس جس طرح مشتری من الغاصب کا آزاد کرانا مغصوب منہ کی اجازت بیع پر موقوف ہے اسی طرح ظہار عورت کی اجازت نکاح پر موقوف ہونا چاہیے تھا۔
If he marries a woman without her permission, then does zihar with her, then the woman gives permission for the marriage, the zihar is invalid. Because he was truthful in the similitude at the time of the action, so he was not one who says evil and false speech. And zihar is not a right from his rights such that it would be suspended. Contrary to the emancipation of a buyer from a usurper, because it is from the rights of ownership. Translation: So if a man marries a woman without her permission, then that man does zihar with her, then the woman gives permission for the marriage, then the zihar is invalid. Because this person at the time of his action was truthful in the similitude. So he was not one who says foul and false speech. And zihar is not one of the husband's rights such that it would be suspended. Contrary to the emancipation of a buyer from a usurper, because emancipation is among the rights of ownership. Explanation of the case: If a person marries a woman without her command, i.e., a fuduli (unauthorized agent) conducted the marriage on her behalf, then this person does zihar with her, then the woman gives permission for the marriage, then this zihar is invalid. The proof is that this person at the time of zihar was truthful in the similitude, because before permission this woman was unlawful (haram) for him. Therefore the essential element (rukn) of zihar—i.e., comparing the wife (mahall) to a mahram—was not found. Hence this person did not become one who says false and evil speech (munkaran min al-qawl wa zuran). And zihar is named 'munkaran min al-qawl wa zuran'. So when the essential element of zihar was not found, this person is not one who does zihar. 'And zihar is not a right' is an answer to a question. The question is: Zihar is suspended on the ownership of marriage (milk al-nikah), and ownership of marriage is suspended on the woman's permission. Therefore it would be appropriate that zihar be suspended on the woman's permission. Then when the woman gives permission for the marriage, the zihar should become valid, just as when a person buys a slave from a usurper and then frees him, this emancipation is suspended on the permission of the rightful owner (maghsib minhu) for the sale. So just as the emancipation by the buyer from the usurper is suspended on the permission of the owner for the sale, similarly zihar should be suspended on the woman's permission for the marriage.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the validity of zihar in a marriage conducted by a fuduli (unauthorized agent) without the woman's consent. The ruling is that if a man marries a woman through a fuduli, then does zihar before the woman ratifies the marriage, the zihar is invalid even if she later ratifies the marriage. The reasoning is that at the time of the zihar statement, the woman was not his lawful wife (she was haram for him due to lack of permission), so the similitude (tashbih) in zihar—comparing the wife to a mahram relative—was truthful, not false. In Islamic law, zihar is condemned as evil and false speech (munkaran min al-qawl wa zuran) because it falsely compares a lawful wife to a forbidden relative. If the comparison is truthful (i.e., the woman was actually forbidden at that time), the speech is not evil or false, so it does not constitute zihar. The passage then answers a potential objection: 'But shouldn't zihar be suspended (mawquf) on the marriage ownership, which itself is suspended on ratification, similar to the case where a person buys a slave from a usurper and then frees him—the emancipation is suspended on the owner's ratification of the sale?' The answer is that the two cases are different: emancipation is a right of ownership (haqq min huquq al-milk), so it can be suspended on the owner's permission. Zihar, however, is not a right of the husband; it is a form of speech that must be false to take effect. Since the speech was truthful, it cannot be zihar. The analogy with the usurper's case is thus rejected.

Key Terms
فضولی (fuduli): An unauthorized person who acts on behalf of another without prior permission; here, one who contracts marriage on behalf of a woman without her consent.
موقوف (mawquf): Suspended; a contract or act whose validity is conditional upon subsequent ratification.
منکر من القول و زورا (munkaran min al-qawl wa zuran): Evil and false speech; this is the Quranic description of zihar (58:2). The effectiveness of zihar depends on the speech being false—i.e., comparing a lawful wife to a mahram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is zihar invalid in a fuduli marriage even after the woman ratifies it?
A) Because zihar is a right of the husband and cannot be suspended.
B) Because at the time of zihar the woman was not a wife, so the comparison was truthful, and zihar requires false speech.
C) Because the fuduli's marriage is always invalid regardless of ratification.
D) Because zihar must be pronounced in the presence of witnesses.

Key Takeaway
A zihar pronounced before the marriage is ratified is invalid because it lacks the essential falsity required for zihar.

Dhihar to Multiple Wives: One Expiation or Multiple?
Ruling on dhihar to multiple wives with dispute on number of expiations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on dhihar to multiple wives and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument using the illa of hurma versus sanctity of Allah's name.

Core Idea
Each wife's prohibition is separate, requiring a separate expiation – one for each, not one for all.

When a husband declares dhihar to multiple wives simultaneously, the key dispute is whether one expiation suffices or multiple are required. The Hanafi school, along with Imam Shafi'i and early authorities, holds that the prohibition (hurma) attaches to each wife individually, so the expiation must be individual. The Maliki school analogizes to ila, where a single expiation suffices. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the practical difference.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on multiple dhihar
Identify the ruling: the man becomes mazahir to all wives simultaneously, and a separate kaffarah is due for each wife before relations can resume.
2
Identify the opposing school and its proof
Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad hold that one kaffarah suffices. They analogize (qiyas) to ila: in ila from multiple wives, only one kaffarah is due on breaking the oath.
The qiyas is on the ruling level, not the cause.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response: distinguishing the illa
In dhihar, kaffarah removes a personal prohibition (hurma) attached to each wife. In ila, kaffarah is for violating the sanctity of Allah's name, which is singular. The cause is different, so the analogy fails.
The illa in dhihar is the individual hurma; in ila it is the violation of a single oath using Allah's name.
4
Apply the ruling to a practical scenario
Hanafi: a man with four wives must perform four separate kaffarahs (e.g., fasting 60 days for each, or feeding 60 poor for each) before he can approach any wife. Maliki: one kaffarah suffices for all.
The thamarah al-khilaf directly affects the husband's obligation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شوہر نے اپنی بیویوں کو کہا اَنْتُنَّ عَلَيَّ كَظَهُرٍ اُمّی سب سے ظہار کرنے والا ہوگا

ومن قال لنسائه انتن على كظهر امي كان مظاهرا منهن جميعا لانه اضاف الظهار اليهن فصار كما اذا اضاف الطلاق و عليه لكل واحدة كفارة لان الحرمة تثبت في حق كل واحدة والكفارة لانهاء الحرمة فيتعدد بتعددها بخلاف الايلاء منهن لان الكفارة فيه لصيانة حرمة الاسم و لم يتعدد ذكر الاسم

ترجمہ اور جس شخص نے اپنی عورتوں سے کہا تم میرے اوپر میری ماں کی پیٹھ کے ماند ہوتو یہ شخص ) ان سب سے ظہار کرنے والا ہو جائے گا ۔ کیونکہ اس نے ان کی طرف ظہار منسوب کیا ہے۔ پس ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ جب اس نے (ان کی طرف ) طلاق کو منسوب کیا ہو اور اس شخص پر ہر ایک کے لیے کفارہ واجب ہوگا اس لئے کہ حرمت ہر ایک کے حق میں ثابت ہوگئی ہے اور کفارہ حرمت کو ختم کرنے کے لئے ہوتا ہے لہذا حرمت کے متعدد ہو جانے سے کفارہ متعدد ہو جائے گا۔ برخلاف ان سے ایلاء کرنے کے، کیونکہ کفارہ ایلاء میں اللہ کے نام کی تعظیم و حرمت کی حفاظت کے لئے ہے اور حال یہ کہ اللہ کے نام کا ذکر متعدد نہیں ہوا۔

تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص نے اپنی متعدد عورتوں سے کہا انتن علی کظیر امی تو شخص بالا تفاق ان سب عورتوں سے ظہار کرنے والا ہو جائے گا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس شخص نے تمام عورتوں کی طرف ظہار منسوب کیا ہے۔لہذا تمام سے ظہار ثابت ہوگا۔ جیسے اگر یہ شخص اپنی تمام عورتوں کی طرف طلاق منسوب کرتے ہوئے کہتا انتن طوالق ، تو سب پر طلاق واقع ہو جاتی ۔ رہی یہ بات کہ شوہر پر تمام کی وجہ سے ایک کفارہ واجب ہوگا یا متعدد ، سو اس بارے میں اختلاف ہے، چنانچہ ہمارے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک ظہار کے متعدد ہونے کی وجہ سے کفارے متعدد ہوں گے ان میں سے جن کے ساتھ وطی کرنے کا ارادہ کرے گا اس کی وجہ سے شوہر پر پہلے کفارہ واجب ہوگا اس کے قائل ہیں حسن، امام شخصی ، امام زہری اور امام ثوری، امام مالک اور امام احمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ سب کی طرف سے ایک کفارہ کافی ہو جائے گا امام مالک اور امام احمد کفارہ ظہار کو قیاس کرتے ہیں کفارہ ایلاء پر کہ جس طرح اپنی متعدد عورتوں سے ایلاء کرتے ہوئے کہا اللہ لا اقر بکن اور مدت ایلاء میں کسی کے قریب نہیں گیا یہاں تک کہ چار ماہ کی مدت گزرگئی تو سب پر طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اور اگر مدت ایلاء کے اندر سب سے ولی کر لی تو اس پر صرف ایک کفارہ واجب ہوگا اسی طرح اگر متعد د عورتوں سے ظہار کیا ہے تو اس صورت میں بھی ایک ہی کفارہ واجب ہوگا۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ظہار کی وجہ سے ہر ایک عورت کے حق میں حرمت ثابت ہو گئی ہے اور کفارہ اس لئے ہوتا ہے کہ حرمت کو ختم کر دے لہذا جتنی حرمتیں ہوں گی اسی قدر کفارے ہوں گے اور رہا ایلا ، تو اس میں اللہ کے نام کی بے حرمتی کرنے کی وجہت کفارہ واجب ہوتا ہے اور چونکہ سب عورتوں سے ایک ایلاء کرنے میں اللہ کا نام متعدد ند کور نہیں ہوا اس وجہ سے ایک ہی کفارہ واجب ہوگا نہ کہ متعدد جمیل احمد عفی عنہ
The husband said to his wives: 'You are to me like the back of my mother.' He will be a mazahir (one who declares dhihar) to all of them. And whoever said to his women: 'You are to me like the back of my mother,' he is a mazahir from all of them, because he attributed the dhihar to them, so it becomes like when he attributed divorce. And upon him is a kaffarah for each one, because the prohibition (hurma) is established for each one, and the kaffarah is to terminate the prohibition, so it multiplies with its multiplicity, unlike ila from them, because the kaffarah in it is for the sanctity of the name, and the mention of the name is not multiplied. Translation: And whoever said to his women: 'You are to me like the back of my mother' - this person will become a mazahir to all of them. Because he attributed dhihar to them. So it becomes like when he attributed divorce to them. And upon him is a kaffarah for each one, because the prohibition (hurma) is established for each one, and the kaffarah is to remove the prohibition, so because the prohibitions are multiple, the kaffarah becomes multiple. Unlike ila from them, because the kaffarah in ila is to protect the sanctity of the name of Allah, and the mention of the name of Allah is not multiple. Explanation: The case is that if a person said to his multiple wives: 'antunna 'ala ka zahri ummi,' then this person, by agreement, becomes a mazahir from all of them. The proof is that he attributed dhihar to all of them, so dhihar is proven from all. As if he attributed divorce to all of them saying 'antunna tawaliq,' divorce would occur to all. As to whether one kaffarah is due or multiple: there is disagreement. According to us (Hanafis) and Imam Shafi'i, due to the multiplicity of dhihar, the kaffarahs are multiple; from which one he intends to have intercourse, for that a kaffarah is due first. This is the view of Hasan, al-Sha'bi, al-Zuhri, and al-Thawri. Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad said that one kaffarah suffices for all. Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad analogize the kaffarah of dhihar to the kaffarah of ila: just as if a man makes ila from his multiple wives, saying 'Allah! La aqrabu bikunna' and does not approach any during the period until four months pass, then divorce occurs to all; but if he approaches them within the period, only one kaffarah is due. Similarly, if he made dhihar from multiple wives, one kaffarah suffices. Our proof is that because of dhihar, a prohibition (hurma) is established for each wife, and kaffarah is to remove the prohibition, so as many prohibitions, so many kaffarahs. As for ila, the kaffarah is due because of the disrespect of the name of Allah, and since in one ila from all wives the name of Allah is not multiplied, only one kaffarah is due, not multiple. Jamil Ahmad 'ufiya 'anhu.
Source pages p. 116

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on dhihar (a reprehensible form of declaring one's wife like one's mother) when a man addresses his multiple wives collectively. The ruling is clear: he becomes a mazahir from all of them, just as he would if he divorced all of them with a single statement. The main point of legal disagreement (ikhtilaf) is whether he owes one expiation (kaffarah) or multiple. The Hanafi school, along with Imam al-Shafi'i and several early authorities, holds that multiple expiations are required, one for each wife. The reasoning (ta'lil) is that dhihar establishes a specific prohibition (hurma) against marital relations with each wife individually, and expiation is the means to remove that prohibition. Since the prohibition is multiple, the expiation must be multiple. In contrast, Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad hold that one expiation suffices, drawing an analogy (qiyas) to ila (an oath of abstention). In ila, if a man swears not to approach any of his wives and then breaks his oath by approaching one, only one expiation is due, even though the oath was against all. The Hanafi response distinguishes the two cases: in ila, the expiation is for violating the sanctity of Allah's name, which was pronounced only once; in dhihar, the expiation is for removing a personal prohibition, which is individually attached to each wife. The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that a Hanafi must perform a separate expiation for each wife before being allowed to resume marital relations, while a Maliki may do a single expiation for all. The text affirms the Hanafi position as the relied-upon view.

Key Terms
ظهار (Dhihar): A declaration by a husband that his wife is like his mother's back, rendering marital relations prohibited until expiation.
ايلاء (Ila): An oath by a husband to abstain from marital relations with his wife for a period of four months or more.
كفارة (Kaffarah): An expiatory act required to remove a prohibition or sin, such as in dhihar, ila, or breaking an oath.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many expiations are required if a man declares dhihar to his four wives simultaneously?
A) One expiation for all
B) Four expiations, one for each wife
C) Two expiations, one for the first two and one for the last two
D) No expiation is required because dhihar is invalid if addressed to multiple wives

Key Takeaway
Dhihar to multiple wives creates multiple independent prohibitions, each requiring its own expiation before relations can resume.

The Sequential Kaffarah for Dhihar
Ruling on the sequential obligations of expiation for dhihar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the cause of kaffarah for dhihar, recite the sequential steps of expiation, and explain why 'fa' indicates order, not choice.

Core Idea
Kaffarah for dhihar is sequential: free, then fast, then feed — 'fa' commands order, not option.

This chapter explains the expiation required when a husband declares dhihar and intends to return to his wife. The ruling is derived directly from Surah Al-Mujadilah, where the word 'fa' establishes a strict sequence. The Hanafi school holds that the obligation arises only upon the husband's decision to resume relations ('aud).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the kaffarah (expiation) for dhihar. It is wajib upon the husband when he intends to return to his wife after declaring dhihar.
The Hanafi school differs on whether the cause is dhihar alone or dhihar plus 'aud; the mufta bihi is the latter.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is Quran 58:3-4. The verse mentions freeing a slave, then fasting, then feeding, each preceded by 'fa'.
The verse is qati al-thubut (certain transmission) but zanni al-dalala (speculative meaning) regarding the sequential interpretation.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In Hanafi usul, the particle 'fa' (ف) indicates immediate succession and sequence (tartib). Therefore the three alternatives are ordered, not optional.
Other schools may interpret 'fa' differently, leading to different rulings on choice versus sequence.
4
Apply the sequence
The husband must first free a slave. If he cannot (due to financial inability or unavailability), he must fast two consecutive months. If he cannot fast (e.g., due to illness), he must feed sixty poor people.
Inability is assessed at each step; one cannot skip to feeding unless both previous options are genuinely impossible.

فصل في الكفارة

ترجمه ی فصل کفارہ (کے احکام کے بیان ) میں ہے

تشریح سابق میں مصنف نے ظہار کا حکم یعنی حرمت ولی اور حرمت دوائی ولی کو ذکر فرمایا ہے ۔ لہذا اس فصل میں اس چیز کو بیان کریں گے جس سے یہ حرمت ختم ہو جائے گی یعنی کفارہ، علماء نے اختلاف کیا ہے کہ اس کفارہ کا سبب کیا ہے پس جمہور مشائخ کے نزدیک کفارہ ظہار کا سبب ،ظہار اور بھی کی طرف رجوع کرنا ہے۔ کیونکہ قرآن پاک کی آیت والذين يظـاهـرون من نسائهم ثم يعودون لما قالوا فتحرير رقبة میں اللہ تعالیٰ نے کفارہ کا سبب بیان کرتے ہوئے عود ( ولی کی طرف رجوع کرنا ) کا ظہار پر عطف کیا ہے پھر فا کے ذریعہ سے اس پر حکم مرتب کیا ہے اور قاعدہ ہے کہ معطوف علیہ اور معطوف کے بعد اگر کوئی حکم ذکر کیا جائے تو یہ حکم دونوں کی طرف منسوب ہوتا ہے پس معلوم ہوا کہ ظہار اور عود دونوں کا مجموعہ کفارہ ظہار کا سب سے اور مینی شرح ہدایہ میں مذکور ہے کہ اس کفارہ کا سبب صرف عود یعنی ولی کی طرف رجوع کرنا ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب

کفارہ ظہار
و كفارة الظهار عتق رقبة فان لم يجد فصيام شهرين متتابعين فان لم يستطيع فاطعام ستين مسكينا للنص الواردفيه فانه يفيد الكفارة على هذا الترتيب

ترجمہ کہا اور کفارہ ظہار ایک غلام کا آزاد کرنا ہے پھر اگر غلام نہ پاوے تو دو ماہ کے پے در پے روزے رکھے۔ پھر اگر یہ طاقت نہ ہو تو ساٹھ مسکینوں کوکھانا دے اس نص کی وجہ سے جو کفارہ ظہار کے باب میں وارد ہوئی ہے اس لئے کہ یہ نص اسی ترتیب کے ساتھ کفارہ کا افادہ کرتی ہے۔

تشریح امام قدوری نے کفارہ ظہار کی ترتیب بیان فرمائی ہے کہ ایک غلام آزاد کرے اگر اس پر قدرت نہ ہو تو پے در پے ساتھ روزے رکھے اور اگر اس کی بھی قدرت نہ ہو تو ساتھ مسکینوں کو کھانا دے۔ دلیل نص قرآنی ہے یعنی فتحرير رقبه من قبل ان يتماسا ذالكم توعظون به والله بما تعملون خبير فمن لم يجد فصيام شهرين متتابعين من قبل ان يتمآسافمن لم يستطع فاطعام ستين مسكينا ذالک لتو منوا بالله و رسوله - ترجمہ: ۔ ایک غلام یا لونڈی کا آزاد کرنا ہے قبل اس کے کہ دونوں (میاں بیوی ) باہم اختلاط کریں اس سے تم کو نصیحت کی جاتی ہے اللہ تعالی کو تمہارے سب اعمال کی پوری خبر ہے پھر جس کو ( غلام لونڈی ) میسر نہ ہو تو اس کے ذمہ پے در پے (لگا تار ) دو مہینے کے روزے ہیں قبل اس کے کہ دونوں باہم اختلاط کر میں پھر جس سے یہ بھی نہ ہو سکیں تو اس کے ذمہ ساٹھ مسکینوں کو کھانا کھلانا ہے یہ حکم اس لئے ( بیان کیا گیا ہے ) ہے کہ اللہ اور اس کے رسول پر ایمان لے آؤ ( مرشد تھانوی) یہ نص مفید ترتیب ہے کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے کلمہ فاکے ساتھ بیان فرمایا ہے اور فاء ترتیب کے لیے آتا ہے نہ کہ تخیر کے لئے۔
Chapter on the Kaffarah

Translation: This chapter is on the rulings of kaffarah (expiation).

Explanation: Previously the author mentioned the ruling of dhihar, i.e., the prohibition of marital relations and the prohibition of something else. Therefore in this chapter we will mention that which removes this prohibition, i.e., kaffarah. The scholars differed as to what is the cause (sabab) of this kaffarah. According to the majority of mashayikh, the cause of kaffarah of dhihar is dhihar and the return (al-'aud) to the wife. Because in the Quranic verse, 'Those who declare dhihar among you from their wives, then they return to what they said, then free a slave' (58:3), Allah mentioned the cause of kaffarah by connecting 'aud (return) to dhihar, then attached the ruling with 'fa'. And the rule is that when a ruling is mentioned after the conjunction and the conjoined, the ruling is attributed to both. So it becomes clear that the combination of dhihar and 'aud is the cause. And in Minih Sharh Hidayah it is mentioned that the cause of this kaffarah is only 'aud (return to the wife). And Allah knows best.

Kaffarah of Dhihar
And the kaffarah of dhihar is to free a slave; if he does not find one, then fasting for two consecutive months; if he is unable, then feeding sixty poor people, due to the text that has come, because it conveys the kaffarah in this order.

Translation: He (al-Quduri) said: The kaffarah of dhihar is to free a slave; then if he does not find, then fast for two consecutive months; then if he is unable, then feed sixty poor people. This is due to the text that has come in the chapter of dhihar, because the text conveys the kaffarah in this order.

Explanation: Imam al-Quduri mentioned the order of kaffarah: free a slave; if unable, fast two consecutive months; if also unable, feed sixty poor. The proof is the Quranic text: 'free a slave before they touch each other; this is an admonition to you, and Allah is Aware of what you do. And whoever does not find [or is unable] then fasting for two consecutive months before they touch each other; and whoever is not able then feeding sixty poor persons. This that you may believe in Allah and His Messenger.' (58:3-4). This text conveys order because Allah expressed it with the word 'fa', and 'fa' is for sequence (tartib), not for choice (takhyir).
Source pages p. 117

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter (fasl) on the kaffarah (expiation) for dhihar. It first discusses the cause (sabab) of the expiation: the majority of Hanafi scholars hold that both the dhihar declaration and the 'aud (intention to return to the wife) together are the cause, based on the Quranic verse where 'aud is conjoined to dhihar and the ruling is attached with 'fa'. However, some (like the author of Minih Sharh Hidayah) maintain that only 'aud is the cause. The relied-upon view is that the kaffarah becomes obligatory only when the husband decides to resume marital relations, not upon merely uttering the dhihar. The core ruling is the sequence of the kaffarah itself, based on the clear text of the Quran (58:3-4). The sequence is strict: first, freeing a slave; if incapable (due to poverty or unavailability), then fasting two consecutive months; if incapable (due to health reasons), then feeding sixty poor people. The word 'fa' in the verse indicates sequential order (tartib), not option (takhyir). Thus, the kaffarah must be performed in this exact order, moving to the next only if unable to fulfill the previous. This is the standard Hanafi position, known from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
عود (Aud): The husband's intention or act of returning to his wife after declaring dhihar, which makes the kaffarah obligatory.
ترتیب (Tartib): Sequence or order; in this context, the required order of performing the three types of kaffarah: first freeing, then fasting, then feeding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Fast for two consecutive months
C) Free a slave even if he cannot afford it
D) He may choose any of the three options

Key Takeaway
The kaffarah for dhihar is not optional; it must follow the strict sequence of freeing, then fasting, then feeding, based on the particle 'fa' in Surah Al-Mujadilah.

Which Slaves Are Valid for Kafarat-uz-Zihar?
Ruling with proof on valid slave for zihar expiation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for a valid slave in zihar expiation and identify which defects invalidate the expiation using the Hanafi proof from Quran 58:3.

Core Idea
Only a fully bonded slave with full benefit suffices for zihar expiation—partial freedom or loss of benefit invalidates.

This passage from the chapter of Zihar explains the conditions for a valid slave in kafarat-uz-zihar. Understanding these conditions is crucial because expiation must be complete; a defective slave fails to fulfill the Quranic requirement of 'raqabah'. The author presents the ruling with proof, listing specific invalid cases and the exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is freeing a slave to expiate zihar. The ruling is that only a complete slave (kamil ar-raq) suffices; defective or partially free slaves do not.
The ruling is derived from the absolute word 'raqabah' in the Quranic verse.
2
Locate the primary proof (dalil)
The proof is the Quranic verse 'fa tahriru raqabah' (Quran 58:3). This is a qat'i thubut (certain transmission) but zanni dalala (the meaning is open to interpretation).
The verse commands freeing a slave, but the Hanafis interpret 'raqabah' as requiring a full slave without any prior right to freedom.
3
Apply the Hanafi usul principle of mutlaq (absolute) text
The word 'raqabah' is absolute (mutlaq) and indicates a complete slave. Any defect that reduces full benefit (like loss of grip) or full bondage (like tadbir or istilad) violates this absoluteness.
Hanafis hold that an absolute term must be applied to its complete meaning unless there is a specified exception.
4
Identify the specific invalid cases and the exception
Invalid cases: (1) a slave with both thumbs cut (loss of benefit), (2) a permanently insane slave (no benefit), (3) a mudabbar (slave promised freedom after master's death), (4) an umm walad (slave mother of master's child). Exception: an intermittently insane slave, if freed during sanity, is valid.
The mudabbar and umm walad have partial freedom entitlement, making their bondage deficient.
5
Derive the operative ruling (mufta bihi)
A slave must be fully owned, free from any prior right to freedom, and capable of full benefit to be valid for zihar expiation. The Hanafi position is clear: only a complete slave suffices.
This ruling is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text

باب الظهار
ہے تو (اس کو آزاد کرنا ) کافی ہے کیونکہ اس میں جو خلل ہے وہ مانع نہیں ہے اور مدبر اور ام ولد کا آزاد کرنا کافی نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ وہ دونوں ایک جہت سے آزادی کے مستحق ہو گئے ہیں پس ان دونوں میں رقیت ناقص ہوگئی۔
تشریح مسئلہ، اگر کسی غلام یا باندی کے دونوں ہاتھ کے دونوں انگوٹھے کئے ہوئے ہوں، تو کفارہ ظہار میں اس کا آزاد کرنا جائز نہ ہوگا ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ دونوں ہاتھ کے دونوں انگوٹھوں کے کٹ جانے کی وجہ سے اس کی گرفت کی قوت زائل ہو گئی پس گرفت کی قوت زائل ہونے کی وجہ سے جنس منفعت ہی زائل ہوگئی اور سابق میں گزر چکا کہ جنس منفعت کا زائل ہونا مانع کفارہ ہے اس وجہ سے اس غلام یا باندی کا آزاد کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور وہ مجنون غلام یا باندی جس کو معقل نہ ہو اس کا آزاد کرنا بھی جائز نہیں ہو گا دلیل یہ ہے کہ اعضاء سے نفع اٹھانا بغیر عقل کے ممکن نہیں لہذا یہ بھی فائت المنفعت ہو گیا اور وہ غلام یا باندی جو کبھی مجنون ہو جاتا ہے اور کبھی اسکو افاقہ ہوتا ہے تو افاقہ کی حالت میں اگر اس کو آزاد کر دیا تو کفارہ ادا ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس میں جو خلل ہے وہ مانع کفارہ نہیں۔ اور مدبر اور ام ولد کو آزاد کرنا ادائے کفارہ میں کافی نہیں ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ قرآن میں تحریر رقبہ آیا ہے اور رقبہ مطلق ہے اور مطلق جب بولا جاتا ہے تو اس سے فرد کامل مراد ہوتا ہے اور مدبر اور ام ولد کا رقبہ کامل نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ مدبر تدبیر کی وجہ سے مستحق حریت ہے اور ام ولد استیلا د کی وجہ سے آزادی کی مستحق ہوگئی پس معلوم ہوا کہ ان دونوں میں رقیت کے معنے ناقص ہیں۔
Chapter of Zihar. (A slave with a defect) is sufficient because the defect in it is not an impediment. But freeing a mudabbar or umm walad is not sufficient because both have become entitled to freedom from one aspect, thus their bondage has become deficient. Explanation: If a slave or slave-girl has both thumbs cut off, then freeing them in the expiation of zihar is not permissible. The proof is that due to the cutting of both thumbs of both hands, the power of grip is lost. Since the power of grip is lost, the entire genus of benefit is lost. It has passed previously that the loss of the genus of benefit is an impediment for expiation. For this reason, freeing such a slave or slave-girl is not permissible. And freeing a mad slave or slave-girl who has no intellect is also not permissible. The proof is that benefiting from limbs is not possible without intellect, so this one also has lost benefit. A slave or slave-girl who sometimes becomes insane and sometimes recovers, if freed during recovery, the expiation will be fulfilled because the defect in that is not an impediment. And freeing a mudabbar and umm walad is not sufficient for fulfilling expiation. The proof is that in the Quran, 'tahriru raqabah' (freeing a neck) appears, and raqabah is absolute. When absolute is used, it means a complete individual. The raqabah of mudabbar and umm walad is not complete because the mudabbar is entitled to freedom due to tadbir, and the umm walad is entitled to freedom due to istilad (giving birth to master's child). Thus it became known that the meaning of bondage in both of them is deficient.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter of Zihar, explaining which slaves are invalid for expiation. The author first states that a slave with a minor defect is acceptable. However, freeing a mudabbar (a slave promised freedom upon master's death) or umm walad (a slave mother who bears her master's child) is not acceptable because they have already earned a right to freedom, making their bondage incomplete. The commentary then lists specific defective slaves: a slave with both thumbs cut off loses grip strength, thus the entire benefit of the slave is lost, as previously established, so expiation is not valid. A permanently mad slave cannot benefit from limbs, so also invalid. But an intermittently mad slave, if freed during sanity, is valid. The key proof for mudabbar and umm walad is the Quranic word 'raqabah', which is absolute, requiring a complete slave. These types have partial entitlement to freedom, so their raqabah is not complete. The ruling is that only a fully bonded slave (kamil ar-raq) with full benefit suffices for kafarat-uz-zihar.

Key Terms
رقبہ (raqabah): A slave in full bondage; a complete neck to be freed.
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who has been promised freedom upon the master's death by a declaration (tadbir).
ام ولد (umm walad): A slave girl who gives birth to her master's child, becoming free upon the master's death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following slaves is acceptable for kafarat-uz-zihar according to this passage?
A) A slave with both thumbs cut off
B) A permanently insane slave
C) A mudabbar
D) A slave who is occasionally insane, freed during sanity

Key Takeaway
For zihar expiation, only a fully bonded and fully beneficial slave (kamil ar-raq) suffices; incomplete bondage or loss of benefit invalidates.

Freeing a Mukatab Who Has Paid Part of His Kitaba for Zihar Expiation
Ruling on freeing a mukatab who paid part of his kitaba

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on freeing a part-paying mukatab for kafarat-uz-zihar, identify the intra-madhhab dispute, explain the key distinction from mudabbar and umm walad, and justify the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Freeing a mukatab who has paid some kitaba is invalid for expiation because compensation nullifies worship.

This passage addresses a specific question: if a person liable for zihar expiation frees a mukatab (a slave under a kitaba contract) who has already paid a portion of his kitaba, does this fulfill the expiation? The Hanafi school answers with a nuanced dispute that hinges on whether the mukatab's bondage is complete and whether the freeing involves compensation. Understanding this ruling requires distinguishing the mukatab from other part-free slaves like the mudabbar and umm walad.

Guided Path
1
State the Zahir al-Riwayah position
Identify the relied-upon ruling: freeing a mukatab who has paid some kitaba is not sufficient for kafarat-uz-zihar because the freeing is 'with compensation' (bi badal), which contradicts the pure worship nature of expiation.
This is the position of Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Zufar, and most later Hanafis.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Recognize the weak narration from Abu Hanifa (via Hasan ibn Ziyad) that it is valid. Understand the evidence: the hadith 'al-mukatabu abdu ma baqiya alayhi dirham' shows the slave is fully bonded until full payment.
This narration is not part of Zahir al-Riwayah and is considered marjuh.
3
Analyze the proof for the majority view
Examine why compensation invalidates the act: the mukatab's freedom is being purchased through his own payments, so the freeing is not a gratuitous act of worship but a transaction, which cannot substitute for the required pure 'raqabah'.
The majority's dalil is the principle that expiation requires an act of pure devotion (qurbah), not an exchange.
4
Contrast with mudabbar and umm walad
Understand why the ruling differs for a mudabbar or umm walad: their bondage is already deficient because their ownership is irrevocably restricted, while the mukatab's bondage is full and can be annulled (the kitaba can be rescinded by freeing).
This distinction confirms that the mukatab is still fully a slave in the eyes of the law, but the compensation aspect overrides.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Conclude that the Zahir al-Riwayah position prevails: freeing a mukatab who has paid part of his kitaba does not fulfill the expiation. The expiation remains due and must be performed with a completely owned slave.
The tarjih is supported by the majority of the Sahibayn and later authorities like al-Marghinani.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مکاتب کو کفارہ ظہار میں آزاد کرنا کافی نہیں
وكذا المكاتب الذي أدى بعض المال لأن اعتاقه يكون ببدل وعن ابي حنيفة يجزيه لقيام الرق من كل وجه
ولهذا تقبل الكتابة الانفساخ بخلاف امومية
الولد والتدبير لانها لا يحتملان الانفساخ
ترجمہ اور یہی حکم ہے اس مکاتب کا جس نے کچھ مال ادا کیا کیونکہ اس کا آزاد کرنا بدل کے ساتھ ہو جائے گا اور ابوحنیفہ سے روایت ہے کہ ایسے مکاتب کو آزاد کرنا کافی ہے اس لئے کہ رقیت من کل وجہ موجود ہے اور اسی وجہ سے کتابت مسخ ہونے کو قبول کر لیتی ہے برخلاف ام ولد اور مد بر ہونے کے کیونکہ یہ دونوں فسخ کا احتمال نہیں رکھتے ۔
تشریح مصنف نے فرمایا کہ وہ مکاتب جس نے کچھ بدل کتابت ادا کر دیا ہے کفارہ ظہار میں اس کا آزاد کرنا بھی کافی نہیں ہو گا دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس کا آزاد کرنا بالعوض ہوگا اور عوض قربت اور عبادت کے معنی کو باطل کر دیتا ہے یہی حکم ظاہر الروایتہ میں ہے اور اسی کے قائل امام زفر، امام شافعی اور امام مالک اور ایک روایت میں امام احمد ہیں ۔
اور حسن نے امام ابو حنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ کی ہے کہ ایسے مکاتب کا آزاد کرنا بھی کافی ہے دلیل یہ ہے کہ مکاتب جب تک پورا بدل کتابت ادا نہ کرے اس وقت تک وہ من کل وجہ رفیق اور غلام رہتا ہے۔ کیونکہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے المكاتب عبد مابقی علیه در هم یعنی مکاتب غلام ہی رہتا ہے جب تک اس پر ایک درہم بھی باقی ہے اور چونکہ مکاتب من کل وجہ رقیق ہے اسی وجہ سے کتابت فسخ ہونے کو قبول کر لیتی ہے۔ خواہ یہ نسخ کرنا کچھ بدل کتابت وصول کرنے سے پہلے ہو یا بعد میں ۔ اس کے برخلاف ام ولد ہونا اور مدبر ہونا ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ دونوں مسخ ہونے کا احتمال نہیں رکھتے ہیں۔ پس ان دونوں میں رقیت ناقص ہوئی اور پہلے گزر چکا کہ کفارہ ظہار میں ایسے رقبہ کا آزاد کرنا ضروری ہے جو کامل الرق ہو۔
Freeing a mukatab in the expiation of zihar is not sufficient. And likewise the mukatab who has paid some of the property, because his free becomes with a compensation. And from Abu Hanifa (it is narrated) that it suffices because bondage exists from every aspect. And for this reason the kitaba accepts annulment, unlike the umm walad and tadbir, because they do not bear annulment. Translation: And the same ruling is for the mukatab who has paid some property, because his freeing will be with compensation. And from Abu Hanifa there is a narration that freeing such a mukatab is sufficient because bondage exists from every aspect, and for this reason the kitaba accepts being annulled, contrary to being umm walad and mudabbar because these two do not bear annulment. Explanation: The author says that the mukatab who has paid some of the kitaba price, freeing him in kafarat-uz-zihar is also not sufficient. The proof is that his freeing is with compensation, and compensation invalidates the meaning of closeness and worship. This is the ruling in Zahir al-Riwayah, and Imam Zufar, Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and in one narration Imam Ahmad are of this view. And Hasan narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa that freeing such a mukatab is also sufficient. The proof is that as long as the mukatab has not paid the full kitaba price, he remains a slave from every aspect, because the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم said: 'The mukatab is a slave as long as a dirham remains upon him.' And since the mukatab is a slave from every aspect, for this reason the kitaba accepts annulment, whether this annulment is before or after receiving some of the kitaba price. Contrary to being umm walad and mudabbar, because these two do not bear annulment. Thus in these two the bondage is deficient, and it has passed previously that in kafarat-uz-zihar it is necessary to free a raqabah that is complete in bondage.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about freeing a mukatab (a slave under a manumission contract) who has already paid part of his kitaba (contract amount) as expiation for zihar. The relied-upon position (Zahir al-Riwayah) states that such a freeing is invalid because it involves compensation (the slave's payments are exchanged for freedom), which contradicts the nature of worship (ibadah) that must be purely for Allah. Therefore, Imam Zufar, al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad also hold this view. However, Imam Abu Hanifa has a narration through Hasan ibn Ziyad that it is valid. His proof is that the mukatab remains a full slave until he pays the entire kitaba, as the hadith says: 'The mukatab is a slave as long as a dirham remains upon him.' The key difference from a mudabbar or umm walad is that the mukatab's contract (kitaba) can be annulled (if freed, the contract dissolves), proving his full bondage. In contrast, tadbir and umm walad cannot be annulled, so their bondage is already deficient. The Hanafi school follows the ruling of Zahir al-Riwayah that it is not acceptable, though Abu Hanifa's view is recorded as a weak narration.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered into a contract (kitaba) to earn and pay his master a sum to become free.
کتابت (kitaba): The contract of manumission between master and slave, where the slave pays a fixed amount over time.
کفارہ ظہار (kafarat-uz-zihar): The expiation required when a husband declares his wife like his mother's back, which involves freeing a slave, fasting two months, or feeding 60 poor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zahir al-Riwayah, what is the ruling on freeing a mukatab who has paid part of his kitaba for kafarat-uz-zihar?
A) It is valid because he is still a slave.
B) It is invalid because the freeing involves compensation.
C) It is valid only if he has paid more than half.
D) It is invalid because he is like a mudabbar.

Key Takeaway
Freeing a mukatab who has paid part of his kitaba does not fulfill kafarat-uz-zihar because the compensation element negates the purity of the act of worship.

Freeing a Mukatab with No Payment: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Ruling on freeing a mukatab with no payment; Hanafi vs Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on freeing a mukatab who has not paid anything for kafarat-uz-zihar, identify the opposing view, and evaluate the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i analogy.

Core Idea
A mukatab who has paid nothing is fully a slave; his kitaba can be annulled, so freeing him fulfills zihar expiation.

This passage presents a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imams al-Shafi'i, Zufar, Malik, and Ahmad regarding the validity of freeing a mukatab who has not yet paid any portion of his kitaba as expiation for zihar. The Hanafi school relies on the hadith 'al-mukatabu abdu ma baqiya alayhi dirham' and the annullability of the kitaba contract to argue that the mukatab remains a full slave until full payment. The opposing school analogizes the mukatab to a mudabbar, who is also entitled to freedom, and thus holds such freeing invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The legal question: Is freeing a mukatab who has paid nothing sufficient for kafarat-uz-zihar?
The dispute hinges on the status of the mukatab's bondage.
2
State the Hanafi position and evidence
Hanafis: Valid. Evidence: (1) Hadith 'The mukatab is a slave as long as a dirham remains upon him.' (2) Kitaba contract can be annulled, unlike tadbir/istilad, so bondage is complete.
The hadith is a primary textual proof (dalil naqli).
3
Identify the opposing position and evidence
Shafi'i et al.: Invalid. Evidence: Qiyas to mudabbar – both have entitlement to freedom, so their bondage is incomplete.
The opposing school uses analogical reasoning (qiyas).
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafis refute the analogy: The mukatab's entitlement is conditional on payment; if unpaid, he is a full slave. Kitaba can be annulled, unlike tadbir. Thus, the analogy fails.
The key distinction is the revocability of the kitaba contract.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
Practical difference: Hanafis can free a non-paying mukatab for expiation; Shafi'is cannot. The Hanafi position is mufta bihi as per Zahir al-Riwayah.
This dispute has real implications for expiation practice.

فان اعتق مكاتبالم يُود شيئا جاز خلافا للشافعى له انه استحق الحرية بجهة الكتابة فاشبه المدبرولنا ان الرق قائم من كل وجه على مابينا ولقوله عليه السلام المكاتب عبد ما بقى عليه درهم والكتابة لا ينافيه فانه فك الحجر بمنزلة الاذن فى التجارة الاانه بعوض فيلزم من جانبه ولو كان مانعا ينفسخ بمقتضى الاعتاق اذهو يحتمله الا انه يسلم له الا كساب والا ولاد لان العتق فى المحل بجهة الكتابة اولان الفسخ ضرورى لا يظهر فى حق الولد والكسب
ترجمہ اور اگر ایسا مکاتب آزاد کیا جس نے کچھ مال کتابت ادا نہیں کیا ہے تو جائز ہے ( آمیں ) امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مکاتب کتابت کی وجہ سے آزادی کا مستحق ہو گیا ہے تو مد بر کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ( مکاتب میں ) مسن کل وجہ رقیت موجود ہے، چنانچہ ہم اس کو بیان کر چکے اور یہ دلیل کہ آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم کا فرمان ہے المكاتب عبد ما بقى عليه درهم اور کتابت آزادی کے منافی نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے کہ کتابت ممانعت کو دور کرنا ہے اذن فی التجارة کے مرتبہ میں مگر یہ کہ کتابت عوض کے ساتھ ہے۔ لہذا مولیٰ کی طرف سے لازم ہوگی اور اگر وہ (کفارہ میں آزاد کرنے سے مانع ہوتا، تو مقتضی اعتماق کی وجہ سے فسخ ہو جاتا۔ اس لئے کہ وہ نسخ کا احتمال رکھتا ہے۔ مگر یہ کہ کتابت کے لئے اس کی کمائی اور اسکی اولا د سپر د کی جائے گی کیونکہ آزادی ذات میں کتابت کی وجہ سے ہے، یا اس لئے فتح ضرورۃ ثابت ہے، کمائی اور اولاد کے حق میں ظاہر نہیں ہوگا۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مظاہر (ظہار کرنے والے) نے کفارہ ظہار میں ایسا مکاتب آزاد کیا جس نے ابھی تک بدل کتابت کا کوئی حصہ ادا نہیں کیا ہے تو ایسے مکاتب کا آزاد کرنا ہمارے نزدیک جائز ہے اور یہی ایک روایت امام محمد کی ہے اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ ایسے مکاتب کا آزاد کرنا کفارہ ظہار میں کافی نہیں ہوگا اور یہی قول ہے امام زفر اور امام مالک کا ، اور امام احمد سے بھی ایک روایت یہی ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ جس طرح مد بر جہت تدبیر سے مستحق آزادی ہو گیا ہے اس طرح مکاتب بھی کتابت کی جہت سے آزادی کا مستحق ہو گیا ہے، پس جس طرح اے احناف اتمہارے نزدیک کفارہ ظہار میں مدبر کا آزاد کرنا جائز نہیں اسی طرح مکاتب کا آزاد کرنا بھی جائز نہیں ہوگا۔
اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ مکاتب من کل وجہ رفیق اور غلام ہے چنانچہ ہم پہلے بیان کر چکے ہیں کہ کتابت فسح کو قبول کرتی ہے اور مکاتب اس وجہ سے بھی رقیق ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے المكاتب عبد ما بقى عليه درهم - بہر حال مکاتب جب من كل وجه رقیق ہے تو کفارہ ظہار میں اس کا آزاد کرنا بھی درست ہو گا۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر مکاتب نے کچھ بھی بدل کتابت ادا کر دیا ہے تو اس کو آزاد کرنے سے پہلے کفارہ ادا نہیں ہو گا۔
And if he frees a mukatab who has not paid anything, it is permissible, contrary to al-Shafi'i. His proof is that the mukatab has become entitled to freedom by virtue of kitaba, so he resembles the mudabbar. Our proof is that bondage exists from every aspect, as we have explained, and due to his statement عليه السلام: 'The mukatab is a slave as long as a dirham remains upon him.' And kitaba does not contradict that because it is the removal of restriction, like permission for trade, except that it is with compensation, so it becomes binding from the master's side. And if it were an impediment, it would be annulled by the consequence of freeing, because it bears annulment. However, his earnings and children are surrendered to him because the freeing in the substance is due to the kitaba, or because the annulment is necessary but does not appear in the right of the child and earnings. Translation: And if such a mukatab is freed who has not paid any property of kitaba, it is permissible. Imam al-Shafi'i has disagreement. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that the mukatab has become entitled to freedom by virtue of kitaba, so he resembles the mudabbar. Our proof is that (in the mukatab) bondage exists from every aspect, as we have explained, and this proof: the saying of the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم: 'The mukatab is a slave as long as a dirham remains upon him.' And kitaba is not contrary to freedom because kitaba is the removal of restriction, at the level of permission for trade, except that it is with compensation. So it becomes binding from the master's side. And if it were an impediment (to expiation), it would be annulled by the consequence of freeing, because it bears annulment. However, his earnings and children are surrendered for kitaba because the freeing in the substance is due to kitaba, or because the annulment is established by necessity and does not appear regarding the child and earnings. Explanation: The scenario is that if the muzzahir (the one who uttered zihar) freed a mukatab who has not yet paid any portion of the kitaba price in kafarat-uz-zihar, then freeing such a mukatab is permissible according to us, and this is also a narration of Imam Muhammad. Imam al-Shafi'i says that freeing such a mukatab will not be sufficient for kafarat-uz-zihar, and this is also the saying of Imam Zufar and Imam Malik, and from Imam Ahmad there is also one narration. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is that just as the mudabbar has become entitled to freedom due to tadbir, similarly the mukatab has become entitled to freedom due to kitaba. So just as according to you Hanafis, freeing a mudabbar in kafarat-uz-zihar is not permissible, similarly freeing a mukatab would also not be permissible. Our proof is that the mukatab is a slave from every aspect, as we have mentioned before that kitaba accepts annulment, and the mukatab is a slave also because the Prophet صلى الله عليه وسلم said: 'The mukatab is a slave as long as a dirham remains upon him.' In any case, when the mukatab is a slave from every aspect, then freeing him in kafarat-uz-zihar will also be correct. Contrary to this, if the mukatab has paid any portion of the kitaba price, then freeing him before that will not fulfill the expiation.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of freeing a mukatab who has not yet paid anything under his kitaba contract as expiation for zihar. The Hanafi position, narrated from Imam Muhammad, is that it is valid. The opposing schools – al-Shafi'i, Zufar, Malik, and Ahmad (one narration) – hold it invalid. The opponent's argument is qiyas (analogy): just as a mudabbar is entitled to freedom by tadbir and invalid for expiation, the mukatab is entitled to freedom by kitaba, so he should also be invalid. The Hanafi response is twofold: (1) The mukatab is a full slave (from every aspect) until he pays completely, as established by the hadith 'al-mukatabu abdu ma baqiya alayhi dirham'. (2) Unlike tadbir and istilad (which cannot be annulled), the kitaba contract can be annulled (if the master frees the slave, the kitaba dissolves). This shows the slave's bondage is complete and unaffected. Thus, the mukatab who has paid nothing is fully a slave, and freeing him fulfills the expiation. However, if he has paid anything, as previously stated, it is not valid due to the element of compensation.

Key Terms
مکاتب (mukatab): A slave with a kitaba contract who has not yet paid any portion.
تملك كتابت (tamalluk al-kitaba): The entitlement to freedom by virtue of the kitaba contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on freeing a mukatab who has not yet paid any of his kitaba for kafarat-uz-zihar?
A) It is invalid, like a mudabbar.
B) It is valid because he is fully a slave until payment.
C) It is valid only if he has paid more than half.
D) It is invalid because kitaba involves compensation.

Key Takeaway
A mukatab who has paid nothing is a full slave; therefore, freeing him for zihar expiation is valid in the Hanafi school.
