Validity of Kaffarah by Purchasing an Ascendant or Descendant
Inter-madhhab dispute on kaffarah purchase validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fulfilling kaffarah by purchasing one's father or son, and compare it to the Shafi'i position, identifying the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Buying your father or son with the intention of kaffarah is valid and fulfills the obligation — Hanafi position.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a clear inter-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the validity of kaffarah when purchasing an ascendant or descendant. The Hanafi school holds that such a purchase, done with the specific intention of fulfilling the expiation, is valid and discharges the obligation. Imam al-Shafi'i, along with Imam Malik, Imam Ahmad, and Imam Zufar, considers it invalid. The text defers the full proof to the chapter on oaths, but the ruling itself is clear.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute
Determine the exact issue: does purchasing one's father or son with the intention of kaffarah (zihar or oath) fulfill the obligation?
2
State the Hanafi position
Abu Hanifa rules that it is valid and the kaffarah is discharged.
This is the relied-upon view in the Hanafi school.
3
State the opposing position
Imam al-Shafi'i rules that it is not valid. The same view is held by Malik, Ahmad, and Zufar.
The Shafi'i school requires the slave freed to be a non-relative.
4
Note the scope of the dispute
The same difference applies to both kaffarah of zihar and kaffarah of an oath.
The text promises more details in Kitab al-Iman.
5
Consider the practical consequence
According to Hanafis, one can fulfill kaffarah by purchasing an ascendant/descendant; Shafi'is cannot and must seek another slave or alternative.
This is a real difference in practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم ۱۳۳
اگر باپ یا بیٹے کو خریدنے سے کفارہ کی نیت کی تو کفارہ ظہار جائز ہے
وان اشتری اباه اوابنه ينوى بالشراء الكفارة جازعنها وقال الشافعي لا يجوز وعلى هذا الخلاف كفارة اليمين والمسألة تاتيك فى كتاب الايمان ان شاء الله
ترجمہ اور اگر اپنے باپ یا اپنے بیٹے کو خریدا اور انحالیکہ خریدنے سے کفارہ کی نیت کرتا ہے تو یہ کفارہ ظہار سے جائز ہے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ نا جائز ہے اور اسی اختلاف پر کفارہ یمین ہے اور یہ مسئلہ کتاب الایمان میں ان شاء اللہ عنقریب آئے گا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی شخص پر کفارہ ظہار واجب ہو اور اس نے اپنے باپ یا اپنے بیٹے کو خریدا اور خریدتے وقت کفارہ کی نیت کی تو کفارہ ادا ہو جائے گا۔ یہ قول حضرت امام اعظم کا ہے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ کفارہ ظہار ادا نہیں ہوگا یہی قول امام مالک امام احمد اور امام زفر کا ہے اور اگر کفارہ یمین میں یہ بات پیش آئی تو اس میں بھی یہی اختلاف ہے جس کو ان شاء اللہ کتاب الایمان میں بیان کریں گے۔
Ashraf al-Bidaya, Urdu Sharh of Hidayah, Volume Five, 133. If he buys his father or his son with the intention of kaffarah by the purchase, then the kaffarah of zihar is valid. And he said: 'And if he buys his father or his son, intending by the purchase the kaffarah, it is valid for it. And al-Shafi'i said: it is not valid. And upon this difference is the kaffarah of the oath, and the question will come to you in the book of oaths, God willing.' Translation: And if he buys his father or his son and at the time of purchase he intends kaffarah, then this kaffarah of zihar is valid according to Abu Hanifa. And Imam Shafi'i said that it is not valid. And upon this same difference is the kaffarah of the oath. And this question will come soon in the book of oaths, God willing. Explanation: The issue is that if a person has an obligatory kaffarah of zihar and he buys his father or his son and intends kaffarah at the time of purchase, then the kaffarah will be fulfilled. This is the saying of Imam A'zam. And Imam Shafi'i said that the kaffarah of zihar will not be fulfilled. This is also the saying of Imam Malik, Imam Ahmad, and Imam Zufar. And if this situation occurs in the kaffarah of an oath, then there is the same difference of opinion, which will be explained in the book of oaths, God willing.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the validity of fulfilling kaffarah by purchasing one's ascendant or descendant. The matn from Hidayah states the Hanafi position: buying one's father or son with the specific intention of kaffarah (either for zihar or an oath) is valid and the kaffarah is discharged. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, holding it invalid. The Urdu commentary clarifies that this is the view of Abu Hanifa, while also mentioning that the same ruling applies for kaffarah of an oath, and that Imams Malik, Ahmad, and Zufar side with Shafi'i. No proof is provided here; the text refers to Kitab al-Iman for further details. The commentary does not give a tarjih, but the Hanafi position is presented as the primary ruling.

Key Terms
كفارة الظهار (kaffarat al-zihar): Expiation required for zihar (a form of divorce-like pronouncement) that includes either freeing a slave, fasting two months, or feeding sixty poor people.
كفارة اليمين (kaffarat al-yamin): Expiation for breaking an oath, which is feeding or clothing ten poor people, or freeing a slave; if unable, fasting three days.
شراء (shira'): Purchase; in this context, the act of buying a person (father or son) with the intention of using that purchase as the kaffarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, is it valid to fulfill the kaffarah of zihar by purchasing one's father with the intention of kaffarah?
A) Yes, it is valid.
B) No, it is invalid.
C) It is valid only if the father is a slave.
D) It is valid only for kaffarah of an oath, not zihar.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits fulfilling kaffarah (both zihar and oath) by purchasing one's ascendant or descendant with the specific intention of expiation, while the Shafi'i school does not.

Freeing Half of a Shared Slave with Guarantee for Kaffarah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on partial freeing with guarantee

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on freeing half of a shared slave with a guarantee for kaffarah, and explain the reasoning behind each position.

Core Idea
For Abu Hanifa, the defect in the partner's share invalidates the kaffarah; for the Sahibayn, the guarantee perfects ownership, making it valid.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of fulfilling a kaffarah obligation by freeing half of a jointly owned slave and guaranteeing the remaining half. The ruling hinges on whether the freer becomes full owner of a sound slave or inherits a defect that prevents the kaffarah from being accepted.

Guided Path
1
State the facts and the issue
Identify the scenario: a wealthy person frees half of a slave owned jointly with a partner, and guarantees to pay the partner for the other half. The issue is whether this frees the entire slave for kaffarah.
The freer must be wealthy; if poor, all agree it is invalid.
2
Identify the two positions
Abu Hanifa says it is not valid (la yajuz). The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is valid (yajuz).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
They argue that by guaranteeing, the freer takes full ownership of the slave through the guarantee. Therefore, he frees a slave that is entirely his own property, which satisfies the kaffarah requirement.
This reasoning is like the case where the freer is initially wealthy; if poor, the slave must earn (sa'ayah) and the freeing becomes for compensation, which invalidates kaffarah.
4
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa holds that emancipation is divisible (i'taq al-mutajarri). The partner's share was on defective ownership because half of a slave cannot be fully freed independently; when transferred via guarantee, the freer receives that same defective share. Freeing a defective slave does not fulfill kaffarah.
The defect is that the share was 'remaining' (baqi) with the partner in an incomplete state.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
According to Abu Hanifa, the kaffarah is not fulfilled and another slave must be freed. According to the Sahibayn, the kaffarah is fulfilled with this slave.
The practical consequence is whether the obligation is discharged or remains.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر موسر نے نصف مشترک غلام آزاد کر دیا اور باقی کی قیمت کا ضامن ہو گیا کفایت کرے گا یا نہیں ، اقوال فقہاء
فان اعتق نصف عبد مشترک و هوموسر وضمن قيمة باقيه لم يجز عند ابي حنيفة ويجوز معندهما لانه يملك نصيب صاحبه بالضمان فصار معتقاكل العبد عن الكفارة وهو ملكه بخلاف ما اذا كان المعتق معسرا لانه وجب عليه السعاية في نصيب الشريك فيكون اعتاقا بعوض ولابي حنيفة ان نصيب صاحبه ينتقص على ملكه ثم يتحول اليه بالضمان ومثله يمنع الكفارة
ترجمہ ۔ پس اگر اس نے مشترک غلام کے آدھے کو آزاد کیا حالانکہ یہ شخص مالدار ہے اور باقی غلام کی قیمت کا ضامن ہو گیا تو ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک جائز نہیں ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک جائز ہے کیونکہ وہ ضمان دے کر اپنے شریک کے حصہ کا مالک ہو گیا تو پورا غلام کفارہ سے آزاد کرنے والا ہوا۔ درانحالیکہ وہ غلام اس کی ملک میں ہے اس کے برخلاف اگر آزاد کرنے والا تنگدست ہو تو جائز نہیں اس لئے کہ غلام پر شریک کے حصہ کے لئے کمائی کر کے ادا کرنا واجب ہے تو یہ آزاد کرنا بعوض ہو جائے گا اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس کے شریک کا حصہ اس کی ملک پر ناقص رہ گیا پھر گھوم کر بذریعہ ضمانت کے آزاد کرنے والے کی ملک میں آیا اور ایسا ہونا کفارہ ظہار سے مانع ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جس شخص پر کفارہ ظہار واجب ہے اس نے ایسے غلام کا نصف آزاد کیا جو اس کے اور اس کے علاوہ دوسرے کے درمیان مشترک ہے درانحالیکہ یہ آزاد کرنے والا مالدار ہے اور یہ اپنے شریک کے لئے باقی غلام کی قیمت کا ضامن ہو گیا تو حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اس سے کفارہ ظہار ادا نہیں ہوگا اور صاحبین کے نزدیک ادا ہو جائے گا اور اگر آزاد کرنے والا تنگدست ہے تو بالا تفاق کفارہ ادا نہیں ہوگا۔
الظهار
اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم
دلائل بیان کرنے سے پہلے یہ واضح ہو جانا ضروری ہے کہ صاحبین کے نزدیک اعتقاق تجری کو قبول نہیں کرتا اور امام صاحب کے نزد یک اعتاق تجری کو قبول کرتا ہے یعنی اگر غلام کو تھوڑا تھوڑا آزاد کیا گیا تو امام صاحب کے نزدیک جتنا آزاد کیا ہے اتنا ہی آزاد ہوگا۔ لیکن صاحبین کے نزدیک اگر غلام کا نصف یا کم و بیش آزاد کیا ہے تو پورا غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ ان کے نزدیک بعض کو آزاد کر دینے سے کل آزاد ہو جاتا ہے۔
اس وضاحت کے بعد صاحبین کی دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ نصف غلام کو آزاد کرنے والا شخص اپنے شریک کو باقی نصف کا منمان دے کر اس کے حصہ کا بھی مالک ہو گیا پس یہ شخص کفارہ ظہار میں پورا غلام آزاد کرنے والا ہوا درانحالیکہ یہ غلام اس کی ملک میں ہے اور چونکہ پورا غلام آزاد کر دینے سے کفارہ ادا ہو جاتا ہے اس لئے اس صورت میں کفارہ ادا ہو جائے گا۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر آزاد کرنے والا تنگ دست ہے تو بالا تفاق کفارہ ادا نہیں ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں غلام پر واجب ہوگا کہ وہ کما کر دوسرے شریک کے حصہ کی قیمت ادا کرے پس یہ آزاد کرنا بعوض ہوا اگر چہ یہ عوض آزاد کرنے والے کو حاصل نہیں ہوا بلکہ اس کے شریک کو حاصل ہوا ہے۔ لیکن مقصود یہ ہے کہ غلام پر تحریر رقبتہ کے مقابلہ میں عوض واجب ہوا ہے۔ حالانکہ تحریر رقبتہ بلاعوض ہونا چاہیے تھا اس لئے اس صورت میں آزاد کرنا کفارہ میں کافی نہیں ہوگا۔
اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اعتناق متجری ( ٹکڑے ٹکڑے) ہوتاہے ہیں جس پر کفارہ واجب تھا جب اس نے اپنا حصہ آزاد کیا تو اس سے کفارہ ادا نہیں ہوا۔ کیونکہ نصف رقبہ رقبہ نہیں ہوتا اور ر ہا نصف آخر تو اس میں نقصان واقع ہو گیا ہے اس وجہ سے کہ اس میں رقیت کا باقی رکھنا محال ہے اور یہ نقصان اس کے شریک کی ملک میں واقع ہوا ہے پس جب آزاد کرنے والا ضمان دے کر اس نصف آخر کا مالک ہوا تو وہ اس ناقص کا مالک ہوا۔ پس یہ ایسا ہو گیا گویا اس نے کچھ کم پورا غلام آزاد کیا ہے اور ایسے غلام کا آزاد کرنا ادائے کفارہ کے لئے مانع ہے۔ اس وجہ سے کفارہ ادا نہیں ہو گا۔
If a wealthy person frees half of a shared slave and guarantees the value of the remaining half, will it suffice or not? Sayings of the jurists: So if he frees half of a shared slave while he is wealthy and guarantees the value of the remaining half, it is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa, but it is permissible according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) because he owns the share of his partner by the guarantee, so he becomes a freer of the entire slave for the kaffarah while the slave is his property, unlike if the freer is poor because earning for the partner's share becomes obligatory on the slave, so it is an emancipation for compensation. And for Abu Hanifa: the share of his partner remained defective on his ownership then transfers to him by the guarantee, and something like that prevents the kaffarah. Translation: ... (Urdu translation and explanation follow). Details: ... (Urdu commentary explaining positions and proofs).
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the validity of fulfilling kaffarah by freeing half of a jointly owned slave and guaranteeing the remaining half. The matn presents the ruling: Abu Hanifa says it is not valid, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is valid. The explanation clarifies that if the freer is wealthy and guarantees the remainder, he becomes full owner through the guarantee, so freeing the whole slave from his own property is valid according to the Sahibayn. Abu Hanifa argues that the partner's share was in a defective state (since half of a slave cannot be fully freed independently) and when transferred via guarantee, the freer owns a defective slave, which prevents kaffarah. The same dispute applies to kaffarah of an oath. If the freer is poor, all agree it is invalid because the slave must earn to pay the partner, making the freeing compensative.

Key Terms
اعتقاق متجری (i'taq al-mutajarri): The concept that emancipation is divisible or partial; a portion of a slave can be freed leaving the rest unfree.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee; assurance to pay the value of the remaining half of the slave to the partner.
سعایة (sa'ayah): Earning; the slave's obligation to work and pay for the partner's share if the freer is poor.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the key difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding freeing half of a shared slave with a guarantee?
A) Abu Hanifa says it is valid; Sahibayn say it is invalid.
B) Abu Hanifa says it is invalid because the transferred share was defective; Sahibayn say it is valid because the guarantee creates full ownership.
C) Both agree it is invalid if the freer is wealthy.
D) Abu Hanifa says it is valid only for kaffarah of an oath; Sahibayn say it is valid for any kaffarah.

Key Takeaway
The validity of freeing half a shared slave with a guarantee for kaffarah depends on whether the transferred share is considered defective or wholly acquired.

Freeing One's Slave in Two Stages for Kaffarah
Ruling on freeing one's own slave in stages for kaffarah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on freeing one's own slave in parts for kaffarah, explain the Sahibayn's objection, and apply the qiyas analogy of a sacrificial animal.

Core Idea
Freeing half of your own slave for kaffarah is valid; the deficiency does not prevent kaffarah.

This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether freeing one's own slave in two separate acts fulfills kaffarah. Abu Hanifa holds that it is valid because the deficiency (the half-free state) exists on the freer's own ownership, and such a deficiency does not nullify the act. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) argue that emancipation is indivisible, so freeing half automatically frees the whole, making a second act meaningless. The ruling hinges on whether partial emancipation is recognized.

Guided Path
1
1. Identify the act in question
A person frees half of his own slave for kaffarah, then later frees the remaining half for the same kaffarah. Determine whether this fulfills the obligation.
2
2. State Abu Hanifa's position and proof
Abu Hanifa rules it valid. His proof: the deficiency occurred on the freer's own ownership, which does not prevent kaffarah. He analogizes to a sacrificial animal that is injured before slaughter – the sacrifice remains valid.
The qiyas is based on the principle that a defect on one's own property does not invalidate a religious act unless the defect is on property shared with others.
3
3. Understand the Sahibayn's objection
The Sahibayn hold that emancipation is indivisible (ta'ziya). Therefore, freeing half of a slave is equivalent to freeing the whole slave immediately. The later freeing of the remaining half is meaningless – it is not a separate act of emancipation.
This objection is based on a different usul principle regarding the nature of emancipation.
4
4. Compare the qiyas analogy
Abu Hanifa's analogy: if a sacrificial sheep is accidentally injured (knife hits its eye) after being laid down, the sacrifice is still valid. Similarly, the half-free state is a 'defect' on the freer's own property that does not prevent kaffarah. The Sahibayn would reject this analogy because they see the half-free state as impossible – the slave is already fully free.
The dispute reduces to whether emancipation can be partial.
5
5. Identify the relied-upon position (mufta bihi)
The text presents Abu Hanifa's view as the correct one (al-asl). The Hanafi madhhab follows Abu Hanifa on this issue, so the ruling for fatwa is that freeing half then the rest is valid.
The authority weight is zahir riwayah from al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر اپنے نصف غلام کو کفارہ سے آزاد کیا پھر بقیہ نصف کو آزاد کیا کفایت کر جائے گا
وان اعتق نصف عبد عن كفارته ثم اعتق باقيه عنها جاز لانه اعتقه بكلامين والنقصان متمكن على ملكه بسبب الاعتاق بجهة الكفارة ومثله غير مانع كمن اضجع شاة للاضحية فاصاب السكين عينها بخلاف ما تقدم لان النقصان تمكن على ملك الشريك وهذا على اصل ابي حنيفة واما عندهما الاعتاق لا يتجزى فاعتاق النصف اعتاق الكل فلايكون اعتاقا بكلامين
ترجمہ اور اگر اپنا آدھا غلام آزاد کیا اپنے کفارہ میں پھر باقی کو بھی آزاد کیا تو جائز ہے کیونکہ اس نے غلام کو دو دفعہ کلام کر کے آزاد کیا ہے اور جو نقصان اس کی ملکیت میں پیدا ہو وہ کفارہ میں آزاد کرنے کی وجہ سے ہے اور ایسا نقصان مانع کفارہ نہیں ہے ( یہ ) اس شخص کے مانند ہے جس نے قربانی کے واسطے بکری کو پچھاڑا پھر بکری کی آنکھ میں چھری لگ گئی۔ برخلاف اس نقصان کے جو مسئلہ سابقہ میں گذرا کیونکہ وہ نقصان تو شریک کی ملک میں پیدا ہوا ہے اور یہ تقریر امام ابو حنیفہ کی اصل پر ہے اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اعتناق متجری ( ٹکڑے ٹکڑے ) نہیں ہوتا پس آدھا غلام آزاد کر نا کل کا آزاد کرنا ہے لہذا دو دفعہ کلام کر کے آزاد کرنا نہ ہوگا۔
And if he frees half of his slave for his kaffarah, then frees the rest for it, it is valid because he freed it with two statements, and the deficiency occurred on his own ownership due to the emancipation for the sake of kaffarah, and such deficiency is not a preventer, like one who lays down a sheep for sacrifice and the knife hits its eye, unlike what preceded because that deficiency occurred on the partner's ownership. This is on the principle of Abu Hanifa. And according to the two (Sahibayn), emancipation is not divisible, so freeing half is freeing the whole; therefore, it would not be freeing with two statements.
Source pages p. 125

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding freeing one's own slave in two stages for kaffarah. The matn states it is valid: the person frees half, then later frees the remaining half. According to Abu Hanifa, this is valid because the deficiency (the half-slave state) exists on his own ownership, and such a deficiency does not prevent kaffarah. The example given is of a sacrificial animal that is accidentally injured before slaughter; the sacrifice is still valid. This contrasts with the previous case where the deficiency occurred on the partner's ownership. According to the Sahibayn, freeing half immediately frees the entire slave because emancipation is indivisible; thus, freeing the remainder later is meaningless. The commentary aligns with Abu Hanifa's view as the madhhab's relied-upon position.

Key Terms
اعتناق متجری (i'taq al-mutajarri): Emancipation in parts; releasing a slave bit by bit.
اضجاع (idja'): Laying down an animal for sacrifice; used as analogy for a deficiency that does not nullify the act.
لا يتجزى (la yatajazza): Indivisible; not capable of being divided into parts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does Abu Hanifa consider freeing half of one's own slave for kaffarah valid?
A) Because the freer can take back the half-freed status.
B) Because the deficiency occurred on the freer's own ownership and does not prevent kaffarah.
C) Because the Sahibayn agree with him.
D) Because the slave approved the partial freedom.

Key Takeaway
Freeing one's own slave in two stages for kaffarah is valid according to Abu Hanifa, because a deficiency on one's own ownership does not impair the act, analogous to an injured sacrificial animal.

The Two-Month Expiatory Fast for Zihar
Explaining the ruling and conditions of the expiatory fast for zihar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for the valid performance of the expiatory fast for zihar and explain why Ramadan and the prohibited days are excluded.

Core Idea
The expiatory fast for zihar must be two consecutive months, free of Ramadan and days when fasting is prohibited.

Zihar is a prohibited form of divorce that requires expiation before the couple can resume relations. The primary expiation is freeing a slave; if that is not possible, the spouse must fast two consecutive months. This lesson examines the precise conditions of that fast: its mandatory consecutiveness and the exclusion of certain days. Understanding these conditions ensures the expiation is valid and complete.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
First, recognise that the act is the expiatory fast (kaffarah) for zihar when manumission is unavailable. The ruling is that it is wajib (obligatory) as a substitute.
The hukm is wajib, not fard, because it is a penalty, not an original obligation.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is Quran 58:4: 'But if he cannot find (a slave), then a fast of two months consecutive before they touch one another.' Identify this verse as the source of the ruling.
The verse explicitly commands fasting, and the word 'mutatabi'ayn' indicates consecutiveness.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyse how the verse proves the ruling: the imperative 'فصيام' indicates obligation (wujub), 'شهرين متتابعين' requires consecutive months, and 'من قبل أن يتماسا' demands the fast precede marital contact.
The phrase 'من قبل أن يتماسا' also implies that any interruption that allows contact (like breaking the fast) would nullify the consecutiveness.
4
Note the conditions and exceptions
From the hadith and reasoning, the fast must not include Ramadan (because it is a separate obligation) nor the five prohibited days: Eid al-Fitr, Eid al-Adha, and the three days of Tashriq (because fasting is forbidden on these days).
If these days occur within the two-month period, they do not count toward the fast and must be made up, but they break the consecutiveness unless they are unavoidable.
5
Explain the practical consequence
If the person begins fasting in the middle of a lunar month, they must fast 60 days. Interrupting the fast intentionally after 59 days requires restarting the entire 60 days.
This is because consecutiveness (tatābuʿ) is lost by any voluntary break.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الظهار
واذالم يجد المظاهر ما يعتق فكفا رته صوم شهرين متتابعين ليس فيهما شهر رمضان ولا يوم الفطر ولا يوم النحر ولا ايام التشريق اما التتابع فلانه منصوص عليه وشهر رمضان لا يقع عن الظهار لما فيه من ابطال ما اوجبه الله والصوم في هذه الايام منهى عنه فلا ينوب عن الواجب الكامل
ترجمہ اور اگر ظہار کرنے والے نے ایسی چیز نہ پائی جس کو آزاد کرے تو اس کا کفارہ پے در پے دو ماہ کے روزے ہیں جن میں ماہ رمضان نہ ہو اور یوم عید اور بقر عید اور تشریق نہ ہوں۔ پے درپے ہونا اس دلیل سے ہے کہ وہ صراحتا قرآن میں موجود ہے اور ربا ( درمیان میں ) رمضان کا مہینہ ( نہ ہونا ) تو اس وجہ سے ہے کہ رمضان کا روزہ کفارہ ظہار سے واقع نہیں ہوتا کیونکہ اس میں اس چیز کو مٹانا ہے جس کو اللہ نے واجب کیا ہے ، اور اب ایام میں روزے سے منع کیا گیا ہے، تو ان دنوں کا روزہ کفارہ ظہار کا نائب نہ ہوگا
جو کامل واجب ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر ظہار کرنے والا غلام آزاد نہ کر سکے بایں طور کہ غلام ہی دستیاب نہ ہو یا غلام تو دستیاب ہے مگر اس کو خریدنے کیلئے قیمت نہیں ہے تو ایسی صورت میں اس شخص کا کفارہ پے در پے دوماہ کے روزے ہیں بشرطیکہ ان دو ماہ کے دوران ماہ رمضان نہ ہو اور یوم عید اور یوم بقر عید اور اس کے بعد تین دن تشریق کے نہ ہوں دوماہ کے روزے اگر چاند کے حساب سے رکھتے ہیں تو بہر صورت جائز ہے خواه مبینہ ۳ دن کا ہو یا ۲۹ دن کا اور اگر در میان ماہ سے روز رکھنا شروع کیا ہے تو ساٹھ روزے پورا کرے اگر ۵۹ روزے رکھنے کے بعد افطار کر دیا تو اس شخص پر از سر نو ساٹھ روزے رکھنا ضروری ہوگا۔ تابع یعنی بلا انقطاع پے در پے تو روزہ رکھنا اس لئے ضروری ہے کہ قرآن پاک میں اس کی صراحت موجود ہے چنانچہ ارشاد ہے فمن لم يجد فصيام شهرين متتابعين من قبل ان يتماسا اور ماہ رمضان نہ ہونا اس لئے ضروری ہے کہ اگر رمضان میں ظہار کے روزے واقع ہوں تو اس چیز کو باطل کرنا لازم آئے گا جس کو اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرض کیا ہے اس وجہ سے رمضان میں جو بھی روزہ رکھا جائے گا وہ رمضان ہی کا شمار ہوگا نہ کہ واجب آخر کا ۔ اور صوم ظہار کے درمیان ایام نھی عنھا کا واقع نہ ہونا اس لئے ضروری ہے کہ ان پانچ دنوں میں روزہ رکھنے سے حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے منع فرمایا ہے چنانچہ ابن عباس رضی اللہ عنہما کی حدیث ہے۔ ان رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم قال ان لا تصوموا هذه الايام فانها ايام اكل وشرب و بعال یعنی رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ ان دنوں روزہ نہ رکھو اس لئے کہ یہ دن کھانے پینے اور جماع کرنے کے ہیں (طبرانی از معینی شرح ہدایہ ) پس ان دنوں میں روزہ کا کفارہ ظہار کا نائب نہ ہو گا جو کامل واجب ہے۔
Chapter of Zihar: And if the one who performs zihar does not find what to free, then his expiation is fasting two consecutive months in which there is no month of Ramadan, nor the day of Fitr, nor the day of Nahr, nor the days of Tashriq. As for consecutiveness, it is because it is textually stated. Ramadan does not count for zihar because it would entail nullifying what Allah has obligated. Fasting on these days is prohibited, so it does not substitute for the complete obligatory (expiation).
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage states the ruling for the expiation (kaffarah) of zihar when the person cannot free a slave. The expiation is fasting two consecutive months. The passage explains the conditions: the months must be consecutive, and they must not include Ramadan, Eid al-Fitr, Eid al-Adha, or the three days of Tashriq (11, 12, 13 of Dhul Hijjah). The proof for consecutiveness is the Quranic verse (Surah al-Mujadila 58:4): 'But if he cannot find (a slave), then a fast of two months consecutive before they touch one another.' Ramadan cannot be counted because it is already obligatory, and fasting on the prohibited days (Eid and Tashriq) is forbidden by hadith. If the person begins fasting in the middle of a lunar month, they must complete sixty days. If they break the fast after 59 days, they must restart all sixty. The passage also notes that the fast of Ramadan cannot serve as expiation because it would nullify the obligation of Ramadan.

Key Terms
ظهار (zihar): A pre-Islamic form of divorce where a husband says to his wife 'You are to me like the back of my mother', which in Islam requires expiation before resuming marital relations.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for violating a prohibition; here, freeing a slave or fasting two months or feeding sixty poor people.
تتابع (tatābuʿ): Consecutiveness; the fasts must be performed one after another without interruption.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which days are absolutely prohibited from being included in the two-month fast for zihar kaffarah?
A) Only Ramadan
B) Ramadan, Eid al-Fitr, Eid al-Adha, and the three days of Tashriq
C) Only Fridays and Saturdays
D) Any day that is a public holiday

Key Takeaway
The expiatory fast for zihar must be two consecutive months, avoiding Ramadan and five prohibited days, to be valid.

The Zihar Fast Dispute: Does Nighttime Intercourse Break Consecutiveness?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on restarting zihar fast after non-invalidating intercourse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf on restarting the zihar fast due to intercourse, and explain the scriptural basis for the relied-upon ruling.

Core Idea
Non-invalidating intercourse during zihar fasts triggers a dispute: Abu Yusuf spares restart, Abu Hanifa requires it.

This lesson examines a nuanced intra-Hanafi disagreement about the requirement to restart the two-month expiatory fast (kaffarah) for zihar when the husband has intercourse during the fast, but in a manner that does not break the fast (e.g., at night or due to forgetfulness). The Quranic condition 'min qabl an yatamassa' is interpreted differently by the eponymous imams. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to discern how textual conditions are read as cumulative rather than alternative, and how later practice selects the stronger view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
Recognize that the passage deals with intercourse during the two-month fast for zihar, where the act does NOT invalidate the fast (nighttime or forgetful daytime). The dispute is whether restarting (istiʾnāf) is wajib.
Invalidating intercourse (daytime intentional) is agreed to require restart.
2
State Abu Yusuf's position and proof
Abu Yusuf holds that consecutiveness (tatābuʿ) is the only condition; since the fasts themselves remain consecutive, no restart is needed. He also argues that requiring restart would delay all fasts after intercourse, which is worse.
3
State Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's position and proof
They hold two conditions: (1) fasts must precede intercourse, (2) the entire two-month period must be free of intercourse. Intercourse during that period negates the second condition, thus restart is required.
Their proof is the Quranic phrase 'min qabl an yatamassa' understood as requiring a total absence of contact.
4
Analyse the thamarah al-khilaf and tarjih
The practical difference: under Abu Yusuf, one may continue without restart; under the majority, one must start over. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is Abu Hanifa's view due to its textual strength and adoption in Zahir al-Riwayah.

امام ابو یوسف کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ جماع پے در پے ہونے کو نہیں روکتا۔ کیونکہ ایسی وطی سے روزہ نہیں ٹوٹتا اور شرط یہی تھی ( کہ پے رپے ہو ) اور اگر روزں کا وطی پر مقدم کرنا شرط تھا۔ تو جو صورت ہم نے اختیار کی ہے اس میں ( ولی پر ) تھوڑے روزے مقدم ہیں اور جو صورت تم نے بیان کی اس میں تمام روزے ولی سے موخر ہو جاتے ہیں۔
اور امام ابوحنیفہ اور امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ روزی میں (ایک) شرط یہ ہے کہ وہ وہلی سے پہلے ہوں اور (ایک) شرط یہ ہے کہ ولی سے خالی ہوں۔ ( یہ ) بالضرورت نص سے ثابت ہے ) اور یہ شرط ( روزوں کے درمیان ) وطی کرنے کی وجہ سے معدوم ہے اس لئے از سر تو روزے رکھے
Then if the one who performed zihar has intercourse with the woman during the two months at night intentionally or during the day forgetfully, he restarts the fast according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. Abu Yusuf said: He does not restart because it does not prevent consecutiveness, as intercourse does not invalidate the fast, and that is the condition. And if the condition is that the fast precede intercourse, then in what we (Abu Yusuf) hold, some fasts precede, while in what you hold, all fasts are delayed. And according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), the condition for the fast is that it be before intercourse and that it be empty of intercourse, necessarily by the text. This condition is negated by it, so he restarts.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether a person who has intercourse during the two-month expiatory fast for zihar must restart the fasts. The dispute concerns only those acts of intercourse that do NOT break the fast (e.g., at night intentionally, or daytime forgetfully). If the intercourse breaks the fast (e.g., daytime intentionally), then all agree that the fasts must be restarted due to loss of consecutiveness. Quran requires the fasts to be 'before they touch' (min qabl an yatamassa), which is interpreted as the entire two-month fast must be completed without any sexual contact. Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad hold that the condition is both that the fasts precede intercourse and that they are free from any intercourse. Since intercourse occurred during the two months, the condition is violated, so restarting is necessary. Abu Yusuf argues that the condition of consecutiveness does not require the fasts to be completely free from intercourse; rather, consecutiveness means the fasts are performed one after another without break. Since intercourse at night or forgetfully does not break the fast, it does not interrupt consecutiveness. He further points out that if restarting were required on their view, then all fasts would be delayed after intercourse, which is more harmful than allowing some fasts to precede intercourse as in his view. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: restarting is necessary.

Key Terms
استئناف (istiʾnāf): Restarting the two-month fast from the beginning because the condition of consecutiveness was broken.
تتابع (tatābuʿ): Consecutiveness of the fasts; required for zihar kaffarah and violated by any interruption, including intercourse that does not break the fast according to Abu Hanifa.
مسيس (masīs): Sexual contact (intercourse) between spouses; the Quran uses this term in the context of zihar.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi Hanafi position, what is the ruling on a man who has intercourse during the night while performing the two-month zihar kaffarah?
A) He does not need to restart because the fast was not broken.
B) He must restart the two-month fast from the beginning.
C) He must only repeat the day of the intercourse.
D) He can continue as long as he does not repeat the act.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the mufta bihi opinion requires restarting the two-month zihar fast if any intercourse occurs during the fast, even if it does not invalidate the fast.

The Effect of Non-Fast-Breaking Intercourse on Zihar Expiatory Fasts
Intra-Hanafi dispute on non-fasting-breaking intercourse

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on non-fast-breaking intercourse during zihar expiatory fasts and explain the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Even non-fasting-breaking intercourse with the wife of zihar invalidates the expiation; restart is wajib.

This passage examines a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute: does intercourse that does not break the fast (e.g., at night) disrupt the consecutiveness required for zihar expiatory fasts? Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad say yes, requiring a complete restart; Imam Abu Yusuf says no, because the fasts remain valid. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies the Hanafi school's strict interpretation of the Quranic condition in zihar expiation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
Pinpoint the act under dispute: a man performing zihar expiation by fasting two consecutive months has intercourse with his wife during that period, but the intercourse does not break the fast (e.g., at night or forgetfully during the day). Does this invalidate the expiation and require restart?
The dispute is specific to non-fasting-breaking intercourse with the wife of zihar; other scenarios may be by consensus.
2
State the two Hanafi positions
Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (majority): restart is wajib. Abu Yusuf: no restart needed; the fasts remain valid.
Al-Marghinani's Hidayah presents these as the two views, with the majority being the mufta bihi.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's proof
Abu Yusuf argues that since the fast is not broken, consecutiveness (tatabu') is preserved. The condition is only that the fasts be consecutive, not that they be free from all contact. He also points out that if restart were required, all fasts would be postponed after intercourse, whereas in his view some fasts precede intercourse, which is easier.
His proof relies on the principle that a condition not found in the text should not be added.
4
Analyze the majority's proof
The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) derive two conditions from the Quranic phrase 'before they touch each other': (1) fasts must precede intercourse, and (2) fasts must be free from intercourse. Non-breaking intercourse negates the second condition, nullifying the entire expiation, so restart is necessary.
They consider the second condition an implication of the first: precedence implies freedom.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and the mufta bihi
The practical consequence: if such intercourse occurs, the majority holds that the fasts are invalid and must be restarted (isti'naf); Abu Yusuf says they remain valid. The mufta bihi is the majority view, supported by later Hanafi authorities.
Also note that cross-madhhab, Malik and Ahmad agree with the majority; Shafi'i agrees with Abu Yusuf.

روزہ ولی سے خالی ہو اور شرط ثانی۔ شرط اول کے لوازم میں سے ہے۔ کیونکہ تقدیم صوم على الوطی، خلوصوم عن الوطی کو ستلزم ہے اور روزے رکھنے کے درمیان وطی کرنے کی وجہ سے شرط ثانی معدوم ہو جاتی ہے لہذا مشروط یعنی کفارہ بھی معدوم ہو جائے گا پس جب یہ کفارہ باطل ہو گیا تو ضروری ہے کہ از سر نو روزے رکھے اس لئے کہ اگر چہ یہ شخص قبل الوطی کفارہ ،الصیام ادا کرنے پر قادر نہیں مگر ایسے روزے رکھنے پر بالیقین قادر ہے جو وہی سے خالی ہوں۔ اور اگر اس نے ان دو ماہ میں سے ایک دن افطار کیا عذر کی وجہ سے یا بغیر عذر کے تو یہ شخص پھر از سر نو روزے رکھے گا۔ کیونکہ تابع اور پے در پے ہونا فوت ہو گیا ہے حالانکہ یہ شخص پے در پے روزے رکھنے پر قادر ہے۔ واضح ہو کہ اگر مظاہر نے دو ماہ کے پے در پے روزے رکھے پھر آخری دن میں پیشخص غلام آزاد کرنے پر قادر ہے۔ پس اگر غروب آفتاب سے پہلے پہلے قادر ہو گیا تو اس پر غلام آزاد کرنا واجب ہے اور اس کے روزے نفل ہو جائیں گے کیونکہ یہ شخص بدل کے ساتھ مقصود کو حاصل کرنے سے پہلے اصل پر قادر ہو گیا ہے اور اگر آخری دن میں آفتاب غروب ہونے کے بعد قادر ہوا تو روزے ہی کفارے میں شمار ہوں گے۔ غلام آزاد کر نالازم نہیں ہوگا۔
Chapter of Zihar. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on Hidayah Volume 5: [The fasts] must be before the touch [intercourse] and must be free from it, necessarily by the text. This condition is nullified by it, so he starts again. And if he breaks fasts one day with or without excuse, he starts again due to loss of consecutiveness while he is normally capable of it. Explanation: Then if within these two months he had intercourse with the woman from whom he made zihar (whether intentionally at night or forgetfully during the day), then according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, he starts the fasts anew, and Abu Yusuf said that starting anew is not necessary. The proof of Imam Abu Yusuf is that this intercourse does not prevent consecutiveness because such intercourse does not break the fast, and the condition was only consecutiveness. And if the condition was to precede the fasts before intercourse, then in the case we chose, some fasts precede intercourse, while in the case you mentioned, all fasts are postponed after intercourse. And the proof of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad is that in fasting there are two conditions: that they be before intercourse and that they be free from intercourse. This is established by the text by necessity. And this condition is nullified due to intercourse during the fasts, so he starts anew. And if he broke one of these two months with or without excuse, he starts anew due to loss of consecutiveness while he is normally capable of it. Explanation: The scenario is that if the one performing expiation for zihar by fasting has intercourse within these two months with the woman from whom he made zihar, whether intentionally at night or forgetfully during the day, then according to the two sides [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad] he starts anew, and this is also the view of Imam Malik and Imam Ahmad. Imam Abu Yusuf says there is no need to start anew, and this is also the view of Imam al-Shafi'i. In the text, intercourse is restricted to the woman with whom zihar was made because if he had intercourse with another woman, then if this intercourse breaks the fast, e.g., intentionally during the day, then due to interruption of consecutiveness, by consensus restart is obligatory; and if it does not break the fast, e.g., forgetfully during the day, then in that case consecutiveness is not interrupted, so by consensus restart is not obligatory. Similarly, if he had intercourse with the woman of zihar intentionally during the day, restart is obligatory by consensus. So it is known that the dispute concerns intercourse that does not break the fast. So Imam Abu Yusuf's proof is that intercourse at night intentionally or during the day forgetfully does not break the fast, so this intercourse does not prevent consecutiveness. In zihar expiation, consecutiveness of fasts was the condition, and it is found, so in this case restart is not necessary. 'And if it is required to precede' is an answer to a question. The question is: Preceding fasts over intercourse is a condition, and it is not found here, so the expiation should not be valid. The answer: No doubt preceding fasts over intercourse is necessary, but according to our school, some fasts precede intercourse, and according to your statement (i.e., in case of restart) all fasts would be postponed after intercourse, and the delay of some fasts is easier and more tolerable than the delay of all. And the proof of the two sides [Abu Hanifa and Muhammad] is that the text, i.e., 'before they touch each other', requires two conditions: one that the fasts be before intercourse, and second that the fasts be free from intercourse. The second condition is among the implications of the first, because preceding fasts over intercourse necessitates the fasts being free from intercourse. And by having intercourse during the fasting period, the second condition is nullified, so the conditioned, i.e., the expiation, is also nullified. So when this expiation becomes invalid, it is necessary to start anew, because although this person was not able to perform the expiation by fasting before intercourse, he is certainly able to perform fasts that are free from intercourse. And if he broke one of these two months with or without excuse, then this person starts anew because consecutiveness is lost while he is capable of consecutive fasts. It is clarified that if the muzahir [one who made zihar] performed two consecutive months of fasting, then on the last day he becomes capable of freeing a slave. So if he becomes capable before sunset, then freeing a slave becomes obligatory upon him, and his fasts become supererogatory, because this person became capable of the original [freeing] before obtaining the substitute [fasts]. And if he becomes capable after sunset on the last day, then the fasts are counted as expiation, and freeing a slave is not necessary.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of non-fast-breaking intercourse during the two-month expiatory fasts for zihar. The author first states the ruling: according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, any intercourse with the wife of zihar within the two months—whether intentional at night or forgetful during the day—invalidates the continuity and requires restarting the fasts from the beginning. Abu Yusuf, however, holds that restart is not necessary because such intercourse does not break the fast and therefore does not break the required consecutiveness. The text then provides the proofs: Abu Yusuf argues that since the fasts remain valid, consecutiveness is maintained; the condition is merely that the fasts be consecutive, not that they be free from non-breaking intercourse. Furthermore, if the condition were to precede intercourse, then in his view some fasts do precede, whereas requiring restart would postpone all fasts. The majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) argue that the Quranic condition 'before they touch each other' (Quran 58:3-4) implies two things: fasts must be before intercourse and free from it. Intercourse during the fasting period extinguishes the second condition, thus nullifying the entire expiation. The text also notes that if the muzahir becomes capable of freeing a slave on the last day of the fasts, the ruling shifts: if before sunset, he must free a slave and his fasts become nafil; if after sunset, the fasts suffice. This is because the original form of expiation (freeing a slave) becomes possible before the substitute (fasting) is fully performed. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: any non-breaking intercourse with the wife of zihar during the expiatory fasts nullifies the expiation and necessitates starting the fasts anew.

Key Terms
ظہار (zihar): A pre-Islamic practice of declaring one's wife like one's mother in unlawfulness, requiring expiation in Hanafi fiqh.
تتابع (tatabu'): Consecutiveness of the two-month fasts without interruption.
استیناف (isti'naf): Restarting the fasts from the beginning due to invalidation of the previous ones.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a person performing zihar expiation by fasting has intercourse with his wife at night (non-fasting time)?
A) The fasts remain valid; no restart needed.
B) The fasts are invalid; he must restart from the beginning.
C) He must free a slave immediately.
D) He must feed sixty poor people instead.

Key Takeaway
Even non-fasting-breaking intercourse with the wife of zihar nullifies the expiatory fasts; the mufta bihi requires restart (isti'naf).

Slave's Zihar Expiation Limited to Fasting
Ruling that a slave who makes zihar can only expiate by fasting, not by freeing or feeding.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the only valid expiation for a slave who performs zihar and explain why wealth-based options are impossible.

Core Idea
A slave's zihar expiation is limited to fasting because he possesses no legal ownership (milk).

This lesson addresses a specific ruling: a slave who commits zihar (declaring his wife like his mother) cannot expiate by freeing a slave or feeding the poor—acts requiring wealth. Instead, he must fast. The text explains that even if his owner attempts the wealth-based expiation on his behalf, it does not count. Understanding this ruling hinges on the Hanafi principle that a slave is not legally capable of ownership (ahlu al-milk).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is zihar performed by a slave. The ruling is that only fasting is valid for expiation; wealth-based options are invalid.
2
List the three expiation options
Recall the three kaffarah options: freeing a slave, fasting two consecutive months, or feeding sixty poor people. The text eliminates the first and third for a slave.
These are sequential: if one cannot do the first, then the next, etc.
3
Identify why wealth-based options are impossible
A slave has no legal ownership (milk) of property. Freeing a slave or feeding the poor requires ownership of wealth, which the slave lacks.
The Hanafi school holds that a slave is not ahl al-milk, so he cannot expiate with wealth.
4
Explain why the master's intervention fails
Even if the master frees a slave or feeds on his behalf, it does not suffice because the expiation is a personal obligation tied to the slave's own capacity. The master's act does not transfer ownership to the slave.
The text explicitly states this: 'he does not become an owner by being made an owner by the master.'
5
Conclude the mufta bihi position
The only valid expiation is fasting (two consecutive months). This is the operative ruling in the Hanafi school, with no intra-madhhab disagreement.
Other schools may allow the master to perform expiation, but Hanafi requires the slave to fast personally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان ظاهر العبد لم يجز فى الكفارة الا الصوم لانه لا ملك له فلم يكن من اهل التكفير بالمال وان اعتق المولى او اطعم عنه لم يجزه لانه ليس من اهل الملك فلا یصیر مالكابتملیكه
ترجمہ اور اگر غلام نے اپنی بیوی سے ظہار کیا تو (اس کو ) کفارہ میں ( کوئی چیز ) جائز نہیں سوائے روزہ رکھنے کے، کیونکہ غلام کی کچھ ملک نہیں ہے، تو مال سے کفارہ دینے کی لیاقت ہی نہیں رکھتا ہے اور اگر غلام کی طرف سے اس کے مولیٰ نے رقبہ آزاد کر دیا یا اس کی طرف سے کھانا دے دیا تو بھی کافی نہیں ہوگا اس لئے کہ یہ غلام مالک ہونے کا اہل نہیں ہے۔ لہذا مولی کے مالک کرنے سے مالک نہیں ہو گا۔ تشریح مسئلہ، اگر کسی غلام نے اپنی بیوی کے ساتھ ظہار کیا تو اس کا کفارہ صرف روزوں کے ذریعہ سے ادا ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ غلام کی ملک میں کوئی چیز نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ اسلئے وہ مال سے کفارہ ادا کرنے کا اہل نہیں ہوگا اور اگر اس کے مولیٰ نے اس کی طرف سے غلام آزاد کیا یا کھانا دید یا تو بھی کافی نہیں ہوگا۔ اسلئے کہ یہ غلام مالک ہونے کا اہل نہیں ہے۔ لہذا مولی کے مالک کرنے سے مالک نہیں ہوگا ۔
And if a slave makes zihar, only fasting is permissible in expiation, because he has no ownership, so he is not qualified to expiate with wealth. And if the master frees a slave or feeds [the poor] on his behalf, it does not suffice for him, because he is not qualified for ownership, so he does not become an owner by being made an owner by the master. Explanation: If a slave makes zihar to his wife, his expiation is only through fasting, because a slave does not own anything. Therefore, he is not qualified to expiate with wealth. And if his master frees a slave or feeds on his behalf, even that does not suffice, because this slave is not qualified for ownership, so he does not become an owner by the master's making him an owner.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This is a straightforward ruling: a slave who performs zihar (the pre-Islamic oath) upon his wife must expiate only by fasting for two consecutive months. He cannot use the other options—freeing a slave or feeding sixty poor people—because those involve wealth, and a slave is not a legal owner of property (mal). The text emphasizes that even if the master (mawla) attempts to perform the expiation on the slave's behalf by freeing a slave or feeding the poor, it is not valid. The reason is that the expiation is inherently linked to the person liable, and since the slave cannot own property, the master's act cannot transfer ownership to the slave. Thus, only fasting is permissible. The note from Fath al-Qadir adds that the master can forbid the slave from fasting for expiatory fasts except for zihar because the wife's right is attached to zihar expiation. This ruling is unique to the Hanafi school, which strictly limits a slave's capacity for wealth-based worship.

Key Terms
ظہار (zihar): The pre-Islamic practice of declaring one's wife like one's mother, requiring expiation.
ملک (milk): Legal ownership of property; a slave lacks this capacity entirely.
مولی (mawla): Master of the slave; the one who owns him.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is a slave who makes zihar limited to fasting for expiation?
A) Because fasting is the easiest option.
B) Because slaves cannot own property, so wealth-based expiation is impossible.
C) Because the master forbids other options.
D) Because fasting is the only option mentioned in the Quran.

Key Takeaway
A slave's zihar expiation must be fasting only, because his lack of ownership (milk) makes wealth-based expiation impossible, and even the master's intervention cannot substitute.

Multiple Kaffarat: Same Genus vs Different Genera and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Inter-madhhab dispute on multiple kaffarat with proof and analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on multiple kaffarat of the same and different genera, and evaluate the proofs of the Shafi'i and Zufar positions.

Core Idea
The genus of a kaffarah is tied to its cause; same cause permits assignment of a single act to any one.

This lesson examines a specific scenario from the chapter on Zihar: a person owes two expiations. According to the Hanafi school, the outcome depends critically on whether the expiations belong to the same genus (jins) or different genera. We will work through the Hanafi position, the dissenting views of Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Zufar, and the rational proofs (dalil aqli) that animate the dispute. Understanding this dispute sharpens our grasp of how intention (niyyah) and cause (sabab) interact in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Identify the two scenarios: (1) two zihar kaffarat (same genus), (2) zihar and qatl kaffarat (different genera). What does the Hanafi school rule in each case?
The key term is 'jins muttahid' vs 'jins mukhtalif'.
2
Identify the opponents and their views
The text mentions two opposing positions: Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Zufar. What does each hold regarding both scenarios?
Zufar disagrees in both; Shafi'i agrees in both but on different grounds.
3
Follow the opponents' proofs
Extract the proof (dalil) for each opponent. Shafi'i argues based on unity of purpose; Zufar argues based on the act being half for each.
Pay attention to the logic: Shafi'i focuses on maqsud (purpose), Zufar on the physical division.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds with the principle that within the same genus, specifying intention (niyyat al-ta'yin) is useless; between different genera, it is necessary. They support this with analogies from fasting (qada and nadhr).
The key proof phrase: 'ولنا أن نية التعيين في الجنس المتحد غير مفيد'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference between the three positions? If a person owes two zihar and one qatl expiations and frees one slave, which school says it works for one and which says it fails?
This step solidifies the real-world impact of the ikhtilaf.

ایک دن کی قضاء سے کافی ہوگا اور ثانی کی نظیر یہ ہے کہ جب اس پر قضاء اور نذر کا روزہ ہو تو اس میں تمیز دینا ضروری ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب تشریح عبادت میں مسئلہ کی دو صورتیں زیر بحث ہیں ایک یہ کہ ایک شخص یہ ہے کہ اس پر ایک ظہار کا کفارہ واجب ہے اور ایک قتل کا پھر اس نے ایک غلام آزاد کیا تو اس صورت میں دونوں کفاروں میں سے کوئی ادا نہیں ہوگا یہ حکم ہمارے نزدیک ہے اور امام زفر فر ماتے ہیں کہ دونوں صورتوں میں کسی ایک کی طرف سے ادا نہیں ہوگا اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ دونوں صورتوں میں اس کو اختیار ہے جس کے لئے چاہے قرار دیدے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ تمام کفارات کا مقصود ایک ہے یعنی ستر اور اس گناہ کے اثر کو زائل کرنا۔ لہذا تمام کفارات کی جنس بھی ایک ہے اور جنس واحد میں نیت غیر مفید ہے اس وجہ سے اصل کفارہ کی نیت باقی رہی اور یہ شخص اگر اصل کفارہ کی نیت کرتا تو اس کو ان دونوں کفاروں میں سے ایک کے لئے مقرر کرنے کا اختیار ہوتا پس ایسے ہی یہاں بھی دونوں کفاروں میں سے جس ایک کے لیے چاہے مقرر کر دے۔
اور امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس شخص نے دونوں کفاروں میں سے ہر ایک کی طرف سے آدھا غلام آزاد کیا ہے اور کفارے میں آدھا غلام آزاد کر نا صحیح نہیں ہے اس لئے یہ آزاد کر نا تبرع شمار ہوگا اور چونکہ دونوں کفاروں کی طرف سے آزاد کرنے کے بعد اس کے ہاتھ سے معاملہ بھی نکل گیا اس وجہ سے کسی ایک کے واسطے مقرر کرنے کا بھی اختیار نہیں ہوگا۔
اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ جنس واحد میں متعین کرنے کی نیت کرنا غیر مقید ہے لہذا نیت لغو ہوگی اور جب نیت لغو ہوگئی تو ایسا ہو گیا کردیا اس نے ظہار کے دو کفاروں میں ایک غلام آزاد اور دونوں کی طرف سے نیت نہیں کی ہے تو یہ جائز ہے اور اس کو اختیار ہے کہ دونوں ظہار میں سے جس کی طرف چاہے پھیر دے پس ایسے ہی یہاں بھی جائز ہوگا۔
اور اگر دو کفارے مختلف الا جناس ہیں تو ان میں متعین کرنے کی نیت مفید ہوتی ہے لہذا معتبر ہوگی۔ پس جب اس شخص نے کفار قبل اور کفارہ ظہار میں بالا رادہ ایک غلام آزاد کیا ہے تو یہ غلام کسی ایک طرف سے آزاد نہیں ہو گا۔ و اختلاف الجنس سے سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ قتل اور ظہار دونوں کا حکم ایک ہے۔ یعنی کفارہ بالا عتاق ۔ پس جب دونوں کا حکم ایک ہے تو یہ دونوں مختلف الا جناس کیسے ہوں گے ۔
جواب یہ ہے کہ حکم یعنی کفارے میں جنس کا مختلف ہونا سبب کے اختلاف سے ہے۔ اسلئے کہ قتل یقیناً ظہارت مختلف ہے اور اختلاف سبب دلالت کرتا ہے اختلاف حکم پر کیونکہ حکم ملزوم ہوتا ہے اور سبب لازم اور اختلاف لوازم دلالت کرتا ہے ملزومات کے اختلاف پر۔ پس دوسرے مسئلہ میں جب جنس مختلف ہو گئی تو اس کی نیت درست ہوئی اور جب نیت درست ہوئی تو ایک غلام آزاد کرنا مختلف دو کفاروں کی طرف سے ہوگا پس ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک کے لئے آدھا غلام ہوگا اور یہ جائز نہیں کیونکہ ایک کفارہ میں ایک غلام آزاد ہوتا ہے نہ کہ آدھا۔
Chapter of Zihar. ... Whoever owes two expiations of zihar and frees two slaves without intending each specifically, it is valid for both. Similarly, if he fasts four months or feeds one hundred and twenty miskeen, it is valid because the genus is one, so no specific intention is needed. Explanation: If he frees one slave or fasts two months for two zihar expiations, he may assign it to whichever he wishes. If he frees one slave for both a zihar and a qatl expiation, it does not suffice for either. Zufar said: It does not suffice for either in both cases. Al-Shafi'i said: He may assign it to whichever he wishes in both cases, because all expiations are of one genus by virtue of unity of purpose. Zufar's proof: He freed half a slave for each, and after freeing for both, he has no authority to assign it to one. Our proof: Within one genus, specifying intention is useless, so it is void; in different genera, it is useful. The difference in genus here in the ruling (i.e., the expiation) is due to the difference in cause. Analogy: first, if one fasts one day for two missed Ramadan days, it suffices for one day; second, if one owes both qada and nadhr fasts, distinction is necessary. Explanation of worship: Two scenarios: (1) Two zihar expiations, frees one slave or fasts two months: he may choose which one to apply it to. (2) One zihar and one qatl expiation, frees one slave: neither is fulfilled. This is our ruling. Zufar says neither case suffices for either. Al-Shafi'i says he may assign to either in both. Al-Shafi'i's proof: All expiations have the same purpose (concealment and removal of sin), so they are one genus. Zufar's proof: He freed half a slave for each, and after freeing, he loses control. Our proof: In one genus, specifying intention is unnecessary, thus void; in different genera, it is necessary. When there are two kaffarat of different genera, the intention becomes effective, so freeing one slave counts as half for each, which is invalid because each expiation requires a full slave.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on Al-Hidayah deals with the chapter on Zihar. It addresses the scenario where a person owes multiple expiations (kaffarat) and performs a single act of expiation (freeing one slave, fasting one month, etc.) without specifying which expiation it is for. The author presents the Hanafi position, then the opinions of Imam Zufar (within the Hanafi school) and Imam al-Shafi'i, along with their proofs. The core principle is that if the expiations are of the same genus (jins muttahid), such as two expiations for zihar, the single act can be assigned to any one of them at the person's discretion. If they are of different genera (jins mukhtalif), such as one for zihar and one for qatl (killing), the single act does not fulfill either. The Hanafi proof is that within the same genus, specifying intention is useless because the acts are identical in purpose and form; between different genera, intention is necessary because the causes (asbab) differ, making the expiations distinct. The Shafi'i position considers all expiations as one genus based on the unity of their purpose (satr and removal of sin). Zufar argues that freeing one slave for two expiations constitutes freeing half a slave for each, which is invalid, and after the act, the person has no control to assign it. The Hanafi response uses analogies from fasting: if someone owes two missed Ramadan fasts and fasts one day, it counts for one; but if they owe a missed fast and a vow fast, specification is needed. The passage emphasizes that the difference in cause (sabab) leads to a difference in the genus of the expiation, even if the form of expiation is the same (e.g., freeing a slave). The mufta bihi (relied-upon position) is the Hanafi view.

Key Terms
جنس متحد (jins muttahid): Genus that is one and the same, e.g., two kaffarat both arising from zihar.
جنس مختلف (jins mukhtalif): Different genera, e.g., kaffarah for zihar and kaffarah for qatl (murder).
نية التعيين (niyyat al-ta'yin): The intention to specify which particular expiation the act is for.
سبب (sabab): The cause that triggers the obligation of kaffarah, e.g., zihar, qatl, yamin.
مقصود (maqsud): The purpose or goal of the kaffarah, namely expiation of sin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person owes two kaffarat – one for zihar and one for qatl (murder) – and frees a single slave without specifying which kaffarah it is for, what is the ruling?
A) The slave counts for both kaffarat.
B) The slave counts for one of them at the person's choice.
C) The slave does not count for either kaffarah.
D) The slave counts only for the zihar kaffarah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between same-genus and different-genus kaffarat: same genus allows a single act to fulfill one at choice; different genera require specification due to differing causes.

Nikah — Marriage

Li‘an: Definition, Conditions, and Proof from the Qur’an
Defining li’an, its cause, conditions, and proof from Qur’an

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition, cause, and conditions of li‘an, identify its rukn (testimony emphasized by oath), and explain the Hanafi position on eligibility with proof from Surah al-Nur.

Core Idea
Li‘an substitutes for hadd punishment through four sworn testimonies, requiring both spouses to be qualified witnesses.

When a husband accuses his wife of adultery or denies the paternity of her child, a special procedure called li‘an replaces the usual punishment of flogging for false accusation. This procedure is based on the Qur’anic verses in Surah al-Nur. In this lesson, we examine the definition of li‘an, its cause, its essential elements, and the conditions that must be met for it to be valid.

Guided Path
1
Define li‘an linguistically and technically
Understand the lexical meaning (curse, expulsion) and the legal meaning (four testimonies with curse/wrath). Note that it is named li‘an because the curse is mentioned, as prayer is named ruku‘.
The name is taken from the part (curse) that pertains to the husband.
2
Identify the rukn, sabab, and initial condition
The rukn is shahada (testimony) emphasized by yamin (oath). The sabab is the husband's accusation that would incur hadd (qadhf) or denial of child's lineage. The condition for initiating li‘an is the existence of marriage.
The Qur'an explicitly says 'four testimonies by Allah', so the rukn is testimony, not oath alone.
3
Review the proof from Qur’an
Read Surah al-Nur 24:6-9. Note the words 'shahada' (testimony) and 'yamin' (oath). The verse makes the spouses witnesses when no others exist.
The text is qat‘i al-thubut but zanni al-dalala due to the interpretation of 'shahada'.
4
List the conditions for li‘an
Both spouses must be ahl al-shahada (qualified to testify); the wife must be muhsan (so that her accuser receives hadd); and the wife must demand li‘an because it is her right.
The wife's demand is a condition; if she does not demand, li‘an is not obligatory.
5
Analyze the Hanafi-Shafi‘i dispute
Hanafis require ahl al-shahada because the rukn is shahada. Shafi‘is require ahl al-yamin because they consider the oath primary. The practical difference: an unjust person (fasiq) can swear an oath but cannot testify, so Hanafis disqualify such a person from li‘an.
The Hanafi position is based on the explicit Qur'anic wording combining shahada and yamin.

واضح ہو کہ مرد کا اپنے بیوی کو تہمت لگانے کا موجب ابتداء اسلام میں حد قذف تھا۔ جس طرح اجتنبیہ عورت کو تہمت لگانے کا موجب حد قذف ہے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ باری تعالیٰ کا قول ھر بی ترجمہ عام ہے یعنی جو لوگ ( زناء ) کی تہمت لگائیں پاک دامن عورتوں کو اور پھر چاکر گواہ (اپنے دعوئی پر نہ لا سکیں تو ایسے لوگوں کو اسی درے لگاؤ اور ان کی کوئی گواہی کبھی قبول مت کرو یہ دنیا میں ان کی سزا ہوئی ) اور یہ
لوگ (آخرت میں بھی مستحق سزا ہیں کیونکہ ) فاسق ہیں۔ (تھانوی)
Chapter of Li‘an. Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu Sharh of Hidayah, Volume 5. The author (Sahib al-Hidayah) gave an example of the same genus and of different genera. So he said: the example of the same genus is that when someone fasted one day for two missed days of Ramadan, then the qada' of one day is valid. And the example of different genera is that when a person owes one missed fast and one vowed fast, then it is incumbent upon him to specify one so that distinction occurs between the two fasts. And Allah knows best what is correct. Jamil Ahmad, may Allah forgive him. Chapter of Li‘an. Translation: This chapter is on the rules of li‘an. Explanation: Li‘an is the masdar of mufa‘alah. Lexically it means to curse and to remove from mercy. In Shari‘ah, li‘an refers to the four testimonies, the curse, and the wrath that occur between husband and wife. The whole is named li‘an because the curse is mentioned in it, just as prayer is named ruku‘ because it contains ruku‘, and al-Tahiyyat is named tashahhud because it contains tashahhud. So naming it li‘an is of the type of naming the whole by the part. As for why it is named li‘an when wrath is also mentioned in it, the answer is that the curse comes from the husband's side and the wrath from the wife's side, and it is obvious that what pertains to the husband is given precedence, so in naming, precedence was given to la‘n over ghadab. The rukn (pillar) of li‘an is shahada (testimony) emphasized by yamin (oath), its sabab (cause) is the husband's accusation of his wife that would necessitate hadd on the accuser, its condition is the existence of marriage, and its ruling is the prohibition of intercourse and enjoyment immediately upon completion of li‘an. According to us, the person qualified for li‘an is one qualified for giving testimony, while according to Imam Shafi‘i, it is one qualified for swearing oaths. The cause of li‘an, definition of li‘an. He (al-Quduri) said: When a man accuses his wife of adultery, while both are qualified to give testimony, and the wife is one whose accuser would receive hadd, or he denies the lineage of her child, and she demands what is necessitated by the accusation, then the male must perform li‘an. The principle is that li‘an, according to us, consists of testimonies emphasized by oaths, accompanied by the curse, standing in place of the hadd of accusation in his right and in place of the hadd of adultery in her right, due to the saying of Allah Most High: 'And those who accuse their wives and have no witnesses except themselves…' (Qur'an 24:6). And exception is made from the same genus. And Allah Most High said: 'Then the testimony of one of him is four testimonies by Allah' (Qur'an 24:9); He explicitly mentioned testimony and oath. So we say the pillar is the testimony emphasized by the oath. Then He attached the pillar on his side to the curse if he is lying, and it stands in place of the hadd of accusation, and on her side to the wrath, and it stands in place of the hadd of adultery. When this is established, we say: both must be qualified to give testimony because the pillar therein is testimony. And she must be one whose accuser receives hadd because it stands in place of the hadd of accusation in his right, so she must be muhsan. And li‘an is obligatory due to denying the child because when he denies her child, he becomes an accuser of her outwardly, and the possibility that the child is from someone else through intercourse based on a doubtful contract is not considered, just as when a stranger denies the lineage of a known father. And this is because the original in lineage is the bed (of marriage). The valid and invalid are attached to it; so denying it from the valid bed is an accusation until what is attached to the valid becomes clear. And her demand is a condition because it is her right; so her demand is necessary like all other rights. Translation by al-Quduri: When a man accuses his wife of adultery while both are qualified to give testimony, and the wife is such that her accuser would receive the hadd, or he denies her child's lineage, and the wife demands what is necessitated by the accusation, then li‘an becomes obligatory upon the husband. And the principle is that li‘an, according to us, consists of testimonies emphasized by oaths, accompanied by the curse; they stand in place of the hadd of qadhf in his right and in place of the hadd of zina in her right. Because Allah Most High said: 'And those who accuse their wives…' i.e., people who find fault with their wives while they have no witnesses but themselves. And exception is made from the same genus. And Allah Most High said: 'So the testimony of one of them is four testimonies by Allah.' Allah Most High explicitly mentioned testimony and oath. So we say that the pillar is the testimony emphasized by oath. Then with this pillar Allah attached the curse on the husband's side if he is lying, and this stands in place of the hadd of qadhf; and on the wife's side He attached the wrath, and this stands in place of the hadd of zina. When this is established, we say: both husband and wife must be qualified for testimony because testimony is the pillar in li‘an. And it is necessary that the wife be such that her accuser receives hadd, because li‘an stands in place of hadd al-qadhf in the husband's right. So the wife's being muhsan is necessary. And li‘an also becomes obligatory by denying the child, because when he denies her child, outwardly he becomes her accuser, and the possibility that the child is from someone else due to intercourse by shubha is not considered, just as when a stranger denies lineage from a known father. And the non-consideration of this possibility is because the original in lineage is the sound bed, and the defective is attached to it. So denying lineage from the sound bed is an accusation, until what is attached to the sound bed becomes clear. And the wife's demand is a condition because li‘an is her right; therefore her demand is necessary, like all rights. Explanation: The scenario is that when a man accuses his wife of adultery, for example he says: 'You are an adulteress', or 'I saw you committing adultery', or he says 'O adulteress'. This is the madhhab of the majority, and Imam Shafi‘i, Imam Ahmad, and in one narration Imam Malik are of this view. And both husband and wife possess the capacity to perform testimony. And the wife is such that her accuser would receive hadd, or the husband denies the lineage of his wife's child, for example he says 'This child is from adultery' or 'This child is not mine', and the wife demands from her husband what is necessitated by the accusation, then li‘an becomes obligatory upon the husband. It should be clear that the cause for a man to be punished with hadd al-qadhf for accusing his wife originally existed in early Islam. Similarly, the cause for hadd al-qadhf is accusing a chaste woman. The proof is that the saying of Allah Most High is general: 'Those who accuse chaste women and then do not produce four witnesses, flog them with eighty lashes and never accept their testimony...' (Qur'an 24:4). And these people are sinful. (Thanawi)
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi madhhab on the topic of li‘an (mutual imprecation). The author, al-Quduri, states the core ruling: when a husband accuses his wife of adultery, or denies the lineage of her child, and the wife demands her right, then the husband must perform li‘an. The conditions are: (1) both spouses must be qualified to give testimony (ahl al-shahada), (2) the wife must be muhsan (i.e., free and chaste, so that her accuser receives the hadd of qadhf), and (3) the wife must demand li‘an because it is her right. The passage then explains the juristic nature of li‘an: it consists of four oaths by the husband invoking the curse of Allah if he is lying, and after that the wife also swears four oaths invoking the wrath of Allah if she is lying. This procedure substitutes for the prescribed punishment (hadd) that would otherwise apply: hadd al-qadhf for the husband if he were lying, and hadd al-zina for the wife if she were confessing. The proof is from Surah al-Nur (24:6-9). The Imam analyzes the wording: the verse explicitly mentions 'shahada' (testimony) and 'شهادات' (testimonies) and links them with 'yamin' (oath) by saying 'four testimonies by Allah'. So the pillar (rukn) of li‘an is the testimony emphasized by oath, not the oath alone. This leads to the condition that both must be ahl al-shahada. The passage also mentions the disagreement with Imam Shafi‘i, who holds that the qualified person is one who can take an oath (ahl al-yamin). The Hanafi view is that because the rukn is shahada, the capability to testify is required. This is a practical difference: a person who is not just (adil) might be disqualified from testifying but could still be allowed to swear an oath. According to the Hanafi school, such a person would not be eligible for li‘an. The passage also addresses the case of denying lineage (nafy al-nasab): this is treated as an accusation of adultery because the child is presumed to be from the marriage unless proven otherwise (the principle 'al-walad lil-firash'). Mere possibility of conception from shubha does not excuse the husband; the child is legally attributed to the husband until the contrary is proven. Finally, the wife's demand is a condition because li‘an is her right; she may choose to forgo it or pursue it. The commentary concludes by restating the causes and conditions clearly. The author notes that originally, accusing one's wife would have incurred hadd al-qadhf like any other person, but the special procedure of li‘an was revealed to avoid the punishment while still allowing the marital conflict to be resolved.

Key Terms
لعان (li‘an): Mutual imprecation between spouses; four oaths by the husband invoking the curse of Allah and four oaths by the wife invoking the wrath of Allah, substituting for hadd punishments in cases of spousal accusation of adultery.
قذف (qadhf): Accusing a chaste person of adultery or fornication, which is a sin and incurs the hadd punishment of eighty lashes unless proven with four witnesses.
شهادة (shahada): Testimony, the legal declaration of fact. In li‘an, it refers to the four sworn statements of the spouses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the primary pillar (rukn) of li‘an?
A) The oath (yamin) alone
B) The testimony (shahada) emphasized by the oath
C) The curse (la‘n) and the wrath (ghadab)
D) The demand of the wife

Key Takeaway
Li‘an is a wajib procedure that substitutes for hadd punishments when a husband accuses his wife of adultery or denies paternity, with the rukn being testimony emphasized by oath, requiring both spouses to be qualified witnesses.

Li'an in Hanafi Fiqh: Wajib When Conditions Met
Explains when li'an becomes wajib and its nature as testimonies strengthened by oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions that make li'an wajib and explain why the Hanafi school considers its pillar to be testimony (shahada) rather than oath (yamin).

Core Idea
Li'an is wajib when a husband accuses his wife of zina under specific conditions, and its pillar is testimony strengthened by oath.

In this lesson, we explore the Hanafi ruling on li'an (mutual imprecation). The passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies when li'an becomes obligatory on the husband and explains the school's distinctive view that li'an consists of testimonies (shahadat) strengthened by oaths and curses. This has practical implications for who can perform li'an and how it substitutes for hadd punishments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the triggering acts
Recognize that li'an becomes wajib when the husband accuses his wife of zina or denies paternity of her child. Both acts imply imputation of zina.
Denial of paternity is treated as an implicit accusation.
2
List the conditions of obligation
Extract the conditions: both spouses must be competent witnesses, the wife must be muhsana (free, adult, Muslim, chaste), and she must demand the hadd punishment for qadhf.
The wife's demand is a condition because li'an is her right.
3
Analyze the Hanafi view of li'an's nature
Understand that the Hanafi school considers the pillar (rukn) of li'an to be testimony (shahada), not oath. The Quranic verse uses the word 'shahada' four times, so each statement is a testimony strengthened by an oath.
This contrasts with the Shafi'i view that li'an is essentially an oath.
4
Trace the Quranic proof
Read Surah al-Nur 24:6-7 and note the repetition of 'shahada'. The verse shows that testimony is the foundation; the oath ('by Allah') is supportive, not the core.
The Hanafi usul principle: a word is given its literal meaning (haqiqah) unless a reason to deviate.
5
Consider the practical effect
Since li'an is based on testimony, only those competent to give testimony (free, Muslim, just, etc.) can perform it. This restricts li'an to 'adl (upright) spouses.
If either spouse is a fasiq (sinner), they are not qualified to testify, so li'an is not valid and hadd may apply.

یعنی جو لوگ اپنی بیویوں کو عیب لگا وہیں حالانکہ سوائے ان کی ذات کے ان کے واسطے گواہ نہیں ہیں اور استثناء اپنی جنس ہی سے ہوا کرتا ہے اور اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا پس ان میں سے ایک کی گواہی چار گواہیاں ہیں اللہ کی قسم کے ساتھ اللہ تعالیٰ نے) شہادت اور قسم کی صراحت فرمائی ہے پس ہم نے کہا کہ رکن وہی شہادت ہے جو قسم کے ساتھ مضبوط کی گئی ہے۔ پھر اس رکن کے ساتھ اللہ تعالی نے شوہر کی جانب میں لعنت ملائی اگر وہ جھوٹا ہو اور یہ حد قذف کے قائم مقام ہے اور عورت کی جانب میں غضب ملایا اور یہ حد زنا کے قائم مقام ہے جب یہ بات ثابت ہو چکی ، تو ہم کہتے ہیں کہ میاں ، بیوی دونوں کا شہادت کے لائق ہونا ضروری ہے کیونکہ شہادت تو لعان میں رکن ہے اور ضروری ہے کہ یہ عورت ایسی ہو جس کے تہمت لگانے والے کو حد ماری جاتی ہے کیونکہ یہ لعان شوہر کے حق میں حد قذف کے قائم مقام ہے۔ پس عورت کا محصنہ ہونا ضروری ہے اور بچہ کی نفی کرنے سے بھی لعان واجب ہوتا ہے کیونکہ جب اس نے اس کے بچہ کی نفی کی تو ظاہری طور پر وہ اس کو تہمت لگانے والا ہو گیا اور یہ احتمال معتبر نہیں کہ بچہ وطی بالشبہ کی وجہ سے اس کے غیر سے ہو۔ جیسے کسی اجنبی شخص نے اس بچہ کی نفی اس کے مشہور باپ سے کی ہو اور اس احتمال کا معتبر نہ ہونا اس لئے ہے کہ نسب میں اصل فراش صحیح ہے اور فاسد اس کے ساتھ لاحق ہے پس فراش صحیح سے نسب کی نفی کرنا تہمت لگانا ہے۔ یہاں تک کہ وہ ظاہر ہو جائے جو صحیح کے ساتھ لاحق ہے اور عورت کا مطالبہ کرنا شرط ہے۔ کیونکہ لعان عورت کا حق ہے۔ لہذا اس کا طلب کرنا ضروری ہے جیسا کہ تمام حقوق ۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جب مرد نے اپنی بیوی کو زنا کی تہمت لگائی مثلاً کہا تو زانیہ ہے۔ یا میں نے تجھ کو زنا کرتے ہوئے دیکھا یا کہا اے زانیہ۔ یہ جمہور کا مذہب ہے اور اسی کے قائل امام شافعی اور امام احمد اور ایک روایت میں امام مالک ہیں اور میاں بیوی دونوں ادائے شہادت کی لیاقت بھی رکھتے ہیں اور عورت ایسی ہے کہ اس کے تہمت لگانے والے کو حد ماری جاتی ہے یا شوہر نے اپنی بیوی کے بچہ کے نسب کی نفی کی مثلاً کہا کہ یہ بچہ زنا سے ہے یا کہا یہ بچہ میرا نہیں ہے اور عورت نے اپنے شوہر سے موجب قذف کا مطالبہ کیا تو شوہر پر لعان واجب ہوگا۔
