Chapter of Li'an. Sharh by Qaduri: When a man accuses his wife of zina while both are competent for testimony and the woman is such that the accuser would be liable to hadd, or he denies the lineage of her child, and the woman demands [the punishment of] qadhf, then li'an becomes wajib on the man. The basis in our view is that they are testimonies strengthened by oaths and joined with curses. They stand in place of hadd qadhf for the man and hadd zina for the woman. Because Allah said: "And those who accuse their wives and have no witnesses except themselves..." So we said: the pillar is testimony strengthened by oath. Then Allah joined curse for the husband if he is lying and wrath for the wife if he is truthful. It is necessary that both spouses be fit for testimony, and that the woman be muhsana, because li'an is substitute for hadd qadhf. Denial of paternity also necessitates li'an. The woman's demand is a condition. Explanation: When a man says "you are adulteress" etc., this is the madhhab of the majority, Imam Shafi'i, Imam Ahmad, and in one narration, Imam Malik. The man and woman must be capable of testimony, and the woman must be muhsana. If the husband denies the child's lineage, li'an is wajib. It should be clear that the original cause for such accusation was hadd qadhf in early Islam, as Allah says: "And those who accuse chaste women and then do not produce four witnesses..." This verse indicates the original ruling.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah discusses the ruling and conditions of li'an (mutual imprecation) in Hanafi fiqh. It begins by stating the scenario that obligates li'an: a husband accuses his wife of zina or denies paternity while both are competent witnesses and the woman is muhsana (chaste and free), and the wife demands the hadd punishment for qadhf. The author explains the Hanafi position that li'an is fundamentally testimonies (shahadat) that are strengthened by oaths (ayman) and connected with curses (la'n) and wrath (ghadab). For the husband, li'an substitutes for the hadd of qadhf; for the wife, it substitutes for the hadd of zina. The proof is the Quranic verse in Surah al-Nur (24:6-7) where Allah uses the word 'shahada' and mentions oaths. Since the verse uses 'shahada', Hanafis conclude that the pillar (rukn) of li'an is testimony, not mere oath. This has practical implications: only those who are competent to give testimony (i.e., free, adult, Muslim, just, etc.) can perform li'an. The woman must be muhsana because li'an replaces hadd qadhf for the husband, and hadd qadhf only applies when accusing a muhsana woman. Denial of paternity is equivalent to accusation because it implies the child is from zina, even if there is a possibility of wati' bi al-shubha. The principle is that the valid marriage bed (firash sahih) is the basis of lineage; a defective (fasid) bed is attached to it, so denying lineage from the sahih bed is effectively an accusation. The woman's demand is a condition because li'an is her right; without her demand, the husband is not obliged. The passage also notes that the original ruling in early Islam was hadd qadhf for such accusations, but the verses of li'an abrogated that for spouses. The passage ends by quoting the verse on qadhf (Surah al-Nur: 4) to highlight the original law.

Key Terms
لعان (li'an): Mutual imprecation between spouses where they exchange testimonies strengthened by oaths and curses, replacing hadd punishments.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina against a chaste person, punishable by hadd (80 lashes).
محصنۃ (muhsana): A free, adult, Muslim, chaste woman who has not committed zina.
شہادت (shahada): Testimony, which is the pillar (rukn) of li'an in Hanafi view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The husband must be wealthy and able to pay a fine.
B) The wife must be a virgin at the time of marriage.
C) The wife must demand the hadd punishment for qadhf.
D) The accusation must be made in the presence of a judge.

Key Takeaway
Li'an is a special procedure in Hanafi fiqh where testimonies strengthened by oaths replace hadd punishments, and it becomes wajib only under specific conditions including the wife's demand.

The Nature of Li'an: Testimony or Oath?
Uses hadith and Quran to prove abrogation and dispute the nature of li'an.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that li'an is fundamentally testimony (shahada) and contrast it with the Shafi'i view that it is an oath (yamin), identifying the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) regarding who qualifies to perform li'an.

Core Idea
Li'an is testimony strengthened by oaths — its form determines who can perform it.

The revelation of the li'an verses provided a unique solution for a husband who accuses his wife of zina without witnesses. But what is the legal nature of this procedure? Is it a series of testimonies or a set of oaths? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on this foundational question and shows how the answer changes who may perform li'an.

Guided Path
1
Understand the historical context
Read the two hadiths that show the dilemma before li'an: the Ansari's complaint and the story of Hilal ibn Umayyah. Note that the original ruling was hadd qadhf, which was abrogated for spouses.
The hadiths establish the sabab al-nuzul and the naskh.
2
Identify the two positions
State the Hanafi view: li'an is testimonies (shahadat) strengthened by oaths. State the Shafi'i view: li'an is oaths (ayman) strengthened by the word testimony.
Focus on the essence, not the details.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof from the Quran
Analyze the verse (Surah al-Nur 24:6-10). The key point is the word 'shahada' repeated four times, and the exception 'except themselves' (illa anfusahum) which proves the husband is a witness.
Use the principle of istithna': the excepted item must be of the same category.
4
Examine the Shafi'i proof and the Hanafi response
The Shafi'i argue from the phrase 'billahi' (by Allah), indicating oath. The Hanafi response: the word 'shahada' is explicit; 'billahi' merely strengthens the testimony.
Consider the usul principle: a clear word (nass) cannot be overridden by implication.
5
Determine the practical consequence
The thamarah: if li'an is shahada, only those qualified for testimony (adl, free, etc.) can perform it. If it is yamin, even a fasiq can perform it.
This is the operative difference in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب اللعان
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ جلد پنجم به
اور عبد اللہ بن مسعودؓ سے روایت ہے قال كنا جلو سافی المسجد ليلة الجمعة اذ دخل انصاری فقال يا رسول الله ارايتم الرجل يجد مع امراته رجلاً فان قتل قتلتموه وان تكلم جلد تموه و ان سكت، سكت على غيظ ثم قال اللهم أفتح فنزلت آية اللعان یعنی فرمایا ابن مسعودؓ نے کہ ہم شب جمعہ میں مسجد میں بیٹھے ہوئے تھے۔ اچانک ایک انصاری آیا اور کہنے لگا کہ اے اللہ کے رسول آپ کی کیا رائے ہے کہ ایک شخص اپنی بیوی کے ساتھ ایک (اجنبی ) آدمی کو پاتا ہے اگر وہ اس کو قتل کر دے تو آپ حضرات اس کو قتل کر دیں گے اور اگر وہ کچھ بولے آپ حضرات اس کو کوڑے لگاتے ہیں اور اگر وہ خاموش رہے تو اس کو خون کے گھونٹ پینے پڑتے ہیں ۔ پھر اس نے کہا ۔ ائے میرے خدا تو (اس معاملہ ) کوکھول دے۔ پس آیت لعان نازل ہوئی۔ اور ایک مرتبہ حضور صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ہلال بن امیہ سے کہا جب کہ اس نے اپنی بیوی کو شریک بن شما ء کے ساتھ زنا کی تہمت لگادی تھی تم اپنی بات کی صداقت پر چار گواہ پیش کرو۔ ورنہ تمھاری پیٹھ پر کوڑے مارے جائیں گے ۔ صحابہ نے کہا کہ اب ہلال بن امیہ کوکوڑے مارے جائیں گے اور اس کی شہادت مسلمانوں میں باطل ہو جائے گی۔ (عنایه )
اس آیت اور دونوں روایت سے ثابت ہو گیا کہ موجب قذف حد قذف تھی مگر آیت لعان سے یہ حکم منسوخ ہو گیا ۔ پھر ہم نے آیت لعان میں غور کیا تو معلوم ہوا کہ ہمارے نزدیک لعان میں اصل یہ ہے کہ گواہیاں قسموں کے ساتھ مؤکد کی گئیں ہوں اور لفظ لعن کے ساتھ مقترن ہوں اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک لعان وہ قسمیں ہیں جو لفظ شہادت کے ساتھ موکد ہوں ۔ پس ہمارے نزدیک لعان کا اہل وہ شخص ہوگا ، جو شہادت کا اہل ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک لعان کا وہ اہل ہے جو یمین کا اہل ہے۔ خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ لعان شو ہر کے حق میں حد قذف کے قائم مقام ہے۔ اس کی بیوی کے حق میں حد زنا کے قائم مقام ہے۔
دلیل یہ ہے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے کہ والذين يرمون ازواجهم ولم يكن لهم شهداء الا نفسهم فشهادة احدهم اربع شهادات بالله انه لمن الصادقين والخامسة ان لعنت الله عليه ان كان من الكذبين ويدرؤ اعنها العذاب ان تشهد أربع
شهادات بالله انه لمن الكذبين والخامسة ان غضب الله عليها ان كان من الصادقين - یعنی جو لوگ اپنی (منکوحہ بیویوں کو ( زنا) کی تہمت لگائیں اور ان کے پاس بجز اپنے دعوی کے اور کوئی گواہ نہ ہوں ۔ ( جن کو عدد میں چار ہونا چاہیے ) تو ان کی شہادت (جو کہ دافع جبس یا حد قذف ہو ) یہی ہے کہ چار بار اللہ کی قسم کھا کر کہہ دے کہ بے شک میں سچا ہوں اور پانچویں بار یہ کہے کہ مجھ پر خدا کی لعنت ہو اگر میں جھوٹا ہوں اور اس کے بعد اس عورت سے پیز ائے جبس یا حد زنا) اس طرح مل سکتی ہے کہ وہ چار بار تم کھا کر کہے کہ بے شک یہ مرد جھوٹا ہے اور پانچویں بار یہ کہے کہ مجھ پر خدا کا غضب ہوا گر
یہ سچا ہو۔ (بیان القرآن ) اس آیت سے استدلال اس طرح ہوگا کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے شہداء سے ازواج کا استثناء فرمایا ہے پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ زوج شاہد ہے اس لئے استثناء میں اصل یہ ہے کہ مستی مستثنی منہ کا ہم جنس ہوتا ہے۔ حاصل یہ کہ زوج شاہد ہے اور شاہد بغیر شہادت کے نہیں ہو سکتا اور اس
مسئلہ میں شہادت نام ہے حکایت لعان کا ۔ پس ثابت ہو گیا کہ لعان وہ شہادتیں ہیں جو قسموں کے ساتھ مضبوط کی گئیں ہیں ۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک لعان و قسمیں ہیں جو لفظ شہادت کیسا تھ موکد کی گئی ہوں دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا قول فشهادة احدهم اربع
Chapter of Li'an. And from Abdullah ibn Mas'ud (RA) a narration: He said, 'We were sitting in the mosque on Friday night when an Ansari man entered and said: O Messenger of Allah, what do you think if a man finds another man with his wife? If he kills him, you kill him; if he speaks, you flog him; and if he remains silent, he drinks the cup of anger. Then he said: O Allah, open [a solution]. So the verse of li'an was revealed.' And one time the Prophet (SAW) said to Hilal ibn Umayyah when he accused his wife of zina with Sharik ibn Sahma': 'Bring four witnesses to prove your claim, or else your back will be flogged.' The Companions said: 'Now Hilal ibn Umayyah will be flogged and his testimony among Muslims will be invalidated.' (From Inayah) From this verse and these two narrations it is established that the original cause was hadd qadhf, but this ruling was abrogated by the verse of li'an. Then when we examined the verse of li'an, we found that in our view the basis is that testimonies are strengthened by oaths and joined with the word curse, and in Imam Shafi'i's view, li'an are oaths strengthened by the word testimony. So in our view, the one qualified for li'an is he who is qualified for testimony; in Imam Shafi'i's view, the one qualified is he who is qualified for oath. In summary, li'an substitutes for hadd qadhf for the husband and hadd zina for the wife. The proof is that Allah said: 'And those who accuse their wives and have no witnesses but themselves...' (until the end of the verse). From this verse, the deduction is that Allah made an exception of spouses from (the requirement of) witnesses, so it is established that the husband is a witness. Therefore, since the word 'shahada' is used, it proves that li'an is testimonies strengthened by oaths. Imam Shafi'i holds that they are oaths strengthened by the word testimony, based on the word 'shahada' in the verse.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah presents the historical background and the inter-madhhab dispute regarding the nature of li'an. It begins with two hadiths: the narration of Ibn Mas'ud about an Ansari man, and the story of Hilal ibn Umayyah. Both hadiths illustrate the dilemma before the revelation of the li'an verses: a husband who sees his wife committing zina had no recourse other than to kill, speak (which subjects him to hadd qadhf if he cannot produce four witnesses), or remain silent. The Prophet's supplication led to the revelation of the li'an verses (Surah al-Nur: 6-10), which provided a special procedure for spouses. These narrations prove that the original ruling for a false accusation was hadd qadhf, but the li'an verses abrogated (naskh) that ruling specifically for spouses. The author then explains the Hanafi position: the essence of li'an is shahada (testimony), because the Quran calls each statement a 'shahada' and says 'fashahadatu ahadihim arba'u shahadatin'. The oaths (ayman) and curses are attached to strengthen the testimonies. Therefore, the qualification for li'an is the same as for testimony: the person must be just (adil), free, Muslim, etc. In contrast, Imam al-Shafi'i holds that li'an is fundamentally yamin (oath) because the phrases include 'billahi' (by Allah), and the word 'shahada' is used in a broader sense of affirmation. For Shafi'is, the qualification for li'an is the same as for taking an oath, which does not require being just. The practical consequence (thamaratu al-khilaf) is that if a sinful (fasiq) husband who is not qualified to testify accuses his wife, the Hanafi school would not allow him to perform li'an, while the Shafi'i school might allow it because he is still qualified to take an oath. The author provides the Hanafi proof by quoting the full li'an verses and analyzing the exception: Allah says 'except themselves', making the husband a witness. Since a witness gives testimony, li'an must be testimony. The passage ends with the Shafi'i position, stating their proof also relies on the word 'shahada' in the verse, but they interpret it differently.

Key Terms
لعان (li'an): Mutual imprecation procedure between spouses that replaces hadd punishments.
شہادت (shahada): Testimony in the legal sense, requiring competence (adalah).
یمین (yamin): An oath sworn by Allah.
نسخ (naskh): Abrogation of a ruling by a later revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the practical difference between considering li'an as shahada versus yamin?
A) No practical difference
B) A fasiq (sinner) can perform li'an as shahada but not as yamin
C) A fasiq can perform li'an as yamin but not as shahada
D) Li'an is invalid altogether

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that li'an is fundamentally testimony (shahada) strengthened by oaths, so only those qualified to testify can perform it; the Shafi'i view that it is an oath would allow even a fasiq to perform li'an.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Li'an: Definition, Conditions, and the Inter-Madhhab Dispute on Refusal Consequences
Explains li'an as testimony with oaths, conditions, and the inter-madhhab dispute on the consequence of refusal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of li'an, identify its conditions, and explain the Hanafi position on the husband's refusal as opposed to the Shafi'i/Maliki/Hanbali view.

Core Idea
Li'an replaces hadd; the husband is imprisoned until he performs it or retracts — not flogged.

Li'an is a unique procedure in Islamic law that resolves accusations of adultery between spouses without witnesses. The Hanafi school defines it as testimony strengthened by oaths, substituting the fixed punishment for both accuser and accused. This passage from Al-Hidayah explains the nature, conditions, and a key dispute: what happens if the husband refuses to perform li'an?

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi definition of li'an
Extract from the text how the Hanafi school defines li'an: testimonies strengthened with oaths that replace the hadd penalty.
The definition is critical because it shapes the entire procedure and the dispute.
2
List the conditions for li'an according to Hanafi fiqh
Identify the requirements: both spouses must have capacity for testimony, the wife must be muhsana, and the wife must demand li'an.
Note the condition that the wife be muhsana, since li'an substitutes for hadd al-qadhf, which only applies to accusing a muhsan.
3
Understand the core dispute about the husband's refusal
Clarify the issue: What consequence does the husband face if he refuses to perform li'an after accusing his wife? The Hanafi school differs from the majority.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proof for imprisonment
The Hanafi argument: li'an is a right (haqq) due upon the husband, and since he is able to fulfill it, the ruler compels him by imprisonment until he either performs it or retracts.
The Dalil: Quranic verse (24:6-9) establishes li'an as a substitute for hadd, so hadd is not applicable until the procedure is complete or the husband admits lying.
5
Evaluate the opposing schools' proof and the Hanafi response
Opposing schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) say the consequence of false accusation is hadd, so refusal should lead to immediate hadd. The Hanafi response is that li'an replaces hadd, so the husband is not yet proven a liar until he either completes li'an or retracts.
The consensus position is that if the husband retracts, hadd is applied by agreement.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد پنجم
شهادات باللہ ہے۔ اس آیت میں قول باری باللہ یمین کے معنی میں محکم ہے اور شہادت بھی یمین کے معنی کا احتمال رکھی ہے کیونکہ اگر کسی نے اشھد کہا تو یہ یمین ہو گی۔ پس ہم نے محتمل کو محکم پر محمول کیا ہے لیکن احناف کی طرف سے جواب ہوگا کہ اس آیت میں شہادت اور یمین دونوں کی تصریح کی گئی ہے اس لئے ہم نے کہا کہ لعان کا رکن وہ شہادت ہے جو یمین کے ساتھ موکد کی گئی ہو۔ پھر شوہر کی جانب میں لعان کے رکن کو لفظ لعان کے ساتھ ملایا گیا ہے اگر شوہر اپنی قسم میں جھوٹا ہو اور یہ شوہر کے حق میں حد قذف کے قائم مقام ہے اور عورت کی جانب میں لعان کے رکن یعنی شہادت کو لفظ غضب کے ساتھ ملایا ہے اور یہ عورت کے حق میں حد زنا کے قائم مقام ہے۔
-
رہی یہ بات کہ عورت کی شہادت کو لفظ لعن کے بجائے لفظ غضب کے ساتھ مقترن کیوں کیا گیا ہے۔ تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ عورتیں اپنے کلام میں بکثرت لعنت کا لفظ استعمال کرتی ہیں۔ چنانچہ حدیث میں مروی ہے کہ انھن یكثون اللعن ويكفرن العشير يعني عورتيں بکثرت لعنت کرتی ہیں اور اپنے شوہر کی نعمتوں کا کفران کرتی ہیں۔ پس بکثرت لعنت کرنے کی وجہ سے ان کی نظروں کی قباحت ہی جاتی رہی۔ اس لئے ہو سکتا ہے کہ وہ لعنت کے اقدام پر جری ہو جائیں ۔ پس اس مصلحت کے پیش نظر عورت کی شہادت کولفظ غضب کے ساتھ ملایا گیا ہے تا کہ وہ جھوٹی قسم کا اقدام کرنے سے باز رہے۔ یہاں ایک سوال ہے وہ یہ کہ آپ نے فرمایا کہ شہادت (لعان) زوجین کے حق میں حد کے قائم مقام ہے پس سوال یہ ہے کہ شہادت اور حد کے درمیان مناسبت کیا ہے جس کی وجہ سے شہادت کو حد کے قائم مقام کیا گیا ہے۔ جواب ان دونوں میں مناسبت یہ ہے کہ جس طرح حدزا جبر اور معاصی سے روکنے والی ہے۔ اس طرح اللہ کی جھوٹی قسم کھلانا در انحالیکہ وہ لعنت پر مشتمل ہے یہ بھی زاجر ہے بایں طور کہ اس قسم اور شہادت کے سبب پر اقدام کرنے سے باز رہے گا۔ صاحب بدا یہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جب ضابطہ ثابت ہو چکا کہ ہمارے نزدیک لعان وہ شہادتیں ہیں جو قسموں کے ساتھ موکد کی گئیں ہیں۔ تو میاں بیوی دونوں کا شہادت کی لیاقت رکھنا ضروری ہے، اس لئے کہ لعان میں شہادت رکن ہے اور یہ بھی ضروری ہے کہ عورت ایسی ہو جس کے تہمت لگانے والے کو حد ماری جاتی ہے کیونکہ احان شوہر کے حق میں حد قذف کے قائم مقام ہے اس لئے عورت کا محصنہ ہونا ضروری ہے۔ اور بچہ کے نسب کی نفی کر دینے سے بھی لعان واجب ہو جاتا ہے۔ کیونکہ جب شوہر نے اپنی بیوی کے بچہ کے نسب کی نفی کی اور کہا کہ یہ بچہ میرے نطفہ سے نہیں ہے تو یہ اس عورت کو تہمت لگانے والا ہو گیا۔ جیسے کسی اجنبی نے بچہ کے معروف باپ سے اس کے نسب کی نفی کی تو یہ اجنبی عورت کو تہمت لگانے والا شمار ہو گا اسی طرح یہاں بھی۔
ولا يعتبر احتمال سے سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر اپنی بیوی کے والد کی نفی کر دے تو اس سے لعان واجب نہ ہونا چاہیے کیونکہ ممکن ہے کہ یہ بچہ اس کا بیٹا نہ ہو اور اس کی بیوی زانیہ بھی نہ ہو اس طرح پر کہ اس کے ساتھ ولی بالشبہ کی گئی ہو۔ جواب کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ یہ شبہ معتبر نہیں ہے۔ کیوں کہ اس بات پر اجماع منعقد ہو چکا ہے کہ اگر کسی اجنبی نے کسی بچہ کی اس کے مشہور باپ سے نفی کی ہے تو یہ اجنبی شخص قاذف ( تہمت لگانے والا) ہوگا ۔ اگر چہ وہ احتمال یہاں بھی موجود ہے۔

يات اللعان
۱۴۲
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ جلد پنجم اور اس احتمال کا معتبر نہ ہونا اس وجہ سے ہے کہ نسب میں اصل فراش صحیح ہوتا ہے اور فراش فاسد اس کے ساتھ لاحق ہے پس فراش صحیح یعنی باپ کا اپنے سے نفی کرنا باپ کی طرف سے قذف ہوگا یہاں تک کہ ملحق بہ یعنی فراش فاسد کا قطعی طور سے علم ہو جائے ۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ لعان اس وقت واجب ہو گا جب کہ عورت موجب قذف یعنی لعان کا مطالبہ کرے کیوں کہ لعان عورت کا حق ہے۔ اس لئے کہ لعان کی وجہ سے عورت سے زنا کی عار اور ندامت دور ہو جاتی ہے پس جب اعان عورت کا حق ہے تو اس کا طلب کرنا بھی ضروری ہوگا جیسے کہ دوسرے حقوق میں صاحب حق کا طلب کرنا ضروری ہے۔
شوہر لعان کرنے سے رک جائے تو حاکم اسے قید کر دے حتی کہ لعان کرے یا اپنے نفس کی تکذیب کرے
فان امتنع منه حبسه الحاكم حتى يلاعن او يكذب نفسه لانه حق مستحق عليه و هو قادر على ايفائه فيحبس به حتى ياتى بما هو عليه او يكذب نفسه ليرتفع السبب ولولا عن وجب عليها اللعان لماتلونا من النص الا انه يبتدأ بالزوج لانه هو المدعى
ترجمہ پھر اگر شوہر نے لعان کرنے سے انکار کر دیا تو حاکم اس کو قید کرے گا یہاں تک کہ وہ لعان کرے یا اپنے آپ کو جھوٹا بنا دے کیونکہ شوہر پر یہ حق واجب ہے اور وہ اس کو پورا کرنے پر قادر بھی ہے پس اس کے عوض قید کیا جائے گا یہاں تک کہ شوہر ( یا ) تو اس کو پورا کرے جو اس پر واجب ہے یا اپنے آپ کو جھٹلا دے تا کہ سبب ہی دور ہو جائے اور اگر شوہر نے لعان کیا تو عورت پر بھی لعان کرنا واجب ہوگا۔ اس نص کی وجہ سے جو ہم تلاوت کر چکے ہیں مگر ابتداء شوہر سے کی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ وہ مدعی ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر شوہر نے لعان کرنے سے انکار کر دیا تو حاکم اس کو قید کرے گا۔ یہاں تک کہ وہ لعان کرے یہ ہمارا مذ ہب ہے اور امام شافعی ، امام مالک، اور امام احمد فرماتے ہیں کہ اس پر حد جاری کی جائے گی ۔ بنیاد اختلاف یہ ہے کہ ان کے نزدیک موجب قذف حد ہے اور ہمارے نزدیک لعالی ہے یا وہ اپنے آپ کو جھٹلا دے پس اگر اس شخص نے اپنی تکذیب کر دی تو بالا تفاق اس پر حد قذف جاری کی جائے گی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ شوہر پر یہ حق یعنی لعان واجب ہے درانحالیکہ وہ اس کو پورا کر دینے پر قادر ہے۔ لہذا اس حق کی وجہ سے اس کو محبوس کر دیا جائے گا یہاں تک کہ شوہر اس حق کو ادا کر دے یا اپنے آپ کو جھٹلا دے تا کہ لعان کا سبب مرتفع ہو جائے اور لعان کا سبب زوجین میں سے ایک کا دوسرے کی تکذیب کرنا ہے کیونکہ لعان اس وقت واجب ہو گا جب کہ شوہر اپنی بیوی کو زنا کی تہمت لگا دے اور پھر دونوں باہم ایک دوسرے کی تکذیب کریں ہاں اگر شوہر نے اپنی تکذیب کی تو تکاذب باقی نہ رہا بلکہ شوہر عورت کے موافق ہو گیا کہ اس نے زنا نہیں کیا ہے۔ اور اگر شوہر نے لعان کیا تو عورت پر بھی لعان کرنا واجب ہو گا دلیل وہ آیت ہے جو ہم تلاوت کر چکے یعنی فشهادة احد هم اربع الآية لیکن لعان کی ابتداء شوہر سے کی جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ شوہر ہی مدعی ہے اور لعان نام ہے شہادت کا اور شہادت کا مطالبہ مدعی سے ہوتا ہے
Chapter of Li'an. Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary volume 5. 'Testimony by Allah.' In this verse, the saying of Allah 'by Allah' is definitive in meaning of oath, and testimony also has the probability of meaning oath, because if someone says 'ashhad' (I testify) then it is an oath. So we place the probable upon the definitive. But from the Hanafis the response is that in this verse both testimony and oath are specified, so we said that the pillar of li'an is that testimony which is strengthened with oaths. Then for the husband's side, the pillar of li'an is combined with the word la'n (curse) – if the husband is false in his oath, and this stands in place of hadd of qadhf for the husband. And for the wife's side, the pillar of li'an i.e. testimony is combined with the word ghadab (anger) and this stands in place of hadd of zina for the wife. As for why the wife's testimony is combined with the word ghadab instead of the word la'n, the answer is that women frequently use the word la'n in their speech. Thus it is narrated in hadith: 'They frequently curse and are ungrateful to their spouses.' So due to their frequent cursing, the repulsiveness of cursing is lost. Therefore, it is possible that they might become bold in undertaking cursing. So out of this wisdom, the wife's testimony is combined with the word ghadab so that she refrains from undertaking a false oath. Here there is a question: You said that the testimony (li'an) stands in place of hadd for the spouses. So the question is what is the connection between testimony and hadd that testimony is placed in place of hadd? Answer: The connection is that just as hadd repels and prevents sins, similarly swearing a false oath by Allah while it contains cursing is also a deterrent, in that he will refrain from undertaking the cause of this oath and testimony. The author of Bada'i' says: When it is established as a rule that in our view li'an are testimonies strengthened with oaths, then it is necessary for both husband and wife to have the capacity for testimony, because testimony is a pillar in li'an. And it is also necessary that the wife be such that the one accusing her is subject to hadd, because li'an stands in place of hadd of qadhf for the husband, so it is necessary for the wife to be muhsana (chaste and free). And li'an also becomes obligatory by denial of a child's lineage. Because when the husband denies the lineage of his wife's child and says 'this child is not from my sperm,' then he becomes an accuser of that woman, just as if a stranger denies a child's lineage from its known father, that stranger is considered an accuser of the woman – similarly here. 'And the likelihood is not considered' – this is the answer to a question: The question is that if the husband denies his wife's father (i.e. denies the child's lineage from himself) then li'an should not be obligatory because it is possible that this child is not his son and his wife is not an adulteress, in that she may have had intercourse with a shubha. The gist of the answer is that this doubt is not valid. Because there is consensus that if a stranger denies a child from its well-known father, that stranger is a qadhif (accuser), even if that likelihood exists here as well... And this likelihood not being considered is because in lineage the original is the valid bed (firash sahih), and the invalid bed (firash fasid) is attached to it. So denying from the valid bed i.e. the father denying from himself is qadhf from the father's side, until the attached matter i.e. the invalid bed is known with certainty. The author of Hidayah says: Li'an becomes obligatory when the woman who is the object of the accusation demands li'an, because li'an is the right of the woman. Because by li'an the shame and disgrace of adultery is removed from the woman. So when li'an is the woman's right, her demanding it is also necessary, like in other rights the possessor of the right is required to demand. If the husband refuses to perform li'an, the ruler may imprison him until he performs li'an or disavows himself. The translation: Then if the husband refuses, the ruler will imprison him until he performs li'an or makes himself a liar, because this right is due upon him and he is able to fulfill it, so he is imprisoned for it until he does what is upon him or disavows himself so that the cause is removed. And if the husband performs li'an, then it becomes obligatory upon the wife also to perform li'an, due to the text we have recited; but the beginning is with the husband because he is the claimant. Explanation: The issue is that if the husband refuses to perform li'an, the ruler will imprison him until he performs li'an – this is our madhhab. Imam Shafi'i, Imam Malik, and Imam Ahmad say that hadd will be imposed upon him. The basis of the disagreement is that in their view the result of accusation is hadd, and in our view it is li'an. Or he disavows himself – then if he disavows, then by consensus hadd of qadhf will be imposed upon him. The proof is that this right i.e. li'an is obligatory upon the husband while he is able to fulfill it, so due to this right he will be imprisoned until he performs the right or disavows himself so that the cause of li'an is removed. And the cause of li'an is one of the spouses denying the other, because li'an becomes obligatory when the husband accuses his wife of adultery and then both deny each other. Yes, if the husband disavows himself, then mutual denial does not remain; rather the husband agrees with the wife that she did not commit adultery. And if the husband performs li'an, then it becomes obligatory upon the wife also to perform li'an, due to the verse we recited: 'And the testimony of each of them is four testimonies by Allah...' (24:6) But the beginning of li'an is with the husband, because he is the claimant, and li'an is the name for testimony, and testimony is demanded from the claimant.
Source pages p. 142

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of Li'an from the Urdu sharh of Al-Hidayah. It begins by establishing that li'an (mutual imprecation) consists of testimonies strengthened with oaths, based on the Quranic verse (An-Nur 24:6-9). The Hanafi position is that li'an is a form of testimony (shahadah) that serves as a substitute for the hadd penalty for the accuser (husband) and for the accused (wife). The pillar (rukn) of li'an for the husband is his fourfold testimony with oath and his statement of curse (la'nah) upon himself if he is lying; for the wife, it is her fourfold testimony with oath and her statement that she deserves Allah's wrath (ghadab) if her husband is truthful. The author explains why the wife's statement uses 'ghadab' instead of 'la'nah': women often use curses, so using 'ghadab' serves as a stronger deterrent against false oaths. The text then addresses a question about the connection between testimony and hadd: both serve as deterrents against sin. Al-Marghinani (in Al-Hidayah) outlines conditions for li'an: both spouses must be capable of testimony, and the wife must be muhsana (free, adult, Muslim, and chaste) because li'an substitutes for the hadd of qadhf which only applies to muhsan accusers. Denial of lineage of a child also necessitates li'an, as it constitutes an accusation of adultery. A potential objection is raised: if there is a possibility of intercourse under shubha (mistaken contract), then the husband might not be accusing. The response is that such a possibility is not considered because the default rule is that the child belongs to the husband's valid bed (firash sahih); only if the child is clearly from an invalid bed (firash fasid) is the exception recognized. Li'an is only obligatory when the wife demands it, because it is her right to clear herself from the accusation. If the husband refuses to perform li'an, the Hanafi school holds that the ruler should imprison him until he either performs li'an or retracts his accusation (by admitting he lied). This is because li'an is a right due from him and he is capable of fulfilling it. The Shafi'i, Maliki, and Hanbali schools oppose this, holding that the husband should be subjected to the hadd of qadhf instead. The Hanafi proof is that the hadd is replaced by li'an due to the textual provision, and the husband's refusal to fulfill this right warrants compulsion through imprisonment, not immediate hadd. If the husband retracts, then the hadd of qadhf is applied by consensus. The passage concludes that li'an begins with the husband as the claimant, and the wife is required to follow if he performs it.

Key Terms
لعان (li'an): Mutual imprecation; a procedure where a husband and wife each testify under oath, with the husband invoking curses and the wife invoking wrath, to settle an accusation of adultery without witnesses.
شہادت (shahadah): Testimony; in li'an, it refers to the fourfold statement by each spouse swearing by Allah.
یمین (yamin): Oath; the swearing by Allah that is combined with testimony in li'an.
حد قذف (hadd al-qadhf): The fixed punishment for false accusation of adultery; 80 lashes.
محصنہ (muhsana): A woman who is free, adult, Muslim, and chaste (not convicted of zina); required for the hadd of qadhf to apply.
فراش صحیح (firash sahih): Valid bed; a valid marriage relationship that establishes lineage of a child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens if a husband refuses to perform li'an after accusing his wife of adultery?
A) He is immediately given 80 lashes (hadd al-qadhf).
B) He is imprisoned until he performs li'an or retracts his accusation.
C) He is divorced from his wife automatically.
D) He is required to pay compensation to the wife.

Key Takeaway
Li'an is a testimony-oath procedure that replaces hadd for spouses; the Hanafi school compels performance by imprisonment, not by flogging, until the husband completes it or retracts.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
6 min
Conditions for Absence of Li'an and Hadd when Wife Lacks Eligibility
Ruling on when husband is eligible but wife is not, so no li'an or hadd

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which the hadd of qadhf and li'an are not applicable when the husband is eligible but the wife is not, and cite the Hanafi proof (hadith) supporting this ruling.

Core Idea
No hadd and no li'an when the wife lacks ahliyyat al-shahada and ihsan.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in Hanafi law: a husband who is qualified to testify accuses his wife of adultery, but the wife lacks the required eligibility (ahliyyat al-shahada) or the status of muhsanah. In such cases, neither the hadd penalty for false accusation (qadhf) nor the mutual imprecation (li'an) is imposed. The lesson will walk you through the conditions, the reasoning, and the prophetic proof that supports this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
Understand that the passage rules on two legal consequences: the hadd of qadhf (80 lashes) and the procedure of li'an. The ruling is that both are absent (no hadd and no li'an).
The ruling applies when the husband is eligible (ahl al-shahada) but the wife is not.
2
List the conditions for the ruling
Identify the specific conditions of the wife that trigger the negation: she is a slave, a disbeliever, has been punished for qadhf, or is a minor, insane, or an adulteress.
These conditions all point to her lack of ahliyyat al-shahada or ihsan.
3
Understand the legal rationale
The hadd of qadhf requires the victim to be muhsan (free, Muslim, chaste). Li'an requires both spouses to be eligible for testimony. Since the wife fails on one or both, the obligations are dropped.
The text compares this to when the wife confirms the accusation, which also drops the hadd.
4
Analyze the prophetic proof
The hadith lists four categories of wives with whom li'an is not performed: Jewish/Christian under a Muslim, slave under a free man, free woman under a slave. This supports the rule that ineligibility prevents li'an.
The hadith is from Abu Bakr al-Razi's commentary; although not in standard collections, it is considered reliable in the Hanafi school.
5
Apply the ruling to a new case
Given a scenario (e.g., a free Muslim husband with a Jewish wife), predict the legal outcome and state the reasoning.
Practice ensures you can operationalize the conditions.

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد بانهم
شوہر اگر اہل شہادت میں سے اور بیوی باندی ہو یا کافرہ ہو یا محدودہ فی القذف ہو یا ایسی ہے کہ جس کے قاذف کو حد جاری نہیں کی جاتی جیسے بچی ہو یا مجنونہ ہویا زانیہ ہو تو شوہر پر حد نہیں ہے اور لعان بھی نہیں ہے
وان كان من اهل الشهادة وهى امة او كافرة او محدودة في قذف او كانت ممن لا يحد قاذفها بان كانت صبية او مجنونة اوزانية فلاحد عليه ولالعان لانعدام اهلية الشهادة وعدم الاحصان فى جانبها وامتناع اللعان لمعنى من جهتها فيسقط الحد كما اذا صدقته والاصل فى ذالک قوله علیه السلام اربعة لالعان بينهم و بين ازواجهم اليهودية والنصرانية تحت المسلم والمملوكة تحت الحرو الحرة تحت المملوك ولو كانا محدودين في قذف فعليه الحد
ترجمہ اور اگر شوہر لائق شہادت ہو اور حال یہ کہ بیوی باندی ہے یا کافر یا کسی کو تہمت لگانے میں حد ماری گئی ہو یا ایسی عورت ہو جس سے بہت لگانے والے کو مد نہیں ماری جاتی۔ بایں طور کہ بچی ہے یا دیوانی عورت ہے یا زانیہ تو اس کے شوہر پر حد یا لعان کچھ نہیں ہو گا اس ان پر اب میں اہمیت شہادت اور احصان (دونوں) معدوم ہیں اور لعان کا متبع ہونا ایسی بات کی وجہ سے ہے جو عورت کی ات من (شاہ سے امہ سے ) حد قذف ساقط ہو جائے گی جیسے جب عورت اس کے قول کی تصدیق کر دے اور اصل اس جواب میں آ لمتضرت صلی الہ علیہ وسلم کا قول ہے کہ چار ہیں جن میں اور ان کی زوجات میں لعان نہیں ہوتا۔ یہود یہ جومسلمان مرد کے تحت میں ہو اور اللہ الیہ کو مسلمان مردے تحت میں ہو اور ملوکہ جو آزاد مرد کے تحت میں ہو اور آزاد عورت جو غلام کے تحت میں ہو اور اگر دونوں محدود
ترین مسئلہ یہی کہ امر بہ شہادت کی لیاقت رکھتا ہو مگر اس کی بیوی کسی کی باندی ہو یا کافرہ ہے یا اس پر حد قذف ماری گئی ہے یا ایک عورت ہے جس کے ثبات کیا بنے والے تو حد نہیں ماری جاتی ہیں طور کہ وہ بیچی ہو یا مجنونہ ہو یا زانیہ ہو تو ان تمام صورتوں میں اس کے

ب ہوگی اور نہ لعان ۔ کیونکہ یہ تورت نا قابل شہادت ہے اور نہ ہی اس کی جانب میں احسان ہے۔ پس اس عورت کے قابل شہادت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے ایمان واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وجوب بعمان کے واسطے زوہین کا لائق شہادت ہونا ضروری ہے اور اس کے محصنہ ہونے کی وجہ سے شوہر پر وجہ ند قاف از نہیں ہوئی، کیوں کہ صدقذف کسی محمد ن عورت کو تثبت لگانے کی وجہ سے واجب ہوتی ہے۔ صاب ہو ہی جاتے ہیں کہا جان تو ایک ایسی بات کی وجہ سے متبع ہو گیا جو عورت کی جانب میں موجود ہے۔ لہذا شوہر کے ذمہ سے کامان ای ابتدا کے امت یہ بات وہاں ۔ جیسے اس وقت ساتھ ہو جاتی ہے جب بیوی اس کے قول کی تصدیق کر دے اور اس باب میں اصل حضور صلی اللہ کہ چار ہیں جن میں اور ان کی زوجات میں جان نہیں ہوتا (1) یہودیہ جو مسلمان مرد کے تحت میں ہو (۲)
تم یہ جو مسلمان مرد کے تحت میں ہو ( ۳) مملوکہ جو آزاد مرد کے تحت میں ہو ((۴) آزاد عورت جو نام کے نکاح میں ہو۔ یہ حدیث حدیث کی مشہور کتابوں میں مذکور نہیں ہے مگر ابو بکر رازی نے اس کو مختصر الطحاوی کی اپنی شرط میں ذکر کیا ہے اور ابو بکر رازی
عدات اللہ اور ضبط میں مقتدیل اور پیشوا کی حیثیت رکھتے ہیں اس لئے اس حدیث سے استدلال کیا جا سکتا ہے۔
If the husband is among those eligible for testimony and the wife is a slave woman, or a disbeliever, or one who has been punished for qadhf, or one whose accuser is not punished – such as a minor girl, an insane woman, or an adulteress – then there is no hadd upon the husband and no li'an. Because she lacks eligibility for testimony and ihsan on her side, and li'an is prevented due to a meaning from her side, so the hadd is dropped just as when she confirms him. The basis for this is the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'Four between whom and their wives there is no li'an: the Jewish woman under a Muslim, the Christian woman under a Muslim, the slave woman under a free man, and the free woman under a slave.' If both have been punished for qadhf, then hadd is due. Translation: And if the husband is eligible for testimony, and the wife is a slave, or a disbeliever, or has been punished for accusation, or is a woman whose accuser is not punished – i.e., she is a minor, insane, or adulteress – then there is no hadd or li'an upon her husband. Because on her side both the qualification for testimony and ihsan are non-existent, and li'an is prevented due to something from her side, so the hadd of qadhf falls just as when the woman confirms his statement. The basis in this chapter is the Prophet's saying: 'There are four between whom and their wives there is no li'an: a Jewish woman under a Muslim man, a Christian woman under a Muslim man, a slave woman under a free man, and a free woman under a slave.' And if both are limited… The main issue: if he is qualified for testimony but his wife is someone's slave, or a disbeliever, or has been punished for qadhf, or a woman whose accuser is not punished – such as a minor or insane woman or adulteress – then in all these cases there will be no hadd and no li'an. Because this woman is not eligible for testimony and ihsan is not on her side. Thus, due to her not being eligible for testimony, li'an is not obligatory, because for the obligation of li'an it is necessary that both be eligible for testimony. And due to her not being muhsinah, hadd of qadhf does not become obligatory upon the husband, because hadd of qadhf becomes obligatory for slandering a muhsinah. So li'an is prevented due to a meaning present in the wife. Therefore, the obligation from the husband's side drops, just as when the wife confirms his statement. And the basis in this chapter is the Prophet, peace be upon him: 'There are four between whom and their wives there is no li'an: (1) a Jewish woman under a Muslim man, (2) a Christian woman under a Muslim man, (3) a slave woman under a free man, (4) a free woman under a slave.' This hadith is not mentioned in the famous books of hadith, but Abu Bakr al-Razi mentioned it in his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Tahawi, and Abu Bakr al-Razi is reliable and a leader in justice and precision, so deduction from this hadith is permissible.
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the conditions for li'an and hadd. It begins by listing cases where the husband is eligible (ahl al-shahada) but the wife is not: if she is a slave, a disbeliever, has been punished for qadhf, or is a minor, insane, or an adulteress. In all such cases, no hadd is imposed on the husband and no li'an is performed. The reason is that both eligibility for testimony (ahliyyat al-shahada) and ihsan (being free, Muslim, and chaste) are absent in her. Additionally, the hadd of qadhf is only imposed for slandering a muhsinah. The text then cites a hadith listing four types of women with whom li'an does not occur: a Jewish or Christian wife under a Muslim, a slave wife under a free man, and a free wife under a slave. The commentator notes that this hadith is not found in the standard hadith collections but is relied upon because Abu Bakr al-Razi, a reliable authority, narrated it. The ruling follows the Hanafi position that hadd and li'an are contingent upon both spouses being eligible. A practical example: if a Muslim man accuses his Jewish wife of adultery, he does not undergo li'an nor receive the hadd of qadhf.

Key Terms
لِوَاء (li'an): Mutual imprecation between spouses when husband accuses wife of adultery but cannot produce witnesses.
إحصان (ihsan): The state of being free, Muslim, and having engaged in marital relations; required for hadd of qadhf and li'an.
قذف (qadhf): The crime of slandering a chaste person by accusing them of adultery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He undergoes li'an and receives hadd of qadhf
B) No li'an and no hadd
C) Li'an only, no hadd
D) Hadd only, no li'an

Key Takeaway
The hadd of qadhf and li'an are not applicable when the wife lacks the status of muhsanah or eligibility for testimony, as per the Hanafi school and the hadith of the four categories.

Procedure of Li'an: Husband and Wife Oaths
Description of the steps and wording of li'an

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the exact procedure of li'an, including the number and wording of oaths, the pointing gesture, and the ruling when the husband lacks witnesses.

Core Idea
Li'an is a wajib procedure of mutual oaths that replaces witnesses, resulting in permanent separation.

This passage details the exact steps of li'an, the mutual oaths between husband and wife when the husband accuses his wife of adultery without proof. It clarifies the number of oaths, the specific wording, and the required gesture of pointing. It also cites the Quranic evidence and discusses a subtle variation regarding the pronoun used in the oath.

Guided Path
1
Identify the trigger for li'an
The passage states that li'an becomes wajib when the husband accuses his wife of adultery and has no witnesses. This is the condition that activates the procedure.
Without accusation, no li'an.
2
Describe the husband's oaths
The husband gives four oaths (shahadah) testifying that he is truthful in his accusation. Each oath begins with 'I testify by Allah that...'. Then on the fifth, he invokes the curse of Allah upon himself if he is lying.
The oaths are termed 'shahadah' (testimony) though they are oaths.
3
Describe the wife's oaths
Similarly, the wife gives four oaths that the husband is lying, and on the fifth she invokes Allah's wrath upon herself if he is truthful.
The wife's oaths mirror the husband's but with opposite purpose.
4
Identify the pointing gesture
While speaking, the husband points to the wife. This gesture removes ambiguity about whom the oath refers to.
Pointing is considered wajib by the author, though some treat it as sunnah.
5
Recognize the evidence
The passage references the Quranic verse (Surah an-Nur: 6-9) as the primary evidence for this procedure.
The verse directly prescribes the li'an process.
6
Understand the nuance of direct address vs. third person
Imam Hasan narrates from Abu Hanifa that the husband should use direct address (e.g., 'I accuse you') instead of third person ('I accuse her') to eliminate any possibility of ambiguity. However, the book's text uses third person, justified by the pointing gesture.
This shows Hanafi precision in wording.

And if he does not have proof, then li'an becomes obligatory. The form of li'an is that the qadi brings both spouses and begins li'an with the husband. Commentary
This passage explains the procedure of li'an. When the husband accuses his wife of adultery without witnesses, li'an becomes wajib. The qadi assembles both spouses and starts with the husband. This shows the depth of Hanafi usul in preserving precision.

خطاب (khatab): Direct address using second-person pronouns, as opposed to third-person (gha'ib).

Dispute on Timing of Separation after Li'an
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of separation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on when separation occurs after li'an and compare it with Imam Zufar's view, identifying the proof for each.

Core Idea
Separation after li'an requires a qadi's decree; it is not automatic.

The Quran commands that after li'an, the husband must release his wife with kindness. But what if he refuses? This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute: does separation happen immediately upon li'an, or does the qadi need to step in? The mainstream Hanafi position, upheld by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, insists on qadi intervention, while Imam Zufar argues for immediate effect. Let's trace the proofs and consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the issue
Identify the precise point of dispute: whether the legal separation (furqah) between spouses occurs immediately upon completion of li'an or only after the qadi formally separates them.
2
Present the mainstream Hanafi position
State the ruling of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad: separation does not take place until the qadi issues a decree. The li'an itself does not effect divorce.
3
Present Imam Zufar's opposing view
Imam Zufar argues that separation occurs automatically as soon as li'an is completed, because li'an establishes a permanent prohibition (hurmat al-mubaddah) that makes marriage impossible.
4
Analyse the proofs
Examine the evidence for each side. The Hanafi majority relies on the hadith of the companion who, after li'an, said retaining his wife would amount to triple divorce, implying that the marriage still existed after li'an. Zufar bases his view on the general hadith that li'an creates permanent prohibition.
5
Determine the practical difference and tarjih
The thamarah al-khilaf: under the majority view, the marriage continues until the qadi rules; under Zufar's view, the spouses are instantly divorced. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is the majority view: separation requires qadi's decree.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the timing of separation after li'an. The base text (al-Quduri) states that separation does not occur until the qadi formally separates the spouses. Imam Zufar argues that separation occurs immediately upon completion of li'an because li'an establishes permanent prohibition (hurmat al-mubadda) according to a hadith. The Hanafi response (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that li'an causes the loss of the possibility of retaining the wife with kindness (imsaak bi al-ma'ruf), so the husband is obliged to release her with kindness (tasrih bi al-ihsan). If he does not, the qadi steps in to enforce this. The evidence is a hadith where a companion, after li'an, said he had lied, and the Prophet told him to retain her, but he said that would be a triple divorce. This implies that separation after li'an is not automatic but requires a decision (either the husband's release or the qadi's decree). The commentary then clarifies that the separation is a ba'in talaq (irrevocable divorce) according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, because the qadi's action is attributed to the husband as his representative, similar to the ruling of an impotent man ('anin) where the qadi separates them and it counts as a ba'in talaq. The passage ends abruptly, but the ruling is clear.

Key Terms
فرقة (furqah): Separation between spouses after li'an.
تسریح بالاحسان (tasrih bi al-ihsan): Releasing a wife with kindness, i.e., a proper divorce without harm.
حرمت موبدة (hurmat al-mubaddah): A permanent prohibition that makes marriage unlawful forever.

In the Hanafi school, separation after li'an requires a qadi's decree; it is not automatic, even though the marriage becomes permanently prohibited.

The Exact Procedure of Li'an in the Hanafi School
Describes the exact procedure of li'an for both spouses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the exact procedure of li'an for both spouses, including the number of oaths and their wordings.

Core Idea
Li'an requires four oaths of testimony and a fifth of cursing for each spouse, with specific Arabic phrases.

In this lesson, we examine the precise judicial procedure of li'an as established in the Hanafi school. The husband accuses his wife of adultery without four witnesses; the judge then administers a series of oaths. Understanding the exact wording and sequence is crucial for the validity of the procedure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Li'an is wajib (obligatory) for the husband when he accuses his wife of adultery without four witnesses and she demands vindication.
The ruling is derived from the Quranic imperative in Surah An-Nur.
2
Outline the husband's procedure
The husband testifies four times using the phrase 'ashhadu billah inni lamina al-sadiqin' (I bear witness by Allah that I am truly among the truthful) regarding the accusation. In the fifth, he says 'la'nat Allah 'alayhi in kana min al-kadhibin' (May the curse of Allah be upon him if he is among the liars). He gestures towards the wife throughout.
The fifth oath is a curse upon himself, not a testimony.
3
Outline the wife's procedure
The wife testifies four times using the phrase 'ashhadu billah annahu lamina al-kadhibin' (I bear witness by Allah that he is among the liars) regarding the accusation. In the fifth, she says 'ghadab Allah 'alayha in kana min al-sadiqin' (May the wrath of Allah be upon her if he is among the truthful).
The wife's oaths are designed to vindicate herself by asserting the husband's lie.
4
Identify the judge's role
The judge initiates the procedure and separates the spouses during the oaths. The judge's presence and management are essential for the li'an to be valid.
The judge does not take an oath; he only administers the process.
5
Connect to the Quranic proof
The procedure is based on Surah An-Nur (24:6-9), which prescribes the li'an when a husband accuses his wife without witnesses. The imperative form indicates obligation, and the exact wording is established by the Prophet's practice (sunnah) as transmitted in the Hanafi school.
The Quranic verses are qati al-thubut (certain transmission) but zanni al-dalala (speculative meaning) in terms of wording, hence the need for the Prophet's clarification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصفة اللعان ان يبتدى القاضى بالزوج فيشهد اربع مرات يقول في كل مرة اشهد بالله اني لمن الصدقين فيمار ميتها به من الزناء ويقول فى الخامسة لعنة الله عليه ان كان من الكاذبين فيما رماها به من الزناء يشير اليها فى جميع ذالك ثم تشهد المرأة اربع مرات تقول في كل مرة اشهدبا الله انه لمن الكاذبين فيمارماني به من الزناء وتقول في الخامسة غضب الله عليها ان كان من الصادقين فيمارمانى به من الزناء والاصل فيه ماتلوناه من النص
And the description of li'an is that the judge begins with the husband, so he testifies four times, saying each time: 'I bear witness by Allah that I am truly among the truthful in what I accuse her of regarding adultery.' And in the fifth he says: 'May the curse of Allah be upon him if he is among the liars in what he accused her of regarding adultery.' He gestures towards her in all of that. Then the woman testifies four times, saying each time: 'I bear witness by Allah that he is among the liars in what he accused me of regarding adultery.' And in the fifth she says: 'May the wrath of Allah be upon her if he is among the truthful in what he accused me of regarding adultery.' And the basis for this is what we have recited from the text (Quran).

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, explaining the exact procedure of li'an (mutual imprecation) as practiced in the Hanafi school. The judge initiates with the husband, who must swear four times using the phrase 'ashhadu billah' (I bear witness by Allah) that he is truthful in his accusation of adultery against his wife. In the fifth oath, instead of a testimony, he invokes Allah's curse upon himself if he is lying. The wife then does the same, swearing four times that he is lying, and in the fifth invokes Allah's wrath upon herself if he is truthful. Throughout, the husband and wife gesture towards each other. The proof is the Quranic verses from Surah An-Nur (24:6-9) which command this procedure. This description follows the standard Hanafi position as recorded in the zahir al-riwayah.

Key Terms
لعان (li'an): A special judicial procedure of mutual oath-taking and curse between spouses when the husband accuses the wife of adultery without witnesses.
اشهد بالله (ashhadu billah): The specific phrase used in li'an testimonies, meaning 'I bear witness by Allah'.

Wording of the Husband's Testimony: Direct vs Indirect in Li'an
Explains a dispute between Abu Hanifa and a narration from Hasan on the husband's wording

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two positions on the husband's wording in li'an (direct vs indirect with gesture) and identify the mufta bihi position according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Indirect speech with gesture suffices for li'an; direct address is more definitive but not required.

In li'an, the husband must testify to his accusation of adultery. A key question is the precise wording: must he directly address his wife ('I accuse you'), or can he speak about her indirectly ('I accuse her')? The matn (Hidayah) holds that indirect wording coupled with a gesture removes all ambiguity. However, a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad reports that Abu Hanifa required direct address for greater certainty. This lesson unpacks the dispute and the relied-upon position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What is the legal point of contention? The husband's wording in the li'an testimony: direct address (مخاطبة) or indirect (غائب) with gesture.
The issue is not whether to name the wife, but the pronoun and mode of address.
2
State the two positions
The matn (Hidayah) holds that indirect speech (e.g., 'fīmā ramāhā bihi') accompanied by a gesture is sufficient. Hasan ibn Ziyad's narration from Abu Hanifa holds that direct address (e.g., 'fīmā ramaytuki bihi') is required because it is more definitive.
Both are attributed to Abu Hanifa, creating an intra-madhab ikhtilaf.
3
Analyze the dalil for each
The narration from Hasan argues that direct address cuts off any possibility of ambiguity (āqta‘ li-l-ihtimāl). The matn argues that indirect speech with gesture also severs possibility (inqaṭa‘a al-iḥtimāl).
The matn’s dalil is ‘illa: gesture achieves the same certainty as direct address.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
If the husband uses indirect speech without gesture, the testimony would be invalid according to the narration from Hasan, but valid according to the matn (since gesture compensates).
This practical difference affects court rulings.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Marghinani) adopt the matn’s view as more comprehensive. The relied-upon position is that indirect speech with gesture suffices.
This is the operative rule for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وروى الحسن عن أبى حنيفة انه ياتى بلفظة المواجهة يقول فيما رمتیک به من الزناء لانه اقطع للاحتمال وجه ماذكر فى الكتاب ان لفظة المغايبة اذا انضمت اليها الاشارة انقطع الاحتمال
And Hasan narrated from Abu Hanifa that he (the husband) uses the direct address wording, saying 'in what I accused you of regarding adultery' because it is more definitive in cutting off possibility. The reason for what is mentioned in the book (the matn) is that the indirect wording, when accompanied by gesture, the possibility is also cut off.
Source pages p. 146

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the precise wording the husband should use during li'an. The matn (Hidayah) mentions indirect speech: 'fīmā ramāhā bihi' (in what he accused her of). Hasan ibn Ziyad narrates from Abu Hanifa that direct address should be used: 'fīmā ramaytuki bihi' (in what I accused you of). The reason given is that direct address eliminates any ambiguity about whom is being referred to, while the matn's position is that gesture accompanying indirect speech also removes ambiguity. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) according to later Hanafi authorities is the matn's view, as it is more comprehensive.

Key Terms
لفظة المواجهة (lafzat al-muwājahah): The direct address form of speech (e.g., 'you' instead of 'her').
لفظة المغايبة (lafzat al-maghāyabah): The indirect form of speech (e.g., 'her' instead of 'you').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the matn prefer indirect speech in li'an according to the commentary?
A) It is more respectful
B) It is the Quranic wording
C) Gesture with indirect speech removes ambiguity
D) The Prophet used indirect speech

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that indirect speech accompanied by gesture cuts off ambiguity, making it legally sufficient in li'an, though direct address is more definitive.
